#### Publishing, Copyright & Licensing Manual

> **Version:** 1.0  
> **Status:** Master Manual  
> **Author & Publisher:** Sharique Chaudhary

---

#### Copyright Notice

Copyright © Sharique Chaudhary. All rights reserved.

This publication and its associated materials are protected by applicable copyright and intellectual property laws. Except where expressly permitted by law or by prior written authorization from the copyright holder, no portion of this publication may be reproduced, distributed, transmitted, translated, stored, or incorporated into another work in any form or by any means.

This manual establishes the official publishing, copyright, licensing, and intellectual-property framework for the Engineering Handbook ecosystem.

Nothing in this manual constitutes legal advice. Jurisdiction-specific legal review should be obtained before adopting any policy contained herein as a legally enforceable agreement.

---

#### About This Manual

The **Publishing, Copyright & Licensing Manual** is the authoritative policy manual governing the publishing ecosystem for all Engineering Handbook publications.

Rather than functioning as a simple copyright notice, this manual defines the long-term principles governing publication, licensing, ownership, digital rights, institutional licensing, commercial licensing, anti-piracy policy, and future publishing operations.

---

#### Intended Audience

This manual is intended for:

- Authors
- Publishers
- Editors
- Contributors
- Licensing Administrators
- Legal Reviewers
- Platform Developers
- Educational Institutions
- Enterprise Customers
- Publishing Partners

---

#### How to Read This Manual

The manual is divided into independent parts.

Each part focuses on one major aspect of the publishing ecosystem while building upon the principles established in previous parts.

Although individual sections may be referenced independently, new readers are encouraged to read the manual sequentially.

---

#### Manual Organization

The manual is organized into multiple parts.

Each part contains several major sections that address a specific publishing domain.

---

  - [1. Purpose and Scope](#1-purpose-and-scope-1)

## Part III

- [License Types & Rights](#part-iii--license-types--rights)

---

#### Remaining Parts

> The remaining parts continue the handbook licensing framework and follow the same navigation structure.

---

#### Normative Language

The following keywords are used throughout this manual.

| Keyword | Meaning |
|----------|---------|
| **SHALL** | Mandatory requirement |
| **SHALL NOT** | Mandatory prohibition |
| **SHOULD** | Recommended practice |
| **SHOULD NOT** | Generally discouraged practice |
| **MAY** | Optional or discretionary action |

---

#### Document Conventions

Throughout this manual:

- **Handbook** refers to an independent publication.
- **Volume** refers to a commercial subdivision of a handbook.
- **Edition** refers to a formally published revision.
- **License Family** identifies the licensing relationship of a handbook.
- **Purchase Entitlement** identifies purchased content.
- **License Type** defines permitted usage rights.

---

#### Versioning Policy

The manual follows semantic versioning.

- **Major versions** introduce significant policy changes.
- **Minor versions** introduce compatible additions or clarifications.
- Editorial corrections do not normally constitute a new version.

---

#### Disclaimer

This manual defines publishing policy.

It should not be interpreted as legal advice. Professional legal review should be obtained before adopting these policies as legally binding agreements.

---

## Part I — Publishing Philosophy & Intellectual Property Framework

**Author and Publisher:** Sharique Chaudhary

**Status:** Master Manual — Part I

---

### 1. PURPOSE OF THIS MANUAL

This manual establishes the common publishing, copyright, licensing, ownership, and rights-management philosophy for the handbook ecosystem. It is not merely a copyright notice. It is the internal policy authority from which detailed license types, institutional rules, digital-rights systems, anti-piracy measures, edition policies, and publishing operations are derived.

The ecosystem may contain independent handbooks, hundreds of publishing volumes, sequels, companion works, revised and remastered editions, digital and print publications, code repositories, and a future dedicated publishing platform. A short notice inside a PDF cannot govern that system consistently. This manual exists so future decisions are made from documented principles rather than temporary assumptions.

The manual is intended for the author and publisher, future collaborators, licensing administrators, developers building the handbook platform, editorial staff, and legal reviewers. Selected policies may later become reader-facing license terms, institutional agreements, FAQs, copyright notices, or license certificates.

The framework aims to protect original work while keeping legitimate educational use understandable. It should minimize friction for honest readers and apply stronger restrictions to redistribution, unlicensed organizational use, piracy, and unauthorized commercial exploitation.

This manual defines policy intent and operational rules. It is not a substitute for jurisdiction-specific legal advice. Contractual penalties, privacy-sensitive tracking, international terms, and enforcement language should receive qualified legal review before public adoption.

#### EXCEPTIONS

A policy may be overridden where applicable law requires different treatment, a publishing platform creates an unavoidable contractual limitation, a separately negotiated written agreement grants different rights, a publication has an expressly documented special model, or a later version of this manual changes the policy.

Silence and informal assumptions are not exceptions.

---

### 2. VISION OF THE HANDBOOK ECOSYSTEM

The handbook ecosystem is designed as a long-term engineering and educational library, not a collection of temporary trend books. Each handbook should provide structured, practical, deeply researched, and conceptually complete coverage of its defined domain.

Handbooks are independent but may complement one another. A Backend Engineering Handbook may explain the database knowledge required for backend work and optionally direct a reader to the Database Engineering Handbook for engine internals. The backend book must still fulfil its own learning objective. A cross-reference is a learning aid, not a hidden purchase requirement.

The ecosystem is expected to evolve through new volumes, revisions, major editions, remastered editions, sequels, companion publications, translated editions, multiple physical and digital formats, supplementary repositories, and a dedicated licensing platform. The licensing philosophy must therefore scale beyond a single PDF or payment provider.

Reader trust is part of the publishing model. Important restrictions should be understandable before purchase. Buyers should know what handbook, edition, volumes, format, and license scope they are receiving. Companion recommendations must be described honestly, and ownership must never be misrepresented.

The publisher should protect the catalogue without designing the entire reader experience around suspicion. Security and anti-piracy controls are supporting systems. Education remains the primary purpose.

---

### 3. INTELLECTUAL PROPERTY PHILOSOPHY

Unless expressly stated otherwise, original intellectual property created for the handbook ecosystem remains with the author or legally designated rights holder. Purchasing a handbook grants usage rights under an applicable license; it does not transfer the copyright or general ownership of the intellectual property.

Original material may include written explanations, original educational sequencing, diagrams, architecture maps, illustrations, comparison tables, exercises, projects, examples, original teaching datasets, visual systems, layouts, supplementary content, and original code. Different assets may use different licenses. For example, handbook prose may remain under restrictive publication terms while an official example repository uses MIT or Apache-2.0.

The handbook does not claim ownership over public facts, established algorithms, standards, mathematical principles, programming languages, or general engineering concepts. The protectable interest is in original expression and other protectable creative contributions, subject to applicable law.

**Example**

> The publisher does not own the concept of a B+ tree. An original B+ tree diagram, explanatory analogy, written explanation, and custom exercise may be protected.

Research-based content requires special discipline. Official documentation, RFCs, papers, source repositories, standards, incident reports, and engineering blogs may inform a handbook, but public accessibility does not make third-party content publisher-owned. The author should create original explanations, cite sources where appropriate, preserve required notices, and respect applicable licenses.

AI tools may assist research, drafting, editing, brainstorming, or code review. AI assistance does not remove editorial responsibility. Material must still be reviewed for technical accuracy, originality, accidental reproduction, attribution, licensing compatibility, and source quality.

Future contributor material must be governed by a written contributor arrangement. The project should define whether copyright is transferred or licensed, whether the license is exclusive or non-exclusive, what attribution is provided, and whether the contributor may reuse the work.

#### THIRD-PARTY EXCEPTION

Lawfully licensed or otherwise permitted third-party material may be included. The handbook’s copyright notice must not falsely imply exclusive ownership of such material, and required attribution or license notices must be preserved.

---

### 4. COPYRIGHT AND LICENSING: DIFFERENT FUNCTIONS

Copyright and licensing solve different problems.

Copyright concerns ownership and legal protection of original creative work. Licensing defines what another person or organization is permitted to do with that work.

A personal buyer may be permitted to read, annotate, and retain a licensed copy. A university may receive controlled classroom and LMS rights. A commercial training provider may require separate authorization to use handbook material in paid courses. The underlying content can be identical while the permitted uses differ.

The normal relationship is:

```text
AUTHORIZED PURCHASE OR ACCESS
            ↓
APPLICABLE LICENSE TERMS
            ↓
DEFINED USAGE RIGHTS
            ↓
COPYRIGHT AND UNDERLYING IP REMAIN WITH THE RIGHTS HOLDER
```

Buying a copy is not buying copyright. A physical purchaser may own the physical object subject to applicable law, but does not thereby own the copyright in its contents.

Copyright alone is not enough for the ecosystem because it does not answer operational questions such as whether a professor may upload a PDF to an LMS, whether a company may train hundreds of employees from one copy, whether a sequel uses the same license family, whether a remastered edition is included, or whether example code may be reused commercially.

Licenses must also respect applicable law. A license is not a mechanism for overriding mandatory legal rights. Public-facing terms should eventually receive jurisdiction-specific review and appropriate governing-law, consumer-rights, and severability treatment.

#### SEPARATE AGREEMENT EXCEPTION

A signed special agreement may grant rights beyond the standard license. It should identify the handbook, volumes, edition, format, authorized users, permitted uses, duration where relevant, restrictions, and termination conditions. A special agreement changes rights only for the covered party; it does not modify the standard license for everyone.

---

### 5. GUIDING PRINCIPLES OF THE LICENSING SYSTEM

**FIRST:** Protect against misuse, not normal learning. A legitimate reader should generally be able to read, highlight, annotate, bookmark, create personal study notes, and apply learned concepts. Restrictions should focus on unauthorized redistribution, mass sharing, unlicensed institutional use, and commercial exploitation.

**SECOND:** Transparency before enforcement. Important restrictions must be stated clearly. The publisher should not invent a new rule after an incident and claim that a buyer should have assumed it.

**THIRD:** Independent licensing by default. Each independent handbook requires its own licensing scope unless a bundle, sequel rule, promotion, or special agreement explicitly provides otherwise.

**FOURTH:** Proportionality. An accidental private sharing mistake should not automatically be treated like organized commercial piracy. Enforcement should consider scale, intent, repetition, harm, and cooperation.

**FIFTH:** Technology neutrality. Core rights should not depend on one PDF DRM vendor, payment processor, license tracker, or website framework. The project may begin with third-party infrastructure and later migrate to its own platform without rewriting the licensing philosophy.

**SIXTH:** Scalability. Handbook IDs, Volume IDs, Edition IDs, and License IDs should support a catalogue that may grow to hundreds of volumes and multiple publication families.

**SEVENTH:** Accessibility and legitimate use. Anti-piracy controls should be reviewed if they break screen readers, prevent reasonable offline use, make annotation impossible, create excessive device lockouts, or collect unnecessary personal data.

**EIGHTH:** Human review. Automation may issue, verify, suspend, or flag licenses, but significant disputes and enforcement decisions should support human review.

The central principle is simple: protect the work strongly enough to sustain the publishing ecosystem without making legitimate education unnecessarily hostile.

---

### 6. HANDBOOK INDEPENDENCE PHILOSOPHY

Every handbook is an independent educational and commercial work. Each has its own defined scope, curriculum, publication identity, editions, volumes, pricing classification, and licensing relationship.

#### DEFAULT RULE

**ONE INDEPENDENT HANDBOOK = ONE INDEPENDENT HANDBOOK LICENSING SCOPE.**

Purchasing the Linux Engineering Handbook does not grant rights to Operating Systems, DevOps, Security, or Computer Networks merely because those subjects overlap.

Independence was chosen for reader clarity, commercial fairness, publishing flexibility, software simplicity, and institutional clarity. A college can license Computer Networks for a networking course without licensing the complete engineering catalogue. One handbook can be remastered without changing every other handbook’s license.

Independence is also an editorial philosophy. When another discipline is necessary to understand the current subject, the current handbook should explain the required concept at the depth needed for its own objective.

**Example**

> A Backend Engineering volume discussing indexes should explain why indexes affect backend query performance. It may recommend the Database Engineering Handbook for B-tree page structures and engine implementation. The reader should not be forced to purchase the database handbook to continue the backend chapter.

Cross-references are encouraged when they improve learning. They should identify the related handbook, relevant topic, and reason deeper study may help. They do not transfer ownership or license rights.

#### BUNDLE EXCEPTION

An authorized bundle may sell multiple independent handbooks together. The buyer receives rights to each handbook expressly listed in the bundle. The bundle is a purchase mechanism, not a merger of handbook identities.

#### PROMOTIONAL EXCEPTION

The publisher may grant temporary or permanent access to another handbook. Promotional access must define its scope and does not create a permanent rule for other purchasers.

---

### 7. COMPANION HANDBOOK PHILOSOPHY

A companion handbook is an independent work that provides deeper, adjacent, or specialized coverage useful to readers of another handbook.

Companion relationships describe educational relevance. They do not automatically create shared licensing.

Companion works must be optional by default. The series rejects hidden prerequisites created merely to force additional purchases. A handbook marketed as independent must contain enough information to meet its own stated learning objectives.

#### REFERENCE DEPTH RULE

When a topic primarily belongs to another handbook, the current work should explain enough context for the current chapter and then offer an optional deeper reference.

**Example**

> The Security Engineering Handbook may explain memory corruption sufficiently for exploit mitigation. The Operating Systems or Compiler handbook may contain deeper memory-layout or executable-format treatment. The security reader must still be able to understand the security lesson.

A companion handbook normally requires its own license.

#### EXCEPTIONS

A publisher-authorized companion bundle may grant both handbooks. A promotion may include companion access. A study guide, lab book, diagram atlas, or quick-reference publication may have a specially declared companion license. The word ‘companion’ alone never means free, included, or separately licensed; the product terms must say which model applies.

Marketing should avoid statements implying that another purchase is mandatory when it is not. Recommended cross-reference language should make clear that deeper coverage is optional.

---

### 8. SEQUEL, SERIES, AND VOLUME PHILOSOPHY

A publishing volume is a commercial and reading unit within a handbook. Volumes remain part of the same handbook identity unless explicitly published as separate handbooks.

Where handbook-level licensing is used, volumes in the same handbook family may share one license family and Handbook ID. However, license family and purchase entitlement are different concepts.

**LICENSE FAMILY** answers: Which handbook do these rights belong to?

**PURCHASE ENTITLEMENT** answers: Which volumes has this buyer actually purchased or been granted?

**Example**

> Linux Engineering Volume 1 and Volume 2 may share the Linux Handbook license family. A reader who purchased only Volume 1 does not automatically own Volume 2. After purchasing Volume 2, that entitlement can be attached to the same handbook license family.

A sequel may reuse the same license family when it clearly continues the same handbook, retains the same core subject identity, is published as a continuation, and is explicitly designated by the publisher as part of that family.

#### SEQUEL EXCEPTION

A sequel does not require a completely new license identity merely because it was released later. A Database Engineering sequel may be attached to the existing Database Engineering license family. The buyer may still need to purchase the sequel entitlement unless the applicable purchase terms include it.

A sequel should normally become an independent handbook when it moves into a substantially different engineering domain, has a fundamentally different purpose, has an independent curriculum and roadmap, is marketed as standalone, or would create confusing rights if grouped with the original.

Future volumes are not automatically free unless the product explicitly promises all-future-volume access, a subscription, lifetime handbook access, or another entitlement model.

#### LIFETIME ACCESS WARNING

The term ‘lifetime access’ must not be used casually. If offered, the terms must define whose lifetime or what product lifetime is meant, whether access covers the purchased edition only, whether future revisions are included, and whether major new editions are included.

---

### 9. EDUCATIONAL PHILOSOPHY AND LEGITIMATE LEARNING

Education is the primary purpose of the handbook ecosystem. Licensing should protect the sustainability of the work without preventing readers from learning and applying engineering knowledge.

The publisher does not own a reader’s understanding. A reader may use knowledge and skills learned from the handbook in education, employment, personal projects, research, and professional engineering.

**Example**

> A reader who learns API security may apply those principles to secure an employer’s API. This is legitimate use of learned knowledge.

A licensed reader may create personal notes, summaries, flashcards, and study material. Personal notes must not be transformed into a systematic redistributed substitute for the handbook.

**Allowed example**

> A student writes B+ tree notes in their own words for revision.

**Potentially prohibited example**

> A person recreates every chapter, diagram, exercise, and table as a ‘complete summary’ specifically designed to replace the paid handbook and distributes or sells it.

Students may cite and reference the handbook according to normal academic practice and applicable quotation rules. Purchasing a handbook does not authorize copying complete chapters into assignments, course packs, or public repositories.

An instructor may teach concepts learned from a handbook using independently created explanations and materials. Directly distributing handbook pages, reproducing substantial original diagrams, or using the handbook itself as official course material may require institutional or commercial training rights.

The publishing platform should support accessibility. Future DRM and watermarking must be reviewed for compatibility with assistive technologies and reasonable educational use.

### CURRICULUM MATURITY MODEL

The Engineering Handbook ecosystem classifies learning progression into six curriculum levels.

These levels are educational classifications only and do not affect licensing rights, ownership, pricing, or publication identity.

The official curriculum levels are:

1. Foundation
2. Intermediate
3. Advanced
4. Professional
5. Specialist
6. Capstone

The Capstone level represents the integration of knowledge acquired throughout the previous five levels into complete production-grade engineering systems, end-to-end implementations, architectural case studies, and comprehensive engineering projects.

Curriculum levels are descriptive rather than contractual and may evolve in future editions without affecting existing licenses.

#### GOOD-FAITH READER PRINCIPLE

Ordinary legitimate use should be presumed unless evidence indicates misuse. This does not prohibit anti-piracy systems. It means anti-piracy systems should not make the normal reading experience unnecessarily hostile.

---

### 10. SCOPE OF THIS MANUAL

This manual may govern Engineering Handbook Series publications and other future handbook families that expressly adopt it. It may apply to digital volumes, print editions, companion works, sequels, remastered editions, official supplementary materials, license certificates, and publisher-operated handbook platforms.

Later parts define the handbook licensing model, license types, institutional rights, digital identity, watermarking, anti-piracy, enforcement, ISBN and publication identity, website licensing architecture, third-party licensing providers and trackers, legal notices, content policies, and publishing operations.

Some matters remain primarily governed by separate standards:

- Pricing is governed by the Engineering Handbook Series Pricing Standard.
- Editorial structure and curriculum design are governed by the handbook-series editorial rules.
- Official code repositories use their declared software licenses, subject to the code policy defined later in this manual.
- Personal-data collection by a future publishing platform requires a dedicated privacy policy.
- Technical platform security should be governed by a separate security standard.

#### RECOMMENDED POLICY HIERARCHY

1. Applicable law and binding legal obligations.
2. Signed special agreements.
3. Public license terms applicable to the specific purchase.
4. This Publishing, Copyright & Licensing Manual.
5. Internal operational and implementation procedures.

Conflicts should be documented and resolved deliberately.

---

### 11. REVISION, VERSIONING, AND POLICY EVOLUTION

This manual is a living specification. The publishing ecosystem may introduce automated licensing, institutional dashboards, verification APIs, subscriptions, new formats, and new publication families. Material changes to rights or operations should be reflected in the manual.

**Recommended versioning:**

- **v1.0** — First formally adopted manual.
- **v1.1, v1.2** — Compatible clarifications, additions, and minor policy improvements.
- **v2.0** — Major structural or licensing-philosophy change.

Typographical corrections that do not change policy do not require a major version change.

Every formal revision should maintain a change log containing the version, effective date, changed sections, summary, reason, and whether existing licenses are affected.

A future manual revision should not silently remove rights already granted under a binding license. The publisher must decide whether a change applies only to future purchases, allows voluntary migration, preserves old terms for existing buyers, or requires another treatment under applicable law.

Emergency operational action may be required because of legal requirements, security incidents, fraud, licensing abuse, or third-party platform changes. Emergency action should later be documented if it creates a lasting policy change.

The manual should receive formal review before launching the dedicated handbook website, introducing institutional or enterprise sales, expanding internationally, implementing invasive tracking or DRM, and adopting a publication model not covered by current rules.

#### FINAL PRINCIPLE OF PART I

Copyright establishes the foundation of ownership. Licensing defines permission. Publishing policy creates consistency. The handbook ecosystem should protect original work, preserve reader trust, and remain scalable without turning legitimate education into an unnecessarily restricted experience.

---

### 12. Decision Summary

1. This manual is the common internal policy framework for publishing and licensing.

2. Copyright ownership and purchaser usage rights are separate concepts.

3. Each independent handbook is independently licensed by default.

4. Cross-references and companion recommendations do not transfer licenses.

5. Companion handbooks remain optional and educationally independent by default.

6. Volumes may share a handbook license family while retaining separate purchase entitlements.

7. A sequel may remain in the same license family when explicitly designated as a continuation.

8. Future volumes are not automatically included unless the purchase terms grant that entitlement.

9. Readers may apply learned engineering knowledge; protected handbook content remains subject to copyright and license restrictions.

10. Restrictions should target meaningful misuse rather than ordinary study.

11. Special agreements and applicable law may create documented exceptions.

12. The manual is versioned and may evolve, but previously granted rights must not be silently removed.

---

## Part II — Handbook Licensing Model

**Author and Publisher:** Sharique Chaudhary

**Status:** Master Manual — Part II

**Relationship:** Continues Part I — Publishing Philosophy & Intellectual Property Framework

---

### 1. PURPOSE OF THE HANDBOOK LICENSING MODEL

#### 1.1 Purpose

The handbook licensing model defines how licenses are associated with handbooks, volumes, sequels, companion works, editions, remastered works, bundles, and related publications.

Part I established the general principle that copyright ownership and purchaser usage rights are separate. Part II converts that philosophy into a practical licensing structure.

The model must answer questions such as:

- Does one license cover every handbook in the catalogue?
- Does purchasing one volume grant access to later volumes?
- Can several purchased volumes share one License ID?
- Does a sequel require a new license?
- Is a companion handbook included?
- Does a remastered edition replace the original license?
- What happens when independent handbooks are sold as a bundle?
- How should a future website represent these relationships?

The objective is to create a licensing structure that remains understandable to readers and implementable in software.

#### 1.2 Core Design Principle

The licensing model separates four concepts:

**HANDBOOK IDENTITY**

What intellectual and publishing work does the content belong to?

**LICENSE FAMILY**

Under which handbook licensing relationship are rights organized?

**PURCHASE ENTITLEMENT**

Which specific volumes, editions, or products has the buyer purchased or been granted?

**LICENSE TYPE**

Under what usage conditions may the entitled content be used?

These concepts must not be treated as interchangeable.

**Example**

> A reader may hold a Personal License for the Linux Engineering Handbook license family. The reader may currently have purchase entitlements for Volumes 1, 2, and 3 only.

The existence of the Linux license family does not automatically grant Volumes 4 through 20. The license identifies the rights framework. Entitlements identify accessible content.

#### 1.3 Why This Separation Is Necessary

Without this separation, the future licensing platform could incorrectly assume that:

- one purchased volume means ownership of every volume;
- a bundle creates one merged handbook;
- a sequel must always receive a new license;
- a remastered edition is automatically included;
- a companion work inherits the parent handbook's rights.

The model deliberately prevents those assumptions.

---

### 2. INDEPENDENT HANDBOOK PHILOSOPHY

#### 2.1 Default Rule

Every independent handbook is a separate educational, publishing, commercial, and licensing work.

**DEFAULT RULE**

> **ONE INDEPENDENT HANDBOOK = ONE INDEPENDENT HANDBOOK LICENSE FAMILY**

Examples include:

- Operating Systems Engineering Handbook
- Linux Engineering Handbook
- Computer Networks Engineering Handbook
- Backend Engineering Handbook
- Security Engineering Handbook
- Data Engineering Handbook

A license associated with one of these works does not automatically authorize another.

#### 2.2 Subject Overlap Does Not Merge Licenses

Engineering disciplines naturally overlap.

Linux discusses operating-system concepts. Backend engineering discusses databases and networks. Security engineering discusses operating systems, browsers, APIs, cloud systems, and programming languages.

Overlap does not create shared licensing.

The test is not whether two books discuss similar concepts. The test is whether the publisher has classified them as the same handbook or as independent works.

#### 2.3 Independent Handbook Identity

Each independent handbook should eventually receive its own internal Handbook ID.

**Illustrative format**

```text
HB-LINUX
HB-OS
HB-NETWORKS
HB-SECURITY
```

The exact technical ID format is defined later in the manual.

The Handbook ID should remain stable across ordinary volume additions and compatible revisions. A major publishing reclassification may justify a new identity, but such a decision must be explicit.

#### 2.4 Commercial Independence

Independent licensing allows each handbook to have:

- its own price classification;
- its own release schedule;
- its own volume count;
- its own edition history;
- its own maintenance cycle;
- its own institutional adoption;
- its own license records.

A reader may therefore purchase only the handbooks relevant to their needs.

#### 2.5 Educational Independence

The licensing model reinforces the editorial requirement established in Part I.

A handbook marketed as independent must not intentionally omit essential explanations solely to force purchase of another handbook.

Optional deeper references are permitted. Hidden commercial prerequisites are not.

#### 2.6 Exception: Explicit Integrated Product

The publisher may create a future product that intentionally combines several domains into one integrated handbook.

**For example**

> Systems Infrastructure Engineering Handbook

If the work has one unified curriculum, one publication identity, and one declared Handbook ID, it may be treated as one independent handbook even if it contains operating systems, networking, and cloud topics.

This exception must be determined before publication. Merely bundling three existing handbooks does not create an integrated handbook.

---

### 3. ONE HANDBOOK, ONE INDEPENDENT LICENSE PRINCIPLE

#### 3.1 Meaning of the Principle

The phrase "one handbook, one independent license" means that rights for one independent handbook do not automatically extend to other independent handbooks.

It does not necessarily mean that the system must generate a completely new License ID for every individual PDF.

A license platform may maintain one customer account and multiple license records.

**Example**

```text
Customer Account
│
├── License: Linux Engineering Handbook — Personal
├── License: Computer Networks Engineering Handbook — Personal
└── License: Security Engineering Handbook — Personal
```

The account is shared. The handbook licenses remain independent.

#### 3.2 Why a Universal Catalogue License Is Not the Default

A single purchase granting all current and future handbooks would create several problems:

- unequal value between early and later purchasers;
- difficulty pricing a rapidly expanding catalogue;
- unclear institutional rights;
- unsustainable future publication obligations;
- inability to classify independent works properly.

Therefore, no buyer receives catalogue-wide rights merely because they purchased one handbook.

#### 3.3 Multiple Handbooks Under One Transaction

A buyer may purchase several handbooks in one checkout transaction.

This does not merge the licenses.

The purchase record may contain one order, while the licensing system creates or updates multiple handbook license relationships.

```text
ORDER #1001
│
├── Linux entitlement
├── Networks entitlement
└── Backend entitlement
```

The transaction is one. The licensed handbook scopes are three.

#### 3.4 Same License Type Across Handbooks

A buyer may hold the same license type for multiple handbooks.

**For example**

- Linux — Personal License
- Networks — Personal License
- Backend — Personal License

The repeated license type does not create a universal Personal License for the entire series.

#### 3.5 Explicit Catalogue License Exception

A catalogue-wide or series-wide license may be created in the future for a specifically defined product, institutional agreement, enterprise agreement, or promotional program.

Such a license must explicitly identify:

- the catalogue or series covered;
- whether future handbooks are included;
- the license duration;
- the authorized users;
- excluded products;
- edition rights;
- termination and renewal rules.

A catalogue license is an exception and must never be inferred from a normal handbook purchase.

---

### 4. VOLUME LICENSING AND PURCHASE ENTITLEMENTS

#### 4.1 Volume as a Commercial Unit

A publishing volume is a purchasable content unit within a handbook.

A handbook may contain:

```text
Volume 1
Volume 2
Volume 3
…
Volume 40
```

The volume structure supports manageable publication, pricing, reading, updates, and delivery.

#### 4.2 Handbook License Family vs Volume Entitlement

Volumes within the same handbook normally belong to the same handbook license family.

However, the buyer only receives entitlements granted by the purchase.

**Example**

```text
Database Engineering Handbook License Family

Entitled:
- Volume 1
- Volume 2
- Volume 3

Not Entitled:
- Volume 4
- Volume 5
```

The buyer is a licensed Database Engineering reader, but cannot access unpaid volumes.

#### 4.3 Individual Volume Purchases

The publisher may sell volumes individually.

When Volume 1 is purchased:

- the buyer accepts or receives the applicable license;
- the handbook license relationship is created if necessary;
- Volume 1 entitlement is recorded.

When Volume 2 is later purchased:

- the existing handbook license relationship may be reused;
- Volume 2 entitlement is added.

This avoids unnecessary duplication while preserving precise purchase history.

#### 4.4 Complete Handbook Purchases

A handbook may be sold as a complete collection of all currently published volumes.

The product terms must state whether the purchase includes:

A. only volumes published at the purchase date;

B. future volumes in the same edition;

C. all future volumes in the handbook;

D. a subscription period;

E. another explicitly defined entitlement.

The phrase **"complete handbook"** should not automatically imply future content.

#### 4.5 Future Volume Rule

**DEFAULT RULE**

> **PURCHASING EXISTING VOLUMES DOES NOT AUTOMATICALLY GRANT FUTURE VOLUMES.**

Future volumes require a separate purchase or another valid entitlement unless the buyer was explicitly promised future-volume access.

This rule protects the publisher from unintentionally creating an unlimited future publication obligation.

#### 4.6 Volume Removal or Consolidation

A later edition may merge, split, or retire volumes.

Existing purchase records should be preserved.

If Volume 4 and Volume 5 are merged into a revised Volume 4, the publisher must define whether existing buyers receive the consolidated revision.

The decision should consider:

- whether the change is a correction;
- whether substantial new material was added;
- whether the publication remains the same edition;
- the published upgrade policy.

#### 4.7 Complimentary Volume Entitlements

The publisher may grant a volume without payment for:

- promotions;
- review copies;
- scholarships;
- accessibility arrangements;
- customer support resolutions;
- contributor access;
- launch campaigns.

The entitlement record should identify that access was granted rather than purchased.

Complimentary access remains subject to its declared license conditions.

#### 4.8 CURRICULUM LEVEL INDEPENDENCE

Curriculum levels are independent of licensing.

Whether a volume is classified as Foundation, Intermediate, Advanced, Professional, Specialist, or Capstone has no effect on:

- License type
- Purchase entitlement
- Upgrade eligibility
- Edition rights
- Bundle eligibility
- Ownership
- Copyright

Curriculum levels exist solely to communicate educational progression.

Licensing decisions are based on handbook identity, edition, volume entitlement, and applicable license terms rather than curriculum classification.

---

### 5. COMPANION HANDBOOK LICENSING RULES

#### 5.1 Default Companion Rule

A companion handbook is independently licensed unless an explicit product term says otherwise.

**Example**

> Operating Systems Engineering Handbook
> Companion recommendation: Linux Engineering Handbook

Purchasing Operating Systems does not grant Linux.

#### 5.2 Why Companion Works Remain Separate

A companion handbook may contain its own:

- curriculum;
- volumes;
- edition history;
- pricing;
- research effort;
- maintenance cycle;
- institutional use cases.

Educational relevance is not sufficient reason to transfer commercial rights.

#### 5.3 Companion Bundle

The publisher may create a companion bundle.

**Example**

```text
Systems Foundations Bundle

- Operating Systems Engineering Handbook
- Linux Engineering Handbook
- Computer Networks Engineering Handbook
```

A buyer receives entitlements for the explicitly listed works.

Each handbook retains its own Handbook ID and licensing scope.

#### 5.4 Included Companion Material

A small companion product may be included with a handbook.

**Examples**

- quick-reference guide;
- official exercise answer supplement;
- diagram atlas;
- study checklist.

If included, the product description and entitlement record should identify the included material.

#### 5.5 Companion Access Does Not Create Precedent

If one edition includes a companion guide for free, the publisher is not automatically required to include all future companion publications.

Each included product should be expressly identified.

#### 5.6 Institutional Companion Use

An institution licensing Handbook A does not receive classroom rights to Companion Handbook B unless B is separately licensed or expressly included in the institutional agreement.

This rule applies even when the instructor personally owns both handbooks.

---

### 6. SEQUEL LICENSING AND SAME-LICENSE EXCEPTION

#### 6.1 Purpose of the Sequel Exception

A genuine continuation should not be forced into a completely unrelated license identity merely because it was released later.

The sequel exception permits a continuation to remain within the same handbook license family.

#### 6.2 Qualification Test

A publication may be classified as a same-family sequel when most of the following are true:

- it directly continues the original handbook;
- it retains the same core engineering domain;
- its curriculum extends the original learning path;
- it is marketed as a continuation;
- its naming clearly indicates the relationship;
- using the same Handbook ID family improves reader clarity;
- the publisher expressly approves the classification.

No single factor automatically determines sequel status.

#### 6.3 Same License Family Does Not Mean Free

This distinction is mandatory.

> **SAME LICENSE FAMILY DOES NOT MEAN AUTOMATIC PURCHASE ENTITLEMENT.**

**Example**

> **Database Engineering Handbook**
> **Advanced Database Engine Construction — Official Sequel**

The sequel may use the Database Engineering license family.

An existing buyer may still need to purchase the sequel. After purchase, the sequel entitlement is attached to the existing license relationship.

#### 6.4 Sequel Included by Purchase Terms

A special product may expressly include sequel rights.

**Example**

> Database Engineering Lifetime Handbook Package

If the terms explicitly include future official sequels within the same handbook family, the sequel may be automatically granted.

Such promises must be defined narrowly and reviewed carefully.

#### 6.5 Independent Sequel Decision

A continuation should receive a new handbook identity if its purpose has changed enough that independent treatment is clearer.

**Example**

> **Database Engineering Handbook**
> vs.
> **Build Your Own Distributed Database Company Platform**

The second work may use database knowledge but could have a different purpose, audience, curriculum, and generation classification.

The publisher should classify it independently before release.

#### 6.6 Sequel Decision Record

Every ambiguous sequel should receive an internal classification record containing:

- proposed publication name;
- related handbook;
- same-family or independent decision;
- reasons;
- entitlement treatment;
- edition relationship;
- approval date.

This record prevents future confusion.

---

### 7. EDITION SEPARATION AND EDITION RIGHTS

#### 7.1 Edition Definition

An edition represents a formally published state of a handbook or volume.

**Examples**

- First Edition
- Second Edition
- Remastered Edition

Minor corrections do not automatically create a new edition.

#### 7.2 Default Edition Rule

A license entitlement should identify the edition to which access applies.

Purchasing First Edition does not automatically grant every future major edition.

Major edition access is governed by the applicable upgrade policy.

#### 7.3 Minor Revisions

Typographical corrections, broken references, minor factual corrections, and similar maintenance may be issued within the same edition.

Where operationally practical, licensed readers of that edition should receive corrected files without repurchasing the volume.

This is the preferred policy because readers should not be charged merely for error correction.

#### 7.4 Major Edition

A major edition may involve:

- substantial curriculum restructuring;
- major chapter rewrites;
- significant new technical coverage;
- replacement of obsolete material;
- new projects;
- new diagrams;
- changed educational architecture.

A major edition may be sold separately.

Existing buyers may receive upgrade pricing under the Pricing Standard.

#### 7.5 Edition Coexistence

Old and new editions may coexist.

A buyer licensed for First Edition retains rights to the First Edition under the terms that apply to that purchase, subject to law and valid termination provisions.

The publisher may stop selling an old edition without automatically revoking existing lawful entitlements.

#### 7.6 Security or Legal Removal Exception

Content may need to be removed or access restricted because of:

- a legal order;
- confirmed third-party rights infringement;
- dangerous accidental disclosure;
- severe platform security issues.

Such cases should be handled under documented incident procedures. They are not ordinary edition upgrades.

---

### 8. REMASTERED EDITION RULES

#### 8.1 Definition

A remastered edition is not merely a corrected revision.

It is a substantial reconstruction of an existing handbook intended to improve depth, curriculum, explanations, diagrams, practical coverage, technical accuracy, or overall publishing quality.

#### 8.2 Why Remastered Editions Require Special Treatment

The Engineering Handbook Series may begin with an earlier edition and later apply the expanded "massacre" curriculum methodology to rebuild the subject at a much greater scale.

Such a work may contain significantly more intellectual and production effort than the original edition.

Automatically treating it as a free minor update would make the edition classification meaningless.

#### 8.3 Default Remastered Rule

**DEFAULT RULE**

> **A REMASTERED EDITION IS A NEW COMMERCIAL EDITION.**

Existing buyers do not automatically receive the full remastered edition unless the original purchase terms explicitly promised it.

#### 8.4 Existing Buyer Treatment

Existing buyers should normally be considered for preferential upgrade treatment.

Possible models include:

- percentage upgrade discount;
- loyalty pricing;
- credit for previously purchased volumes;
- limited-time remaster upgrade offer;
- bundle conversion.

The Pricing Standard determines the commercial framework.

#### 8.5 License Family

A remastered edition may remain within the same broad handbook license family while using a distinct Edition ID.

**Example**

```text
Handbook ID: HB-DATABASE
Edition ID: ED-01

Remastered:
Handbook ID: HB-DATABASE
Edition ID: ED-RM01
```

This preserves the publication relationship while keeping entitlements separate.

#### 8.6 New Handbook Identity Exception

A remastered work may receive a new Handbook ID if the scope changes so radically that it is no longer reasonably the same handbook.

This should be rare and documented.

#### 8.7 Original Edition Rights

Purchasing the remastered edition does not automatically grant the original edition unless the product includes archival access.

Likewise, owning the original does not automatically grant the remaster.

The publisher may include both for convenience, but the entitlement must be explicit.

---

### 9. BUNDLE LICENSING

#### 9.1 Bundle Definition

A bundle is a purchasing arrangement containing multiple products.

A bundle may contain:

- several volumes from one handbook;
- several independent handbooks;
- a handbook and companion publication;
- an edition upgrade package;
- a curated series collection.

#### 9.2 Bundle Does Not Merge Intellectual Property

A bundle does not create one new handbook merely because several works are sold together.

Each handbook retains its identity.

#### 9.3 Entitlement Recording

The licensing system should record the products granted by the bundle.

**Example**

```text
Bundle: Core Systems Collection

Granted:

HB-OS          — Volumes 1–15
HB-LINUX      — Volumes 1–16
HB-NETWORKS   — Volumes 1–15
```

The bundle purchase record may remain linked for billing and support purposes.

#### 9.4 Bundle Updates

Future products are not automatically added to a previously purchased bundle unless the bundle terms promise ongoing additions.

A bundle called **"2027 Core Systems Collection"** may contain a fixed product list.

A subscription bundle may evolve during the subscription term.

These are different products and must be described differently.

#### 9.5 Partial Ownership and Bundle Purchase

A reader may already own some products in a bundle.

The publisher may choose to offer:

- dynamic bundle pricing;
- upgrade credit;
- fixed bundle pricing;
- no duplicate discount.

The selected commercial rule belongs in the Pricing Standard and product terms.

The licensing system must avoid creating conflicting duplicate entitlements.

#### 9.6 Refunds

If a bundle is refunded, entitlements granted solely by that bundle may be removed or revoked according to the refund and licensing policy.

Entitlements independently purchased before the bundle must remain intact.

---

### 10. CROSS-REFERENCE LICENSING RULES

#### 10.1 Purpose of Cross-References

Cross-references connect related engineering concepts across the handbook ecosystem.

They may direct readers to:

- another chapter in the same volume;
- another volume in the same handbook;
- a companion handbook;
- an independent handbook;
- an official supplementary resource.

#### 10.2 Cross-Reference Does Not Grant Access

A reference to another publication does not create an entitlement to that publication.

**Example**

> *"For a deeper treatment of consensus, see the Distributed Systems Engineering Handbook."*

This recommendation does not grant access to the Distributed Systems handbook.

#### 10.3 Avoiding Broken Learning Paths

A cross-reference should not replace an explanation that is necessary to understand the current chapter.

If the reader must know a concept to continue, the current handbook should provide the necessary explanation.

The cross-reference may then provide deeper optional study.

#### 10.4 Licensed Digital Cross-Links

A future handbook platform may create clickable cross-handbook links.

If the reader owns the referenced content, the platform may open it directly.

If the reader does not own it, the platform may show:

- publication information;
- a brief description;
- purchase or access options.

The platform should not imply that the reader already owns the referenced material.

#### 10.5 Preview Exception

The publisher may provide a lawful preview of referenced material.

Preview access is not a full license entitlement and should be identified as preview content.

---

### 11. EXCEPTIONS, EDGE CASES, AND CLASSIFICATION PROCEDURE

#### 11.1 Why Edge Cases Must Be Documented

A catalogue of hundreds of volumes will eventually produce publication relationships that do not fit simple labels.

The solution is not to abandon the model. The solution is to document the classification decision.

#### 11.2 Ambiguous Publication Test

When a new work is difficult to classify, review:

1. Does it have an independent learning objective?
2. Does it have an independent curriculum?
3. Is it a continuation of an existing handbook?
4. Does it serve the same primary audience?
5. Does it remain in the same engineering domain?
6. Is it marketed as standalone?
7. Would a shared license family confuse buyers?
8. Does it require independent institutional adoption?
9. Does it have a separate edition lifecycle?
10. What treatment best preserves reader clarity?

The publisher should then classify the work as:

- same-handbook volume;
- same-family sequel;
- companion publication;
- remastered edition;
- independent handbook;
- bundle-only supplementary product;
- another expressly defined category.

#### 11.3 Special License Override

A signed institutional, enterprise, translation, or publishing agreement may override the default model for the covered party.

The override should be explicit.

**Example**

> A university agreement may license five independent handbooks under one administrative contract. The handbooks remain independent, but the contract manages them together.

#### 11.4 Platform Limitation

A third-party licensing provider may not support the ideal license hierarchy.

In that case, the internal records should preserve the intended model even if the vendor uses simplified product keys.

The project should avoid allowing a vendor's database structure to redefine the publishing philosophy.

#### 11.5 Migration

When migrating from a third-party system to the publisher's own platform, existing valid entitlements should be mapped to:

- customer identity;
- license type;
- Handbook ID;
- Edition ID;
- Volume IDs or product entitlements;
- purchase or grant history.

Migration must not silently convert limited rights into catalogue-wide rights or remove valid purchased entitlements.

#### 11.6 Manual Resolution

If an entitlement dispute cannot be resolved automatically, the publisher should review:

- purchase evidence;
- license records;
- product terms at purchase time;
- edition history;
- bundle composition;
- prior support decisions.

Manual corrections should be logged.

#### 11.7 No Implied Expansion Rule

When a situation is not covered, rights should not automatically expand to every related publication.

The issue should be reviewed and clarified.

This rule prevents accidental creation of unlimited rights through ambiguity.

#### 11.8 Reader-Favouring Clarification

The no-implied-expansion rule does not authorize misleading ambiguity.

If the publisher's own product description clearly created a reasonable expectation of specific access, the matter should be reviewed fairly and in light of applicable consumer law.

The publisher should correct unclear product language rather than repeatedly relying on technical loopholes.

---

### 12. FUTURE WEBSITE IMPLEMENTATION GUIDANCE

#### 12.1 Recommended Conceptual Model

The future licensing platform should conceptually separate:

- USER
- LICENSE
- LICENSE TYPE
- HANDBOOK
- EDITION
- VOLUME
- PRODUCT
- ORDER
- ENTITLEMENT
- BUNDLE

A simplified relationship may be:

```text
USER
│
└── LICENSE
    ├── LICENSE TYPE
    ├── HANDBOOK
    └── ENTITLEMENTS
        ├── EDITION
        └── VOLUME / PRODUCT
```

Orders prove commercial transactions. Entitlements define access. Licenses define permitted use.

#### 12.2 Do Not Use Payment Records as the Entire License Database

Payment history alone is insufficient.

A user may receive:

- a complimentary copy;
- an institutional entitlement;
- an upgraded edition;
- a replacement entitlement;
- a scholarship grant;
- migrated access.

The licensing system therefore needs explicit entitlement records.

#### 12.3 Immutable Historical Context

The system should preserve enough historical information to determine what the buyer was promised at the time of purchase.

Product descriptions and bundle composition may change later.

Where practical, order records should reference a versioned product definition or store relevant purchase-time terms.

#### 12.4 Human-Readable License View

A customer dashboard should eventually display rights in understandable language.

**Example**

```text
Security Engineering Handbook

License: Personal
Edition: First Edition
Entitled Volumes: 1–12
Status: Active
```

It should not expose only internal database identifiers.

#### 12.5 Administrative Override

Authorized administrators may need to correct entitlement records.

Every override should record:

- administrator identity;
- date and time;
- previous state;
- new state;
- reason.

This protects both the publisher and the reader.

---

### 13. Decision Summary

1. Every independent handbook has an independent handbook licensing scope by default.
2. Subject overlap does not merge handbook licenses.
3. A customer account may contain multiple independent handbook licenses.
4. Handbook license family and purchase entitlement are separate concepts.
5. Volumes in one handbook may share a license family while remaining separately purchasable.
6. Existing volume purchases do not automatically grant future volumes.
7. Companion handbooks are independently licensed unless expressly included.
8. A same-family sequel may reuse the original handbook license family.
9. Same-family sequel status does not make the sequel free.
10. Major editions may have separate commercial entitlements.
11. Minor corrections should normally remain available to licensed readers of the same edition.
12. A remastered edition is a new commercial edition by default.
13. Existing buyers may receive preferential remastered-edition upgrade treatment.
14. Bundles grant the specifically identified products and do not merge handbook identities.
15. Cross-references do not grant access to referenced handbooks.
16. Ambiguous publications must receive a documented classification decision.
17. Special written agreements may expressly override standard rules for covered parties.
18. Third-party platform limitations must not redefine the internal licensing philosophy.
19. Future software should separate licenses, orders, products, and entitlements.
20. Ambiguity must not be used to mislead readers or silently create unlimited rights.

---

## Part III — License Types & Rights

**Author and Publisher:** Sharique Chaudhary

**Status:** Master Manual — Part III

**Relationship:** Continues Part II — Handbook Licensing Model

---

### 1. PURPOSE OF LICENSE TYPES

A license type defines WHO may use licensed handbook content, FOR WHAT PURPOSE, and under WHAT CONDITIONS.

License type is separate from purchase entitlement.

**Example:**

A purchaser may be entitled to Security Engineering Handbook Volumes 1–10.

The entitlement answers which content is available.

The license type answers whether that content is being used personally, by a verified student, by an educational institution, by an enterprise, or in another authorized context.

The standard license families established by this manual are:

1. Personal License
2. Student License
3. Educational Institution License
4. Enterprise License
5. Commercial Training License
6. Library License
7. Government and Public-Sector License
8. Translation and Localization License

Additional special licenses may be introduced later. A new license type must define its rights, restrictions, authorized users, entitlement model, duration where applicable, and relationship to existing licenses.

No license should rely solely on its name. The actual granted rights must be documented.

---

### 2. RIGHTS COMMON TO LEGITIMATE LICENSES

Unless a specific license states otherwise, an authorized user may use entitled content for legitimate reading and learning.

Common reader rights may include:

- reading licensed content;
- searching the content using supported reader functionality;
- highlighting and annotating;
- creating personal study notes;
- bookmarking;
- using learned knowledge in education and professional work;
- retaining lawfully supplied copies subject to the applicable access terms;
- using accessibility tools where reasonably supported;
- receiving corrections to the same edition where the publisher's update policy provides them.

These rights do not grant permission to:

- publicly redistribute complete handbook files;
- resell digital copies;
- upload files to public drives, torrents, forums, or unauthorized repositories;
- remove or falsify license identification for redistribution;
- use one personal purchase as an organizational content library;
- reproduce substantial protected content as a competing substitute;
- falsely claim authorship or ownership of handbook material.

The exact legal boundary of quotation, fair dealing, fair use, exhaustion, and other statutory rights depends on applicable law.

License language must not falsely claim to eliminate mandatory legal rights.

---

### 3. PERSONAL LICENSE

#### 3.1 Purpose

The Personal License is the default license for an individual purchasing a handbook for their own learning, reference, or professional development.

It is intended for software engineers, independent learners, hobbyists, researchers using the handbook personally, and professionals purchasing access for themselves.

#### 3.2 Authorized User

The authorized user is the named individual associated with the license.

The license is not a household, team, department, company, or classroom license.

#### 3.3 Permitted Uses

A Personal License normally permits the licensed individual to:

- read entitled volumes;
- use the handbook for personal study;
- annotate and highlight;
- create private notes;
- apply learned knowledge in personal or professional projects;
- use the handbook as a personal technical reference;
- access the handbook on personally controlled devices within reasonable technical limits;
- print limited material for personal use where the applicable format and law permit it.

The reader may discuss concepts learned from the handbook with other people.

#### 3.4 Professional Use of Learned Knowledge

A professional may apply knowledge learned from the handbook at work.

**Example:**

A backend engineer personally purchases the Database Engineering Handbook and uses the knowledge to improve query design at their employer.

This does not automatically require an Enterprise License.

The distinction changes when the handbook content itself becomes an organizational resource.

**Example:**

The engineer uploads the complete handbook to the company's internal LMS for 500 employees.

That is not personal use merely because the original purchaser is an employee.

#### 3.5 Device Use

The license should not be designed around an unnecessarily restrictive one-device rule.

A legitimate reader may reasonably use a phone, tablet, laptop, desktop, or replacement device.

The future platform may implement reasonable device or session controls to identify mass account sharing. Such controls should support device replacement and customer support resolution.

#### 3.6 Personal Backup

Where technically and contractually permitted, a reader may retain a reasonable private backup of a lawfully supplied file for personal continuity.

The backup must remain private and subject to the same license.

A backup copy does not become transferable.

#### 3.7 Prohibited Uses

A Personal License does not permit:

- sharing the complete handbook with friends or colleagues;
- distributing copies to students;
- placing files on an organizational LMS;
- using the handbook as licensed material in paid training;
- selling copies;
- public redistribution;
- mass account sharing;
- removing identification for the purpose of unauthorized distribution.

#### 3.8 Family and Friend Exception

There is no automatic family-sharing or friend-sharing right for digital handbook files.

A purchaser may show a brief passage or discuss the content in ordinary personal interaction, subject to applicable law. This is different from giving another person a complete reusable copy.

#### 3.9 Employer Reimbursement

If an employer reimburses an individual's Personal License, the license does not automatically become an Enterprise License.

The decisive factor is the granted license and intended use, not merely who paid the expense.

If the organization needs shared access, it should obtain the appropriate organizational license.

---

### 4. STUDENT LICENSE

#### 4.1 Purpose

The Student License exists to improve affordability for eligible students without turning student pricing into a general discount channel.

It remains an individual-use license.

#### 4.2 Authorized User

The license is issued to an eligible student after any verification required by the publisher.

Verification methods may include:

- recognized student email;
- current student identity document;
- enrollment evidence;
- approved educational verification provider;
- another reasonable method.

The publisher should collect only the information reasonably necessary for verification and should define retention practices in the future privacy policy.

#### 4.3 Rights

A Student License generally grants the same personal learning rights as a Personal License.

The student may:

- study the entitled content;
- annotate it;
- create private notes;
- use learned knowledge in assignments and projects;
- cite the handbook according to academic practice;
- use learned skills in internships and employment.

#### 4.4 Student License Is Not an Institutional License

A student discount does not authorize classroom redistribution.

A student may not upload the handbook to a class group, university drive, Discord server, Telegram group, LMS, or public repository for other students.

One student license serves one authorized student.

#### 4.5 Graduation

Graduation should not automatically destroy the student's lawful access to already purchased content merely because the student is no longer eligible for new student discounts.

**Recommended policy:**

Previously purchased student entitlements remain valid under their applicable license. Future purchases may require a Personal License or another eligible license type.

#### 4.6 Verification Renewal

For ongoing student benefits, the publisher may periodically require renewed verification.

Failure to renew should affect future student pricing or active student-only benefits, not silently erase already purchased entitlements unless the original product was expressly time-limited.

#### 4.7 Fraudulent Student Status

Deliberate falsification of student status may result in:

- cancellation of the discounted transaction where legally permitted;
- requirement to pay the applicable difference;
- suspension pending review;
- revocation in serious or repeated cases.

The publisher should distinguish documentation mistakes from intentional fraud.

#### 4.8 Institution-Purchased Student Rights

If a college purchases per-student learning rights, those rights are governed by the Educational Institution License rather than the ordinary Student License.

The student may receive an individual account, but the entitlement source and usage conditions remain institutional.

---

### 5. EDUCATIONAL INSTITUTION LICENSE

#### 5.1 Purpose

The Educational Institution License governs official use by colleges, universities, schools, and other approved educational institutions.

It exists because organizational teaching use is fundamentally different from one student purchasing a personal copy.

#### 5.2 Core Model

The default institutional model is:

```text
INSTITUTIONAL AUTHORIZATION + AUTHORIZED STUDENT LEARNING RIGHTS =
EDUCATIONAL USE
```

The institution does not obtain unlimited student distribution merely by paying one base license fee.

#### 5.3 Institutional Authorization

The institutional component authorizes the organization to adopt the identified handbook for approved educational use.

It may define:

- institution identity;
- campus scope;
- licensed handbook;
- editions and volumes;
- course or department scope where relevant;
- instructors;
- student allocation;
- term or duration;
- LMS permissions;
- reporting obligations.

#### 5.4 Per-Student Learning Rights

The institution must obtain rights corresponding to the number of students authorized to learn directly from the licensed handbook content, according to the final institutional pricing and licensing terms.

**Example:**

A college adopts Computer Networks Engineering for 120 students.

The college may require:

- institutional authorization for the handbook;
- 120 authorized student learning rights.

The institution cannot purchase one copy and distribute it to all 120 students.

#### 5.5 Student Access

The preferred future implementation is individual controlled access for each authorized student.

Students should not receive one unrestricted master PDF that can be copied indefinitely.

Access methods may include:

- individual licensed files;
- individual platform accounts;
- controlled LMS integration;
- institution-managed access approved by the publisher.

#### 5.6 Instructor Rights

Authorized instructors may receive rights necessary to prepare and deliver the licensed course.

These may include:

- instructor access to licensed content;
- private course planning;
- chapter references;
- limited classroom display;
- approved excerpts where permitted by the agreement.

Instructor rights do not automatically authorize public republication or creation of a commercial derivative handbook.

#### 5.7 LMS Use

Uploading a complete handbook to an LMS requires explicit institutional permission.

Where LMS hosting is authorized, the agreement should define:

- approved LMS;
- authentication requirements;
- enrolled-user restriction;
- download permissions;
- duration;
- removal obligations;
- instructor access;
- audit or reporting requirements where reasonable.

A publicly accessible LMS page is not acceptable controlled distribution.

#### 5.8 Student Count Changes

Institutions should report or license additional students when enrollment exceeds the authorized allocation.

The agreement may include a reasonable adjustment threshold or reconciliation process to avoid administrative disputes over minor temporary changes.

Deliberate systematic underreporting is a licensing violation.

#### 5.9 Multi-Campus Use

A license for one campus does not automatically authorize every campus, franchise, or affiliated institution.

Multi-campus rights must be expressly included.

The agreement may use:

- per-campus licensing;
- organization-wide licensing;
- centrally negotiated multi-campus licensing.

#### 5.10 Remote Learning

Remote students remain authorized students if included in the licensed count and access scope.

Remote delivery does not convert institutional material into public distribution.

#### 5.11 Institutional Independence Rule

Each independent handbook requires its own institutional licensing scope unless a multi-handbook institutional agreement expressly includes several works.

#### 5.12 Institutional Exceptions

Scholarship cohorts, nonprofit education initiatives, pilot programs, or public-interest programs may receive specially negotiated terms.

Such exceptions must be documented and do not establish general pricing or licensing precedent.

---

### 6. ENTERPRISE LICENSE

#### 6.1 Purpose

The Enterprise License governs organizational use by companies and other commercial entities for internal engineering education, employee development, onboarding, technical reference, or approved internal training.

#### 6.2 Authorized Organization

The license is issued to the identified legal or contractual organization.

Affiliates, subsidiaries, contractors, and parent companies are not automatically included unless the agreement defines them as authorized entities.

#### 6.3 Permitted Enterprise Uses

Depending on the agreement, enterprise rights may include:

- employee access;
- internal technical learning;
- engineering onboarding;
- internal training programs;
- approved internal LMS hosting;
- instructor or trainer access;
- internal reference use;
- controlled distribution to licensed employees.

#### 6.4 Employee Count or Seat Model

Enterprise access may be licensed by:

- named users;
- active seats;
- employee bands;
- department;
- business unit;
- negotiated organization-wide rights.

The pricing standard and enterprise agreement should define the chosen model.

#### 6.5 Internal Use Only

An Enterprise License normally covers internal organizational use.

It does not automatically authorize the company to:

- resell the handbook;
- include the handbook in a customer product;
- distribute copies to clients;
- use the handbook in paid public courses;
- translate and republish it;
- create a competing handbook from protected content.

#### 6.6 Contractors

Contractor access must be defined explicitly.

A company may be permitted to grant temporary access to contractors working directly on licensed internal activities.

The agreement should define whether contractors count as seats and when access must be removed.

#### 6.7 Employee Departure

Where platform access is organization-managed, access may be removed when an employee leaves the organization.

The employee does not automatically convert an enterprise entitlement into a Personal License.

Knowledge learned by the employee remains learned knowledge and is not erased.

#### 6.8 Enterprise Handbook Independence

Licensing Backend Engineering does not automatically grant Cloud Engineering, Security Engineering, or Software Architecture.

A multi-handbook enterprise agreement may cover several works when expressly listed.

---

### 7. COMMERCIAL TRAINING LICENSE

#### 7.1 Purpose

The Commercial Training License applies when handbook content is used as part of paid training delivered to clients, public learners, corporate customers, or commercial cohorts.

This license is distinct from an instructor personally learning from a handbook.

#### 7.2 When It Is Required

A Commercial Training License may be required when a trainer or training company:

- distributes handbook content to paying learners;
- adopts the handbook as official paid-course material;
- reproduces substantial diagrams or exercises;
- provides licensed handbook access as part of course fees;
- systematically teaches directly from protected content under the handbook brand.

#### 7.3 Teaching Knowledge vs Using Content

A trainer may learn a concept from the handbook and later explain that concept in their own original words and independently created material, subject to applicable law.

That does not automatically require a Commercial Training License.

The license becomes relevant when protected handbook content itself is being commercially used or distributed.

#### 7.4 Learner Rights

A commercial training agreement should define whether learners:

- receive temporary access;
- receive permanent individual entitlements;
- require individual licenses;
- are covered by cohort-based rights.

The trainer should not receive one file and duplicate it for unlimited paying students.

#### 7.5 Course Branding

A training provider may not imply official partnership, certification, endorsement, or authorization by the handbook publisher unless such rights are expressly granted.

#### 7.6 Official Training Partner Exception

The publisher may create an official training-partner program in the future.

Such a program should use a separate agreement defining branding, quality control, instructor requirements, learner licensing, reporting, and termination.

---

### 8. LIBRARY LICENSE

#### 8.1 Purpose

The Library License governs controlled access through academic, public, corporate, or specialized libraries.

A library use case differs from permanent distribution to every member.

#### 8.2 Access Models

A Library License may support:

- on-premises digital reading;
- authenticated remote reading;
- limited concurrent users;
- controlled digital lending where legally and contractually appropriate;
- physical reference copies;
- organization-specific access.

The exact model must be declared.

#### 8.3 Digital File Control

A library should not receive unrestricted permission to place the handbook on a publicly downloadable server.

Digital access should be controlled according to the agreed model.

#### 8.4 Concurrent Access

Digital library pricing and rights may use concurrent-user limits.

**Example:**

A university library may license five simultaneous readers for a handbook collection.

This is different from granting permanent individual copies to every student.

#### 8.5 Course Adoption

A Library License does not automatically replace an Educational Institution License when a handbook is officially adopted for a course and distributed to an entire class.

Library reference access and course learning rights are separate use cases.

#### 8.6 Archival Rights

Long-term archival preservation may require specific terms, particularly for digital formats and discontinued editions.

The publisher may permit preservation copies that are not available for unrestricted distribution.

---

### 9. GOVERNMENT AND PUBLIC-SECTOR LICENSE

#### 9.1 Purpose

Government departments, public agencies, public research organizations, and similar bodies may require a dedicated licensing structure because procurement, user scope, security, and record requirements can differ from ordinary enterprise purchasing.

#### 9.2 Permitted Uses

A Government License may authorize:

- employee learning;
- internal technical training;
- controlled reference access;
- approved agency LMS use;
- defined inter-department access.

#### 9.3 Agency Scope

The agreement must identify whether the license covers:

- one department;
- one agency;
- a ministry;
- a regional body;
- multiple named public entities.

A purchase by one government unit does not automatically authorize the entire government.

#### 9.4 Public Disclosure

Government licensing does not automatically place copyrighted handbook content in the public domain.

Any public-records, procurement, or disclosure obligations should receive jurisdiction-specific legal review.

#### 9.5 Special Public-Interest Programs

The publisher may create special educational terms for public universities, workforce programs, or nonprofit government initiatives.

Such programs should be documented separately.

---

### 10. TRANSLATION AND LOCALIZATION LICENSE

#### 10.1 Purpose

A Translation and Localization License grants specific permission to translate or officially localize protected handbook content.

Purchasing a Personal or Institutional License does not grant translation-publication rights.

#### 10.2 Translation Is a Derivative Use

An unofficial complete translation can reproduce the substance and structure of the original handbook in another language.

Therefore, public or commercial translation requires explicit authorization, subject to applicable law.

#### 10.3 Agreement Requirements

An official translation agreement should define:

- handbook and volumes;
- source edition;
- target language;
- territory;
- exclusivity or non-exclusivity;
- translator responsibilities;
- technical review;
- terminology standards;
- layout and diagram treatment;
- ownership or licensing of translated text;
- royalties or payment;
- publication channels;
- update obligations;
- termination.

#### 10.4 Translator Attribution

Official translators should receive attribution according to the agreement.

Attribution does not automatically transfer ownership of the original handbook.

Rights in the translated expression must be contractually defined.

#### 10.5 Community Translation Exception

The publisher may authorize a nonprofit or community translation project.

The authorization should still define scope, distribution, quality control, and rights.

Community intent does not automatically create permission to translate the entire work.

#### 10.6 Machine Translation

A reader may use lawful accessibility or personal translation tools for private understanding where permitted by applicable terms and law.

Publishing or distributing a complete machine-translated version is a separate act and is not authorized by ordinary personal access.

---

### 11. LICENSE RESTRICTIONS COMMON TO MULTIPLE LICENSE TYPES

Unless expressly permitted, licenses do not grant rights to:

- resell digital handbook files;
- publicly redistribute complete copies;
- upload complete content to public repositories;
- remove license identification to facilitate redistribution;
- issue sublicenses;
- claim authorship;
- create unauthorized official translations;
