- reporting suspected security compromises where reasonably practicable;
- cooperating during legitimate investigations; and
- taking reasonable corrective action where a licensing issue is identified.

---

#### 26.3 Institutions and Organizations

Institutional customers should ensure that:

- handbook access is limited to authorized users;
- license quantities remain consistent with actual usage;
- internal distribution complies with applicable license terms;
- administrative accounts are properly managed;
- departing personnel lose access where appropriate; and
- internal policies support continued licensing compliance.

---

#### 26.4 Contributors and Publishing Partners

Authors, editors, reviewers, translators, designers, contractors, and other publishing partners who receive access to protected materials should:

- maintain confidentiality where required;
- protect unpublished content;
- comply with applicable contractual obligations;
- avoid unauthorized disclosure; and
- report known security incidents affecting protected materials.

---
Effective copyright protection depends upon shared responsibility rather than enforcement alone. Each participant should perform their respective obligations in a manner that supports the integrity of the licensing ecosystem.

---

### 27. Internal Compliance Reviews

The publisher should periodically review its own licensing and anti-piracy operations to verify that established procedures remain effective and are being applied consistently.

Internal compliance reviews may evaluate:

- licensing documentation;
- investigation procedures;
- record-management practices;
- security controls;
- watermark implementation;
- customer communication;
- enforcement consistency; and
- operational effectiveness.

Where deficiencies are identified, appropriate corrective measures should be implemented within a reasonable timeframe.

The purpose of internal compliance reviews is not solely to identify violations but also to improve operational quality, reduce unnecessary administrative risk, and strengthen the overall licensing framework.

---

### 28. Technology Neutrality

The principles established within this Manual are intended to remain effective regardless of future technological developments.

Accordingly, the rights, obligations, and enforcement procedures described herein apply irrespective of:

- file format;
- document delivery platform;
- reading application;
- operating system;
- cloud infrastructure;
- storage medium;
- authentication technology; or
- future digital publishing methods.

As publishing technologies evolve, the publisher may modify technical implementation methods without altering the underlying licensing principles established by this Manual.

Technology should therefore be regarded as an implementation mechanism rather than the source of legal rights or contractual obligations. Copyright ownership, licensing conditions, and anti-piracy responsibilities remain governed by the applicable agreements and relevant law regardless of the technologies used to distribute or access handbook publications.

### 29. Policy Review and Amendment

This Part of the Manual should be reviewed periodically to ensure that its provisions remain consistent with evolving legal requirements, technological developments, publishing practices, and organizational objectives.

A review may be initiated in response to:

- significant changes in copyright legislation;
- developments in digital publishing technologies;
- emerging piracy methods;
- material security incidents;
- judicial decisions affecting copyright or licensing;
- operational experience gained through investigations;
- customer or institutional feedback; or
- broader changes to the Engineering Handbook licensing framework.

Where amendments are adopted, the publisher should ensure that revised policies are communicated through appropriate publication channels and incorporated into future handbook editions where applicable.

Unless expressly stated otherwise, amendments shall apply prospectively and shall not retroactively alter rights or obligations that were previously established under an earlier version of the applicable license agreement.

Regular review helps ensure that the anti-piracy framework remains effective, balanced, and aligned with current legal and operational requirements.

---

### 30. Interpretation of this Part

This Part shall be interpreted in a manner consistent with the overall objectives of the Engineering Handbook licensing framework, namely:

- protecting copyrighted works;
- supporting lawful educational use;
- promoting voluntary license compliance;
- ensuring proportionate and evidence-based enforcement; and
- maintaining a fair and sustainable publishing ecosystem.

Where uncertainty arises regarding the interpretation of a provision, the interpretation that best preserves these objectives while remaining consistent with applicable law, contractual obligations, and the publisher's licensing policies should be preferred.

Section headings, examples, explanatory notes, and illustrative scenarios are provided to improve clarity and facilitate consistent application. Unless expressly stated otherwise, they do not create independent contractual rights or obligations beyond those established by the governing license agreement and applicable law.

Nothing in this Part shall be interpreted as:

- limiting the publisher's statutory or contractual rights;
- preventing the publisher from exercising lawful remedies available under applicable law;
- creating rights in favor of unauthorized users beyond those provided by law;
- requiring enforcement action in every reported incident; or
- restricting the publisher from adopting reasonable operational procedures consistent with this Manual.

This Part should always be read together with the remaining provisions of the Publishing, Copyright & Licensing Manual, the applicable license agreement, and any other governing legal documents forming part of the Engineering Handbook licensing ecosystem.

### 31. Reservation of Rights

Except for the limited rights expressly granted under the applicable license agreement, the publisher reserves all rights relating to the Engineering Handbook Series and all associated intellectual property.

Without limitation, the publisher retains all rights concerning:

- copyright ownership;
- derivative works;
- translations;
- adaptations;
- revisions;
- new editions;
- supplementary publications;
- digital distribution methods;
- licensing programs;
- trademarks and branding;
- publisher identity; and
- all other intellectual property rights not expressly licensed.

No provision of this Manual shall be interpreted as granting any ownership interest in the handbook publications or any associated intellectual property unless such transfer is expressly authorized through a separate written agreement executed by the publisher.

The absence of an express prohibition within this Manual shall not be interpreted as creating an implied license, waiver of rights, or authorization for any activity beyond the scope of the applicable license agreement.

---

### 32. No Waiver

A failure or delay by the publisher in exercising any right, remedy, or enforcement power shall not constitute a waiver of that right.

Similarly:

- a decision not to pursue enforcement in one case does not establish permission for similar conduct in future cases;
- a voluntary settlement does not prevent future enforcement relating to separate incidents;
- corrective actions accepted in one investigation do not create precedent for all subsequent investigations; and
- isolated administrative decisions shall not modify the interpretation of this Manual unless formally adopted as part of an authorized policy revision.

Any waiver of rights must be expressly authorized in writing by the publisher or an individual acting with appropriate authority on the publisher's behalf.

---

### 33. Severability

If any provision of this Part is determined by a court or other competent authority to be invalid, unenforceable, or unlawful under applicable law, that determination shall affect only the specific provision to the extent necessary.

The remaining provisions shall continue in full force and effect unless their continued operation would be legally impossible or fundamentally inconsistent with the purpose of this Manual.

Where reasonably practicable, any invalid provision should be interpreted or replaced in a manner that most closely reflects the original purpose while remaining consistent with applicable law.

---

### 34. Governing Principles for Future Technologies

The publisher recognizes that future technological developments may introduce new methods for creating, distributing, accessing, or reproducing digital publications.

Accordingly, the principles established within this Manual are intended to apply to future technologies regardless of whether such technologies presently exist.

Examples may include:

- artificial intelligence systems;
- automated content-generation platforms;
- decentralized storage networks;
- blockchain-based distribution systems;
- future cloud-computing environments;
- immersive educational platforms;
- extended-reality publishing technologies; and
- other emerging methods of digital content distribution.

The emergence of new technologies does not diminish copyright ownership, alter licensing rights, or eliminate contractual obligations unless expressly modified through an authorized amendment to the applicable licensing framework.

The publisher may adopt additional technical safeguards or operational procedures as technology evolves, provided such measures remain consistent with applicable law and the fundamental licensing principles established by this Manual.

### 35. Final Statement

The Engineering Handbook anti-piracy framework exists to preserve the integrity, sustainability, and continued development of the handbook ecosystem while respecting the legitimate rights of licensed customers.

The publisher recognizes that the overwhelming majority of readers, educational institutions, and organizational customers seek to comply with their licensing obligations and use handbook publications for lawful educational and professional purposes.

Accordingly, the primary objective of this Part is not to maximize enforcement activity, but to:

- encourage voluntary compliance;
- promote responsible use of licensed publications;
- protect the rights of legitimate license holders;
- preserve the value of original educational content;
- ensure fair and proportionate enforcement; and
- maintain confidence in the Engineering Handbook licensing ecosystem.

Deliberate copyright infringement, commercial piracy, systematic unauthorized distribution, and other material violations remain incompatible with these objectives and may result in appropriate contractual, administrative, technical, or legal action.

At the same time, investigations should always remain evidence-based, proportionate, transparent, and consistent with the principles established throughout this Manual.

The long-term success of the Engineering Handbook Series depends upon cooperation between the publisher, contributors, institutions, organizations, and licensed customers. Collectively, these stakeholders contribute to a publishing ecosystem founded upon intellectual property protection, professional integrity, lawful educational use, and mutual respect for copyright.

---

### 36. Conclusion

This Part establishes the official anti-piracy and enforcement framework governing the Engineering Handbook Series.

It defines the principles by which suspected piracy is identified, investigated, documented, and addressed while ensuring that enforcement remains consistent with the broader objectives of the Publishing, Copyright & Licensing Manual.

The framework is built upon several fundamental principles:

- copyright protection should be balanced with fairness;
- investigations should rely upon credible evidence rather than assumption;
- enforcement should remain proportionate to the seriousness of the violation;
- legitimate educational and professional use should be protected;
- licensing policies should be communicated clearly;
- privacy and confidentiality should be respected throughout investigative processes; and
- continuous improvement should guide the ongoing development of anti-piracy practices.

No technical safeguard, contractual provision, or legal remedy can eliminate unauthorized distribution entirely. Nevertheless, a comprehensive licensing framework—supported by responsible customers, effective operational procedures, appropriate technical safeguards, and proportionate enforcement—provides the strongest practical protection for the long-term sustainability of the Engineering Handbook Series.

This Part should therefore be interpreted and applied in conjunction with every other Part of the Publishing, Copyright & Licensing Manual, ensuring that copyright protection, licensing administration, customer trust, and professional publishing standards operate as a unified and coherent system.

### Decision Summary

This Part establishes the official anti-piracy and enforcement strategy for the Engineering Handbook Series. It defines the principles, operational procedures, and enforcement framework governing the prevention, investigation, and response to unauthorized distribution while preserving the rights of legitimate license holders.

The following decisions form the authoritative policy of this Part.

#### Policy Decisions

#### Anti-Piracy Philosophy

- Prevention shall be prioritized over enforcement wherever reasonably practicable.
- Customer education and clear licensing documentation are integral components of copyright protection.
- Enforcement shall remain fair, proportionate, evidence-based, and consistently applied.
- Legitimate educational and professional use shall not be unnecessarily restricted.

#### Definition of Piracy

- Piracy consists of unauthorized reproduction, distribution, commercial exploitation, or systematic sharing beyond the scope of the applicable license.
- Not every copyright dispute or license violation automatically constitutes piracy.
- Good-faith errors, technical incidents, and credential compromises shall be assessed independently before enforcement decisions are made.

#### Threat Classification

The publisher recognizes multiple categories of piracy risk, including:

- casual sharing;
- mass redistribution;
- commercial piracy;
- institutional under-licensing;
- account sharing;
- credential compromise;
- watermark removal;
- content cloning;
- counterfeit editions; and
- insider leaks.

Each category requires proportionate investigative and operational responses.

#### Layered Protection Model

The anti-piracy framework consists of multiple complementary protection layers, including:

- clear licensing;
- license identity;
- personalized watermarking;
- controlled distribution;
- audit records;
- discovery procedures;
- documented investigations; and
- proportionate enforcement.

No individual safeguard shall be considered sufficient in isolation.

#### Investigation Principles

Investigations shall:

- rely upon credible evidence;
- preserve relevant records;
- document material findings;
- consider alternative explanations;
- remain proportionate to the seriousness of the incident; and
- respect applicable privacy obligations.

Reports alone do not establish liability.

#### Corrective Actions

Where appropriate, voluntary compliance and corrective measures should be considered before more severe enforcement action.

Corrective measures may include:

- removal of unauthorized copies;
- license correction or expansion;
- security improvements;
- credential replacement; and
- other reasonable remedial actions.

#### Escalation Framework

Enforcement follows a graduated model consisting of:

1. Educational guidance;
2. Formal compliance notice;
3. Administrative license restrictions;
4. License termination; and
5. Legal enforcement.

Serious commercial or intentional piracy may justify immediate escalation without progressing through every intermediate level.

#### Commercial Piracy

Commercial piracy represents one of the highest enforcement priorities.

The publisher may utilize technical, contractual, administrative, and legal remedies where credible evidence demonstrates deliberate commercial exploitation of protected handbook publications.

#### International Enforcement

Cross-border piracy shall be addressed using appropriate lawful mechanisms available within the relevant jurisdictions while considering effectiveness, proportionality, operational cost, and available evidence.

#### Privacy

Investigations shall respect applicable privacy and data-protection requirements.

Information shall be collected, accessed, retained, and disclosed only where reasonably necessary for legitimate operational or legal purposes.

#### Continuous Improvement

The anti-piracy framework shall be periodically reviewed and updated in response to:

- legal developments;
- technological change;
- operational experience;
- emerging piracy methods; and
- improvements in publishing practices.

#### Reservation of Rights

All intellectual property rights not expressly granted under the applicable license remain exclusively reserved by the publisher.

No provision of this Manual transfers ownership of handbook publications unless expressly stated in a separate written agreement.

#### Guiding Principles

This Part shall always be interpreted in accordance with the following principles:

- fairness;
- proportionality;
- evidence-based decision making;
- transparency;
- respect for legitimate license holders;
- privacy;
- continuous improvement; and
- long-term sustainability of the Engineering Handbook ecosystem.

#### Official Effect

This Decision Summary forms the authoritative operational summary of **Part VI — Anti-Piracy & Enforcement Strategy** and shall be interpreted together with the complete provisions of this Part, the applicable license agreement, and the remaining Parts of the Publishing, Copyright & Licensing Manual.

---

## PART VII - Fines, Penalties & Remedies

---

### 1. Purpose and Scope

This Part establishes the official framework governing the fines, penalties, remedies, and corrective measures that may arise from violations of the Engineering Handbook licensing framework. It defines the consequences that may follow after a breach of the applicable license agreement, copyright infringement, contractual non-compliance, or other unauthorized activities have been identified and appropriately verified.

The primary objective of this Part is **not** to punish individuals or organizations. Instead, it seeks to promote lawful use of the Engineering Handbook Series, encourage voluntary compliance, protect the publisher's intellectual property, preserve the rights of legitimate license holders, and ensure that enforcement actions remain fair, proportionate, transparent, and legally defensible.

This Part shall always be interpreted together with the preceding Parts of the **Publishing, Copyright & Licensing Manual**, particularly those governing licensing, copyright ownership, anti-piracy measures, compliance procedures, investigations, and enforcement strategy. The remedies described herein complement those Parts and shall not be interpreted in isolation.

The provisions contained within this Part apply to all licensed customers, individual users, educational institutions, commercial organizations, government entities, distributors, resellers, contributors, contractors, and any other party whose activities are governed by the Engineering Handbook licensing framework or applicable contractual agreements.

For the purposes of this Manual, the terms **fine**, **penalty**, and **remedy** have distinct meanings and shall not be regarded as interchangeable.

#### Fine

A **fine** refers to a monetary consequence imposed only where expressly permitted under applicable law or the governing contractual agreement. Nothing within this Manual shall be interpreted as granting the publisher governmental authority to impose statutory fines or criminal sanctions.

#### Penalty

A **penalty** refers to contractual or administrative consequences resulting from a breach of the applicable license agreement or related obligations. Penalties may include license suspension, account restrictions, termination of access, withdrawal of privileges, additional compliance requirements, or other measures expressly authorized by the governing license.

#### Remedy

A **remedy** refers to any lawful action available to restore compliance, protect intellectual property, compensate for losses, enforce contractual rights, or otherwise resolve violations. Remedies may include contractual remedies, civil remedies, equitable relief, negotiated settlements, corrective actions, or any other measures available under applicable law.

The framework established by this Part recognizes that not every violation warrants identical treatment. Enforcement decisions should always consider:

- the nature of the conduct;
- the seriousness of the violation;
- the intent of the responsible party;
- the scale of the infringement;
- the level of cooperation provided during any investigation;
- previous compliance history; and
- any mitigating or aggravating circumstances.

Accordingly, remedies should remain proportionate to the verified violation rather than being imposed automatically or uniformly. Minor administrative errors, good-faith misunderstandings, technical incidents, and isolated accidental breaches should ordinarily be addressed through corrective measures before more severe consequences are considered, provided that such an approach remains appropriate under the circumstances.

Conversely, deliberate copyright infringement, commercial piracy, systematic unauthorized distribution, counterfeiting, fraudulent conduct, repeated contractual breaches, and intentional attempts to undermine the licensing framework may justify substantially stronger contractual, administrative, technical, or legal responses.

Nothing contained within this Part shall be interpreted as limiting any statutory rights, contractual rights, equitable remedies, or legal protections available to the publisher under applicable law. Likewise, nothing in this Part creates additional legal rights for unauthorized users beyond those established by applicable legislation or the governing license agreement.

This Part does not establish criminal liability, determine criminal penalties, or replace the authority of courts, regulatory authorities, or governmental agencies. Questions relating to criminal responsibility remain exclusively within the jurisdiction of the competent legal authorities in accordance with applicable law.

The provisions contained in this Part are intended to provide a consistent, transparent, and predictable framework for determining appropriate consequences following verified violations while maintaining fairness, protecting legitimate educational use, encouraging voluntary compliance, and preserving the long-term sustainability of the Engineering Handbook publishing ecosystem.

---

### 2. Guiding Principles

The remedies and penalties established within this Part shall be administered in accordance with a consistent set of guiding principles intended to ensure fairness, proportionality, legal compliance, and the long-term integrity of the Engineering Handbook licensing framework. These principles govern the interpretation and application of every remedy described throughout this Part and shall be considered before any enforcement decision is made.

The publisher recognizes that violations may arise under widely differing circumstances. Consequently, no single remedy or penalty is appropriate for every situation. Each verified violation shall be evaluated individually, taking into account the available evidence, the surrounding circumstances, the seriousness of the conduct, the interests of legitimate license holders, and the objectives of the licensing framework.

The following principles shall guide all decisions relating to fines, penalties, corrective actions, settlements, and legal remedies.

#### Proportionality

Any remedy imposed shall be proportionate to the nature and seriousness of the verified violation. Minor administrative errors should not ordinarily result in severe contractual consequences, while deliberate commercial infringement or repeated misconduct may justify significantly stronger responses.

#### Evidence-Based Decision Making

No financial consequence, contractual penalty, or legal remedy shall be imposed solely on suspicion, allegation, or unverified reports. Decisions shall be supported by credible evidence obtained through lawful investigative procedures consistent with this Manual.

#### Fairness

Individuals and organizations shall be treated fairly and consistently throughout the enforcement process. Comparable violations should generally receive comparable responses unless material differences justify a different outcome.

#### Good Faith

Where a violation results from an honest mistake, misunderstanding, technical failure, or other good-faith circumstances, the publisher should, where reasonably appropriate, prioritize education and corrective action before imposing more severe contractual consequences.

#### Consistency

The publisher shall seek to apply policies consistently across comparable situations in order to promote predictability, transparency, and confidence in the licensing framework. Consistency does not require identical outcomes where the surrounding circumstances materially differ.

#### Voluntary Compliance

The licensing framework encourages voluntary compliance wherever reasonably practicable. Corrective measures, cooperative resolution, and negotiated settlements should be considered before pursuing more significant enforcement measures when such an approach adequately protects the publisher's legitimate interests.

#### Protection of Intellectual Property

Every remedy available under this Part ultimately serves the broader objective of protecting copyrighted works, preserving the value of original educational content, safeguarding the rights of legitimate license holders, and maintaining the sustainability of the Engineering Handbook Series.

#### Respect for Legitimate License Holders

Enforcement activities shall minimize unnecessary disruption to customers who have complied with their licensing obligations. Remedies should, wherever reasonably possible, distinguish between authorized users acting lawfully and parties engaged in unauthorized conduct.

#### Transparency

The publisher shall communicate the basis of enforcement decisions with reasonable clarity whenever appropriate. Individuals and organizations subject to contractual penalties should, where practicable, understand the nature of the verified violation and the reasons supporting the selected remedy.

#### Legal Compliance

Nothing contained within this Part authorizes any remedy that would be contrary to applicable law. All contractual, administrative, financial, and legal actions shall remain subject to the laws governing the applicable license agreement and the jurisdiction in which enforcement is pursued.

#### Least Necessary Intervention

Where multiple lawful remedies are available, consideration shall be given to selecting the least restrictive measure capable of achieving compliance, protecting intellectual property, and preventing further violations. Escalation to more severe remedies should generally occur only where lesser measures prove inadequate or where the seriousness of the conduct justifies an immediate stronger response.

#### No Automatic Penalties

The occurrence of a license violation does not automatically require the imposition of financial penalties, license termination, or legal proceedings. The publisher retains discretion to determine the most appropriate response after considering all relevant facts, contractual obligations, and applicable legal requirements.

Collectively, these guiding principles establish the foundation upon which every fine, penalty, contractual consequence, settlement, corrective measure, and legal remedy described throughout this Part shall be interpreted and applied.

---

### 3. Types of Violations

The Engineering Handbook licensing framework recognizes that not all violations are of equal seriousness. The nature of a violation, the intent of the responsible party, the scale of the conduct, the resulting impact, and the surrounding circumstances shall all be considered before determining an appropriate remedy or penalty.

Accordingly, violations are classified into different categories to promote consistency, fairness, and proportionality throughout the enforcement process. These classifications are intended as guidance rather than rigid rules. The publisher may consider additional factors where appropriate and may classify conduct according to its overall substance rather than its description alone.

The following categories represent the principal types of violations that may arise under the Engineering Handbook licensing framework.

#### 3.1 Minor Administrative Violations

Minor administrative violations are non-malicious breaches that generally result from oversight, misunderstanding, clerical errors, or isolated failures to comply with procedural requirements.

Examples include:

- Providing incomplete registration information.
- Failing to update licensing records.
- Accidental use beyond the permitted device limit that is promptly corrected.
- Delayed license renewal where no intentional misuse occurred.
- Isolated reporting errors.
- Other comparable administrative non-compliance.

Such violations should ordinarily be addressed through education, clarification, correction, or administrative guidance rather than severe contractual or financial consequences.

#### 3.2 License Misuse

License misuse occurs when a licensed customer uses the handbook in a manner that exceeds the rights granted by the applicable license without necessarily engaging in deliberate piracy.

Examples include:

- Exceeding the permitted number of licensed users.
- Using a personal license for organizational purposes.
- Sharing licensed materials within an unauthorized department.
- Transferring licenses without authorization.
- Allowing access outside the licensed scope.
- Using handbook content for purposes not permitted by the applicable agreement.

Depending upon the seriousness and duration of the misuse, the publisher may require corrective licensing, additional license purchases, administrative restrictions, or other appropriate contractual remedies.

#### 3.3 Unauthorized Sharing

Unauthorized sharing involves distributing handbook content beyond the permissions granted by the applicable license.

Examples include:

- Sending complete handbook files to unauthorized individuals.
- Uploading licensed publications to public websites.
- Sharing protected content through cloud storage services.
- Distributing copies through messaging platforms.
- Posting handbook files on online forums.
- Making licensed content publicly accessible without authorization.

The seriousness of unauthorized sharing generally increases according to the scale of distribution, the accessibility of the material, and the resulting impact upon the publisher's intellectual property rights.

#### 3.4 Institutional Non-Compliance

Institutional violations arise when an educational institution, business, government organization, or other entity fails to comply with the obligations established under its applicable licensing agreement.

Examples include:

- Exceeding licensed seat allocations.
- Permitting unauthorized departments to use licensed content.
- Deploying handbook materials beyond the licensed campus or organization.
- Failing to maintain required licensing records.
- Systematic under-licensing.
- Other organizational failures to comply with licensing requirements.

Institutional matters should ordinarily prioritize cooperative resolution, license reconciliation, and administrative compliance before more significant enforcement measures are considered.

#### 3.5 Commercial Piracy

Commercial piracy represents one of the most serious forms of violation under the Engineering Handbook licensing framework.

Examples include:

- Selling unauthorized copies.
- Operating commercial piracy websites.
- Reproducing publications for profit.
- Offering counterfeit editions.
- Charging for unauthorized digital downloads.
- Operating subscription services using unauthorized handbook content.
- Any other activity intended to obtain commercial benefit through unauthorized exploitation of copyrighted material.

Commercial piracy may justify immediate contractual termination, civil proceedings, injunctive relief, recovery of damages, or any other lawful remedy available under applicable law.

#### 3.6 Fraudulent Conduct

Fraud involves intentional deception designed to obtain unauthorized access, financial benefit, licensing privileges, or other advantages.

Examples include:

- Submitting false licensing information.
- Impersonating authorized customers.
- Using fraudulent educational credentials.
- Falsifying institutional affiliations.
- Creating multiple accounts to circumvent licensing restrictions.
- Intentionally concealing unauthorized distribution.
- Providing false information during compliance investigations.

Fraudulent conduct may significantly increase the seriousness of any associated violation.

#### 3.7 Counterfeiting

Counterfeiting involves producing or distributing publications that falsely appear to be authentic Engineering Handbook editions.

Examples include:

- Reproducing handbook covers and branding.
- Copying publisher identifiers.
- Removing or replacing copyright notices.
- Creating fake licensed editions.
- Altering publication information to disguise unauthorized copies.
- Distributing counterfeit digital or printed versions intended to appear genuine.

Counterfeiting constitutes a serious violation of both copyright and publisher identity and may warrant the strongest contractual and legal remedies available.

#### 3.8 Repeat Violations

A repeat violation occurs when an individual or organization continues to engage in non-compliant conduct after receiving previous guidance, warnings, corrective opportunities, or enforcement actions.

Repeated misconduct may demonstrate an unwillingness to comply with licensing obligations and may justify progressively stronger contractual, administrative, financial, or legal responses.

#### 3.9 Aggravated Violations

Certain circumstances may substantially increase the seriousness of an otherwise ordinary violation.

Examples include:

- Deliberate concealment of misconduct.
- Destruction of evidence.
- Removal of watermarking or license identifiers.
- Obstruction of investigations.
- Large-scale unauthorized distribution.
- Organized infringement.
- Repeated intentional misconduct.
- Conduct causing significant commercial harm to the publisher.

Aggravating circumstances may justify escalation to more severe remedies than would ordinarily apply.

#### 3.10 Good-Faith Violations

Not every breach results from intentional misconduct. Certain violations may occur despite reasonable efforts to comply with licensing obligations.

Examples include:

- Genuine misunderstanding of license terms.
- Technical failures.
- Accidental administrative errors.
- Isolated compliance mistakes.
- Unauthorized access resulting from compromised credentials.
- Promptly corrected incidents.
- Other comparable good-faith circumstances.

Where credible evidence demonstrates that a violation occurred without dishonest intent and has been addressed responsibly, the publisher should ordinarily consider education, corrective action, or negotiated resolution before pursuing more severe remedies, provided such an approach adequately protects the publisher's legitimate interests.

These classifications provide the foundation for determining the appropriate fines, penalties, contractual consequences, corrective measures, settlements, and legal remedies described throughout the remaining provisions of this Part.

---

### 4. Administrative Penalties

Administrative penalties are non-criminal, non-judicial measures that the publisher may impose to address verified violations of the Engineering Handbook licensing framework. These measures are intended to restore compliance, protect intellectual property, prevent further unauthorized activity, and encourage responsible use of licensed publications.

Administrative penalties are contractual in nature and arise from the applicable license agreement rather than from statutory criminal authority. Unless otherwise required by applicable law or expressly provided in the governing agreement, administrative penalties should generally be applied progressively and proportionately, taking into account the seriousness of the verified violation and the surrounding circumstances.

The publisher retains discretion to determine the most appropriate administrative response based upon the available evidence, the compliance history of the responsible party, the level of cooperation provided during any investigation, and the need to protect the integrity of the licensing ecosystem.

Administrative penalties may include one or more of the following measures.

#### 4.1 Educational Warning

For minor or first-time violations arising from good-faith mistakes or administrative oversight, the publisher may issue an educational warning explaining the applicable licensing requirements and identifying the corrective actions expected from the license holder.

Educational warnings are intended to promote voluntary compliance rather than punishment and should ordinarily be considered before stronger contractual measures where appropriate.

#### 4.2 Formal Compliance Notice

Where a verified violation requires corrective action, the publisher may issue a formal compliance notice describing:

- The nature of the verified violation.
- The applicable licensing obligations.
- The corrective actions required.
- Any applicable compliance deadlines.
- The potential consequences of continued non-compliance.

Failure to respond appropriately to a formal compliance notice may result in further administrative or contractual action.

#### 4.3 Temporary Account Restrictions

The publisher may temporarily restrict access to licensed services or digital resources while a compliance issue is being investigated or corrected.

Temporary restrictions should be limited to the extent reasonably necessary to protect intellectual property or prevent ongoing unauthorized use and should not remain in effect longer than reasonably justified by the circumstances.

#### 4.4 Suspension of License Privileges

Where continued use of the licensed materials presents a material risk of further violations, the publisher may temporarily suspend some or all license privileges until the identified compliance issues have been resolved.

License suspension does not transfer ownership of the licensed materials and does not relieve the license holder of any continuing contractual obligations.

#### 4.5 Download and Distribution Restrictions

The publisher may temporarily limit the ability to download, access, synchronize, or distribute licensed publications where such measures are reasonably necessary to prevent additional unauthorized dissemination.

Such restrictions should be proportionate to the verified risk and removed once compliance has been satisfactorily restored where appropriate.

#### 4.6 Mandatory Corrective Measures

Instead of immediately imposing more severe consequences, the publisher may require reasonable corrective actions, including:

- Updating licensing records.
- Reconciling licensed user counts.
- Purchasing additional licenses where required.
- Removing unauthorized copies.
- Improving account security.
- Replacing compromised credentials.
- Completing administrative verification procedures.
- Implementing other measures necessary to restore compliance.

Successful completion of corrective measures may be considered when determining whether additional administrative action is necessary.

#### 4.7 License Suspension

Where significant contractual violations have been verified, the publisher may suspend the applicable license in accordance with its terms.

During suspension, access to some or all licensed publications or services may be limited until the publisher determines that the applicable compliance requirements have been satisfied or the matter has otherwise been resolved.

#### 4.8 License Termination

License termination represents one of the most serious administrative consequences available under the licensing framework.

Termination may be considered where:

- Deliberate contractual breaches have occurred.
- Commercial piracy has been verified.
- Repeated violations demonstrate persistent non-compliance.
- Fraudulent conduct materially affects the licensing relationship.
- Corrective opportunities have been exhausted.
- Continued licensing would create an unreasonable risk to the publisher's intellectual property.

Termination shall be carried out only in accordance with the applicable license agreement and relevant legal requirements.

#### 4.9 Institutional Administrative Measures

Where the responsible party is an institution or organization, the publisher may implement additional administrative measures, including:

- Institutional compliance reviews.
- Temporary suspension of organizational access.
- License reconciliation.
- Enterprise licensing adjustments.
- Administrative audits.
- Other reasonable contractual measures appropriate to the circumstances.

Institutional actions should ordinarily seek to restore organizational compliance while minimizing unnecessary disruption to legitimate authorized users.

Administrative penalties established under this Section are intended to promote compliance, preserve the integrity of the Engineering Handbook licensing framework, and encourage responsible use of licensed publications. They should always be interpreted consistently with the guiding principles established throughout this Part and should not be regarded as punitive measures beyond the contractual rights provided under the applicable licensing agreement.

---

### 5. Financial Remedies

Financial remedies are contractual or civil mechanisms intended to compensate for losses, recover unpaid licensing obligations, restore compliance, and protect the economic value of the Engineering Handbook Series. They are not intended to function as criminal sanctions or government-imposed fines and shall be interpreted consistently with applicable law and the governing license agreement.

Where appropriate, financial remedies should seek to place the affected parties in the position they would reasonably have occupied had the violation not occurred. The selection of any financial remedy shall consider the seriousness of the verified violation, the extent of the resulting harm, the conduct of the responsible party, any previous compliance history, and the availability of alternative corrective measures.

Financial remedies may include one or more of the following.

#### 5.1 Recovery of Outstanding License Fees

Where licensed materials have been used beyond the scope of the applicable agreement without payment of the required licensing fees, the publisher may seek recovery of the outstanding amounts that would have been payable under the appropriate license.

Recovery of unpaid licensing obligations should reflect the applicable pricing structure in effect during the relevant period unless otherwise agreed between the parties.

#### 5.2 Payment for Additional Licensing

Where unauthorized use results from insufficient licensing rather than deliberate piracy, the publisher may require the purchase of additional licenses necessary to bring the organization or individual into compliance.

Examples include:

- Additional user licenses.
- Institutional seat expansions.
- Enterprise licensing upgrades.
- Departmental licensing adjustments.
- Other licensing modifications appropriate to the verified usage.

Whenever reasonably practicable, corrective licensing should be considered before more severe financial consequences.

#### 5.3 Recovery of Contractual Damages

Where a breach of the applicable license agreement results in measurable financial loss, the publisher may pursue recovery of contractual damages to the extent permitted under applicable law and the governing agreement.

Such damages may include direct losses arising from the verified contractual breach but shall not exceed the limitations imposed by applicable law or the relevant contractual provisions.

#### 5.4 Recovery of Investigation Costs

Where permitted by applicable law or the governing agreement, the publisher may seek recovery of reasonable costs directly associated with investigating significant or deliberate violations.

Recoverable costs may include expenses reasonably incurred for:

- Compliance investigations.
- Technical analysis.
- Digital forensic services.
- Evidence preservation.
- External professional services.
- Other necessary investigative activities.

Only reasonable and properly documented costs should be considered for recovery.

#### 5.5 Recovery Following Commercial Piracy

Commercial piracy may cause substantial economic harm through unauthorized reproduction, distribution, or sale of copyrighted publications.

Where commercial piracy has been verified, the publisher may pursue all lawful financial remedies available, including:

- Recovery of unpaid licensing revenue.
- Compensation for proven financial losses.
- Civil damages where permitted by law.
- Recovery of profits obtained through unauthorized commercial exploitation.
- Other monetary remedies authorized by applicable legislation.

The availability and scope of these remedies shall always remain subject to the governing jurisdiction.

#### 5.6 Settlement Payments

Rather than pursuing prolonged disputes, the publisher and the responsible party may voluntarily negotiate financial settlement arrangements intended to resolve licensing issues efficiently.

Settlement agreements may include:

- Payment of outstanding license fees.
- Purchase of appropriate licenses.
- Removal of unauthorized copies.
- Compliance commitments.
- Agreed compensation.
- Other mutually acceptable financial terms.

A negotiated settlement does not necessarily constitute an admission of legal liability unless expressly stated within the settlement agreement.

#### 5.7 Interest and Late Payment

Where payment obligations arise under a license agreement, settlement, or other contractual arrangement, interest or late payment charges may apply only where expressly authorized by the applicable agreement or governing law.

Any such charges shall be calculated in accordance with the applicable contractual provisions and relevant legal requirements.

#### 5.8 Limitation of Financial Remedies

Nothing contained within this Section authorizes unlimited financial recovery.

All financial remedies shall remain subject to:

- Applicable law.
- The governing license agreement.
- Contractual limitations of liability.
- Judicial oversight where required.
- Principles of proportionality and fairness.
- Any other legal restrictions applicable within the relevant jurisdiction.

Financial remedies should not be imposed arbitrarily or for punitive purposes where corrective licensing or voluntary compliance adequately protects the publisher's legitimate interests.

The financial remedies described throughout this Section are intended to restore compliance, compensate for demonstrable losses where appropriate, protect the economic sustainability of the Engineering Handbook Series, and preserve the rights of legitimate license holders while remaining fully consistent with applicable contractual and legal requirements.

---

### 6. Civil Remedies

Civil remedies are lawful legal mechanisms that may be available to the publisher for the protection and enforcement of its intellectual property rights, contractual interests, and other legally recognized rights. These remedies are pursued through appropriate civil legal processes and shall be governed by the applicable laws of the relevant jurisdiction.

Nothing contained within this Section creates new legal rights or expands the remedies otherwise available under applicable law. Instead, this Section identifies the principal civil remedies that may be available where significant or unresolved violations have occurred.

Civil remedies should ordinarily be considered where administrative measures, voluntary compliance, negotiated settlements, or contractual remedies have proven insufficient or where the seriousness of the violation justifies immediate legal action.

#### 6.1 Injunctive Relief

Where unauthorized activities are ongoing or there is a substantial risk of continued infringement, the publisher may seek injunctive relief from a court of competent jurisdiction.

Depending upon applicable law, injunctive relief may require the responsible party to:

- Cease unauthorized distribution.
- Stop further reproduction of copyrighted materials.
- Remove infringing publications from public access.
- Prevent additional unauthorized use.
- Preserve relevant evidence pending legal proceedings.
- Comply with other lawful court-ordered obligations.

The availability and scope of injunctive relief shall be determined exclusively by the competent court.

#### 6.2 Recovery of Civil Damages

Where legally recoverable financial loss has resulted from copyright infringement, breach of contract, or other civil wrongdoing, the publisher may seek recovery of civil damages as permitted by applicable law.

Recoverable damages may include:

- Proven financial losses.
- Loss of licensing revenue.
- Other compensable economic harm recognized by law.

The assessment of damages shall remain subject to judicial determination and the governing legal framework.

#### 6.3 Recovery of Profits

Where a responsible party has obtained commercial benefit through unauthorized exploitation of the Engineering Handbook Series, the publisher may seek recovery of profits to the extent permitted by applicable law.

Recovery of profits shall be determined according to the applicable legal standards and any available evidence regarding unauthorized commercial gain.

#### 6.4 Copyright Enforcement Proceedings

Where significant copyright infringement has occurred, the publisher may initiate appropriate civil copyright proceedings to enforce its intellectual property rights.

Such proceedings may seek one or more lawful remedies, including:

- Injunctive relief.
- Civil damages.
- Recovery of profits.
- Delivery or destruction of infringing copies where authorized by law.
- Declaratory relief.
- Other remedies recognized under applicable copyright legislation.

#### 6.5 Declaratory Relief

Where uncertainty exists regarding the rights, obligations, or interpretation of the applicable licensing agreement, the publisher may seek declaratory relief from a competent court where such relief is available.

Declaratory judgments may clarify legal rights and obligations without necessarily awarding monetary damages or imposing additional penalties.

#### 6.6 Recovery of Legal Costs

Where authorized by applicable law or ordered by a competent court, the publisher may seek recovery of reasonable legal costs incurred in pursuing civil enforcement proceedings.

Recoverable costs shall remain subject to:

- Applicable procedural rules.
- Judicial discretion.
- Statutory limitations.
- Any contractual provisions governing cost recovery.

Nothing in this Section guarantees recovery of legal expenses.

#### 6.7 Court-Ordered Corrective Measures

A court of competent jurisdiction may order corrective measures where permitted under applicable law.

Such measures may include:

- Removal of infringing materials.
- Delivery or destruction of unauthorized copies.
- Correction of licensing records.
- Compliance with applicable court orders.
- Other equitable relief recognized under the governing legal framework.

The publisher shall comply with all applicable judicial procedures when seeking such remedies.

#### 6.8 Limitation of Civil Remedies

The civil remedies described throughout this Section are subject to the laws of the applicable jurisdiction and shall not be interpreted as automatic consequences of every violation.

Before initiating civil proceedings, the publisher may consider:

- The seriousness of the violation.
- The available evidence.
- Previous compliance efforts.
- Opportunities for negotiated settlement.
- The proportionality of legal action.
- The likely effectiveness of alternative remedies.

Nothing in this Manual obligates the publisher to pursue civil litigation in every case. The publisher retains discretion, subject to applicable law, to resolve disputes through administrative action, contractual remedies, negotiated settlements, alternative dispute resolution, or other lawful means where such approaches adequately protect its legitimate interests.

The civil remedies established under this Section are intended to provide lawful mechanisms for protecting copyrighted works, enforcing contractual rights, recovering legally recognized losses, and preserving the integrity of the Engineering Handbook licensing framework while ensuring full compliance with applicable legal requirements.

---

### 7. Contractual Remedies

Contractual remedies are measures arising directly from the rights and obligations established under the applicable Engineering Handbook license agreement or any related contractual arrangement. These remedies are intended to enforce compliance with contractual obligations, protect the publisher's intellectual property, and preserve the integrity of the licensing framework without relying upon criminal sanctions.

The availability of any contractual remedy depends upon the specific terms of the governing agreement, applicable law, and the verified facts of the particular case. Nothing contained within this Section shall be interpreted as expanding contractual rights beyond those lawfully established by the applicable agreement.

Where reasonably practicable, contractual remedies should encourage voluntary compliance and restoration of the licensing relationship before more severe enforcement measures are pursued.

#### 7.1 Notice of Breach

Where the publisher determines that a contractual obligation has been violated, it may issue a written notice of breach identifying:

- The relevant contractual provision.
- The nature of the verified breach.
- The corrective actions required.
- The applicable response period, where appropriate.
- The potential contractual consequences of continued non-compliance.

Issuing a notice of breach does not waive any contractual rights or legal remedies otherwise available to the publisher.

#### 7.2 Opportunity to Cure

Where permitted by the applicable license agreement and appropriate under the circumstances, the publisher may provide the responsible party with a reasonable opportunity to correct the identified breach.

Corrective actions may include:

- Purchasing the appropriate license.
- Removing unauthorized copies.
- Updating licensing records.
- Correcting administrative deficiencies.
- Strengthening account security.
- Restoring compliance with contractual requirements.

The availability of an opportunity to cure shall depend upon the seriousness of the violation and is not required in every circumstance.

#### 7.3 Suspension of Contractual Rights

Pending resolution of a verified contractual breach, the publisher may temporarily suspend some or all contractual rights granted under the applicable license agreement.

Suspension may include temporary restrictions relating to:

- Access to licensed publications.
- Download privileges.
- Product updates.
- Support services.
- Enterprise management features.
- Other contractual benefits provided under the applicable license.

Suspension should remain proportionate to the verified breach and should not extend beyond what is reasonably necessary to protect the publisher's legitimate interests.

#### 7.4 Termination of License Agreement

Where a material contractual breach has occurred, the publisher may terminate the applicable license agreement in accordance with its terms and applicable law.

Termination may be appropriate where:

- Commercial piracy has been verified.
- Fraudulent conduct materially affects the licensing relationship.
- Serious copyright infringement has occurred.
- Repeated contractual breaches remain unresolved.
- Corrective opportunities have been exhausted.
- Continued licensing presents an unreasonable risk to the publisher's intellectual property.

Termination shall not affect any contractual rights or legal remedies that survive termination under the governing agreement.

#### 7.5 Recovery of Contractual Obligations

Termination or suspension of a license does not automatically release the responsible party from outstanding contractual obligations.

Subject to the applicable agreement and governing law, the publisher may seek fulfillment of obligations including:

- Outstanding license fees.
- Agreed settlement payments.
- Previously accrued contractual obligations.
- Other financial commitments arising before termination.

The scope of any recovery shall remain subject to the governing contractual provisions.

#### 7.6 Reservation of Rights

The publisher's decision to delay enforcement, negotiate a settlement, grant additional time for compliance, or temporarily refrain from exercising a contractual remedy shall not constitute a waiver of any contractual right unless expressly stated in writing.

No previous course of conduct shall prevent the publisher from exercising any contractual remedy available under the applicable agreement in response to subsequent verified violations.

#### 7.7 Relationship with Other Remedies

The contractual remedies described throughout this Section are intended to complement, rather than replace, other lawful remedies available under this Manual or applicable law.

Where appropriate, contractual remedies may be pursued together with:

- Administrative penalties.
- Financial remedies.
- Civil remedies.
- Negotiated settlements.
- Alternative dispute resolution procedures.
- Other lawful enforcement measures.

The selection of any combination of remedies shall remain subject to the governing license agreement, applicable law, and the principles of proportionality, fairness, and good-faith enforcement established throughout this Part.

The contractual remedies established under this Section provide the primary contractual mechanisms through which the publisher may restore compliance, enforce licensing obligations, protect copyrighted works, and maintain the integrity of the Engineering Handbook licensing framework while preserving flexibility for fair and proportionate resolution of contractual disputes.

---

### 8. Institutional Remedies

Institutional remedies are measures intended to address licensing violations committed by organizations rather than individual users. Educational institutions, universities, colleges, training centers, businesses, government agencies, research organizations, libraries, and other entities often operate under organizational licensing arrangements that differ from individual licenses. Accordingly, certain remedies may be applied at the institutional level to restore compliance while minimizing unnecessary disruption to legitimate authorized users.

The primary objective of institutional remedies is to correct organizational non-compliance, protect intellectual property, and encourage responsible institutional governance rather than to impose punitive consequences upon individual employees, students, or authorized users acting in good faith.

Institutional remedies shall be applied proportionately, taking into account the nature of the verified violation, the size of the organization, the scope of the licensing arrangement, previous compliance history, and the level of cooperation provided during any compliance review or investigation.

#### 8.1 Institutional Compliance Review

Where organizational licensing concerns arise, the publisher may conduct a compliance review to determine whether the institution is operating within the scope of its applicable license agreement.

A compliance review may examine matters including:

- Licensed user counts.
- Institutional access records.
- Departmental licensing allocations.
- Distribution practices.
- Administrative controls.
- Other information reasonably necessary to verify licensing compliance.

Compliance reviews should be conducted in a fair, reasonable, and proportionate manner while respecting applicable legal and contractual obligations.

#### 8.2 License Reconciliation

Where discrepancies exist between licensed usage and actual usage, the publisher may require license reconciliation.

License reconciliation may involve:

- Updating institutional licensing records.
- Correcting user allocations.
- Purchasing additional licenses.
- Removing unauthorized users.
- Revising organizational licensing arrangements.
- Other measures necessary to restore contractual compliance.

Whenever reasonably practicable, reconciliation should be pursued before more severe enforcement measures.

#### 8.3 Organizational Corrective Action Plan

Where systemic compliance deficiencies have been identified, the publisher may request that the institution prepare and implement a corrective action plan.

Such a plan may include:

- Internal compliance procedures.
- License management improvements.
- Staff training.
- Administrative oversight measures.
- Security enhancements.
- Timelines for achieving full compliance.

Successful implementation of a corrective action plan may be considered when determining whether additional enforcement measures are necessary.

#### 8.4 Temporary Institutional Restrictions

Pending resolution of significant compliance concerns, the publisher may temporarily restrict certain organizational licensing privileges where reasonably necessary to prevent continued unauthorized use.

Restrictions may include:

- Suspension of additional downloads.
- Temporary limitation of administrative functions.
- Restrictions on new user registrations.
- Suspension of enterprise management features.
- Other proportionate contractual limitations.

Such restrictions should remain limited to the extent necessary to protect the publisher's legitimate interests.

#### 8.5 Institutional License Suspension

Where serious or repeated organizational violations have been verified, the publisher may temporarily suspend the institution's license in accordance with the applicable agreement.

License suspension should ordinarily be considered only after reasonable opportunities for voluntary compliance have been provided, unless immediate action is justified by the seriousness of the violation.

#### 8.6 Institutional License Termination

Where an institution has engaged in persistent, deliberate, or materially significant violations of its licensing obligations, the publisher may terminate the applicable institutional license in accordance with its contractual terms and applicable law.

Termination may be considered where:

- Commercial misuse is widespread.
- Organizational piracy has been verified.
- Fraudulent licensing practices have occurred.
- Repeated compliance failures remain unresolved.
- Corrective opportunities have been exhausted.
- Continued licensing presents an unreasonable risk to the publisher's intellectual property.

Termination shall not affect any contractual obligations or legal rights that survive termination under the applicable agreement.

#### 8.7 Cooperative Resolution

The publisher recognizes that many institutional licensing issues arise from administrative complexity rather than intentional misconduct.

Accordingly, where appropriate, the publisher may seek cooperative resolution through:

- Administrative consultation.
- Licensing guidance.
- Compliance meetings.
- Negotiated licensing adjustments.
- Voluntary corrective actions.
- Settlement discussions.
- Other mutually agreed compliance measures.

Cooperative resolution should ordinarily be preferred where it adequately protects the publisher's legitimate interests and restores organizational compliance.

#### 8.8 Protection of Legitimate Users

Institutional enforcement measures should, wherever reasonably practicable, minimize unnecessary disruption to students, educators, researchers, employees, and other authorized users who have not personally participated in the verified violation.

Where organizational remedies affect legitimate users, the publisher should seek reasonable alternatives that preserve lawful educational and professional access while ensuring that institutional non-compliance is effectively addressed.

The institutional remedies established throughout this Section are intended to encourage responsible organizational governance, strengthen licensing compliance, protect copyrighted educational materials, and maintain long-term partnerships with institutions while preserving the integrity of the Engineering Handbook licensing framework.

---

### 9. Repeat Violations

The Engineering Handbook licensing framework recognizes that repeated non-compliance may demonstrate a greater degree of responsibility than an isolated or first-time violation. While the publisher remains committed to education, voluntary compliance, and corrective action wherever reasonably practicable, repeated violations may indicate that previous enforcement measures have been ineffective or that the responsible party is unwilling to comply with applicable licensing obligations.

Accordingly, repeat violations may justify progressively stronger administrative, contractual, financial, or legal responses consistent with the principles established throughout this Part.

A repeat violation does not automatically require the maximum available penalty. Each subsequent incident shall continue to be evaluated individually, taking into account the surrounding circumstances, the seriousness of the conduct, and the overall compliance history of the responsible party.

#### 9.1 Definition of a Repeat Violation

A repeat violation occurs when an individual or organization commits one or more additional verified violations after previously receiving:

- An educational warning.
- A formal compliance notice.
- A corrective action requirement.
- An administrative penalty.
- A contractual enforcement measure.
- A negotiated settlement.
- Any other documented enforcement action relating to substantially similar conduct.

The existence of a previous violation does not by itself determine the outcome of a subsequent matter but may be considered when selecting an appropriate remedy.

#### 9.2 Progressive Enforcement

Where repeated non-compliance has been verified, the publisher may progressively increase the severity of its response where appropriate.

Progressive enforcement may include:

- Additional compliance requirements.
- Stronger administrative restrictions.
- Temporary suspension of license privileges.
- Financial recovery measures.
- Contractual enforcement.
- Civil remedies.
- Other lawful actions proportionate to the verified conduct.

Progressive enforcement should remain fair, consistent, and proportionate rather than automatic.

#### 9.3 Consideration of Compliance History

When evaluating repeat violations, the publisher may consider the overall compliance history of the responsible party, including:

- Previous warnings.
- Prior investigations.
- Earlier corrective actions.
- Historical cooperation.
- Timeliness of corrective measures.
- Resolution of earlier incidents.
- Overall pattern of compliance.

A long history of responsible compliance may weigh in favor of corrective measures, whereas persistent non-compliance may justify stronger enforcement.

#### 9.4 Distinguishing Good-Faith Recurrence

Not every repeated incident reflects intentional misconduct. A subsequent violation may arise from:

- Independent technical failures.
- Administrative oversight.
- Genuine misunderstanding of revised licensing requirements.
- Unrelated operational errors.
- Other good-faith circumstances.

Where credible evidence demonstrates that repeated incidents do not represent deliberate disregard for licensing obligations, the publisher should consider whether additional education or corrective guidance is more appropriate than immediate escalation.

#### 9.5 Persistent Non-Compliance

Persistent non-compliance refers to repeated or continuous violations despite reasonable opportunities to achieve compliance.

Examples may include:

- Repeated unauthorized sharing.
- Ongoing license misuse.
- Continuous organizational under-licensing.
- Repeated circumvention of licensing controls.
- Failure to implement agreed corrective measures.
- Continued non-compliance following previous settlements or enforcement actions.

Persistent non-compliance may justify stronger contractual, administrative, financial, or civil remedies where lesser measures have proven ineffective.

#### 9.6 Individual Assessment of Each Incident

Although previous compliance history may be relevant, each alleged violation shall continue to receive an independent assessment based upon its own facts and evidence.

The publisher shall consider:

- The seriousness of the current violation.
- The available evidence.
- The level of cooperation provided.
- Any mitigating or aggravating circumstances.
- The effectiveness of previous corrective measures.
- The objectives of achieving lawful and sustainable compliance.

The repeat violation framework established throughout this Section is intended to encourage lasting compliance, discourage repeated misconduct, and provide a consistent basis for escalating enforcement only where such escalation is justified by the verified facts and remains proportionate to the overall circumstances.

---

### 10. Aggravating Factors and Penalty Tiers

Not every violation warrants the same level of enforcement. Two incidents involving similar conduct may justify different remedies depending upon the surrounding circumstances, the intent of the responsible party, the resulting harm, and the overall compliance history. Accordingly, the publisher may consider aggravating factors when determining the appropriate administrative, contractual, financial, or civil response to a verified violation.

Aggravating factors do not automatically require the maximum available remedy, nor do they replace the need for an evidence-based assessment of each individual case. Instead, they assist in determining whether a more significant response is justified under the principles of proportionality, fairness, consistency, and legal compliance established throughout this Part.

To promote predictable and transparent enforcement, violations may be evaluated using the following indicative penalty tiers. These tiers are intended as guidance only and do not create mandatory or automatic consequences.

#### 10.1 General Aggravating Factors

The publisher may consider one or more of the following circumstances as aggravating factors:

- Deliberate or intentional misconduct.
- Commercial exploitation of copyrighted material.
- Large-scale unauthorized distribution.
- Repeat violations.
- Fraudulent conduct.
- Counterfeiting.
- Concealment of evidence.
- Circumvention of licensing controls.
- Obstruction of compliance investigations.
- Refusal to cooperate during enforcement proceedings.
- Significant financial harm to the publisher.
- Systematic organizational non-compliance.
- Any other circumstance demonstrating a heightened level of responsibility.

The presence of multiple aggravating factors may justify escalation to a higher penalty tier where appropriate.

#### 10.2 Tier I — Minor Administrative Non-Compliance

Tier I generally applies to isolated, low-risk, and good-faith violations involving little or no measurable harm.

Examples include:

- Administrative errors.
- Incomplete licensing records.
- Minor reporting deficiencies.
- Accidental procedural non-compliance.
- Promptly corrected technical mistakes.

Typical responses may include:

- Educational guidance.
- Administrative clarification.
- Compliance reminders.
- Corrective action requests.
- Formal warnings.

Financial recovery or stronger contractual measures will ordinarily not be necessary unless additional aggravating factors are present.

#### 10.3 Tier II — Moderate Licensing Violations

Tier II generally applies where verified licensing obligations have been exceeded but the conduct does not constitute deliberate commercial piracy or serious fraud.

Examples include:

- Unauthorized internal sharing.
- Exceeding licensed user limits.
- Organizational under-licensing.
- Repeated administrative deficiencies.
- Unauthorized departmental access.
- Failure to complete required corrective actions.

Typical responses may include:

- Mandatory license reconciliation.
- Purchase of additional licenses.
- Temporary administrative restrictions.
- Formal compliance notices.
- Limited suspension of licensing privileges.
- Recovery of outstanding licensing obligations where appropriate.

#### 10.4 Tier III — Serious Contractual or Copyright Violations

Tier III generally applies where significant contractual breaches or copyright violations have been verified and corrective measures alone are unlikely to provide adequate protection.

Examples include:

- Large-scale unauthorized distribution.
- Repeated license abuse.
- Commercial misuse.
- Deliberate circumvention of licensing controls.
- Fraud relating to licensing eligibility.
- Persistent organizational non-compliance.

Typical responses may include:

- Suspension of license agreements.
- Significant contractual enforcement measures.
- Financial recovery.
- Civil remedies.
- Negotiated settlements subject to appropriate conditions.
- Other lawful measures proportionate to the seriousness of the conduct.

#### 10.5 Tier IV — Exceptional or Deliberate Misconduct

Tier IV represents the most serious category of violations and generally applies where intentional misconduct causes substantial harm to the publisher or its intellectual property.

Examples include:

- Commercial piracy.
- Counterfeiting.
- Organized infringement.
- Large-scale unauthorized commercial distribution.
- Deliberate fraudulent licensing schemes.
- Persistent intentional violations despite previous enforcement actions.

Where supported by applicable law and the governing agreements, the publisher may consider:

- Immediate license termination.
- Civil litigation.
- Recovery of damages.
- Injunctive relief.
- Recovery of profits.
- Other lawful remedies appropriate to the verified circumstances.

The selection of any remedy shall remain subject to applicable legal requirements and judicial authority where necessary.

#### 10.6 Multiple Aggravating Factors

Where several aggravating factors exist simultaneously, the publisher may determine that a higher enforcement tier is appropriate than would ordinarily apply to the underlying violation.

Examples include situations involving:

- Commercial piracy combined with counterfeiting.
- Fraud together with concealment of evidence.
- Repeated violations accompanied by refusal to cooperate.
- Large-scale infringement affecting multiple institutions.

The cumulative effect of aggravating factors should be evaluated carefully to ensure that any escalation remains fair and proportionate.

#### 10.7 Exceptional Mitigating Circumstances

Even where aggravating factors are present, the publisher may consider exceptional mitigating circumstances where supported by credible evidence.

Examples may include:

- Immediate voluntary disclosure.
- Prompt cessation of the violation.
- Full cooperation during the investigation.
- Rapid implementation of corrective measures.
- Demonstrated commitment to future compliance.

Such circumstances do not eliminate responsibility but may influence the selection of an appropriate remedy.

#### 10.8 No Automatic Escalation

The penalty tiers described throughout this Section are intended to provide a structured framework for decision-making rather than mandatory enforcement rules.

Escalation from one tier to another shall always depend upon:

- The verified facts.
- Available evidence.
- Applicable contractual obligations.
- Relevant legal requirements.
- The principles established throughout this Manual.

No individual or organization shall be assigned to a higher enforcement tier solely because a previous matter exists without considering the specific circumstances of the current violation.

#### 10.9 Individual Case Assessment

Every enforcement decision shall ultimately be based upon an individual assessment of the complete circumstances surrounding the verified violation.

The publisher shall consider:

- The seriousness of the conduct.
- The applicable penalty tier.
- Any aggravating or mitigating factors.
- The compliance history of the responsible party.
- The proportionality of the proposed remedy.
- The availability of alternative corrective measures.
- The overall objectives of protecting intellectual property while encouraging lawful and sustainable compliance.

The penalty tier framework established throughout this Section is intended to promote consistency, transparency, and proportionality while preserving the flexibility necessary to address the wide range of circumstances that may arise under the Engineering Handbook licensing framework.

---

### 11. Mitigating Factors

While violations of the Engineering Handbook licensing framework may warrant administrative, contractual, financial, or civil remedies, the publisher recognizes that not every verified violation reflects the same level of responsibility. Certain circumstances may reasonably reduce the seriousness of a violation or support the application of less restrictive corrective measures.

Mitigating factors are circumstances that, when supported by credible evidence, may influence the selection of an appropriate remedy without eliminating responsibility for the underlying violation. The existence of one or more mitigating factors does not prevent enforcement but may justify a more proportionate response consistent with the principles established throughout this Part.

Each mitigating circumstance shall be evaluated individually in conjunction with all other relevant facts of the case.

#### 11.1 Good-Faith Conduct

Where a violation resulted from an honest mistake, misunderstanding, or other good-faith circumstances rather than deliberate misconduct, the publisher should ordinarily consider educational guidance, corrective action, or voluntary compliance before imposing more severe enforcement measures.

Good-faith conduct may include:

- Genuine misunderstanding of license terms.
- Administrative oversight.
- Isolated procedural errors.
- Accidental technical failures.
- Other comparable non-malicious circumstances.

#### 11.2 Voluntary Disclosure

Where an individual or organization voluntarily reports a licensing issue before formal enforcement action has commenced, such cooperation may be considered a mitigating factor.
