Voluntary disclosure may demonstrate a genuine intention to resolve compliance concerns and may support negotiated corrective measures where appropriate.

#### 11.3 Prompt Corrective Action

The publisher may consider whether the responsible party acted promptly to correct the verified violation after becoming aware of the issue.

Examples include:

- Removing unauthorized copies.
- Purchasing the appropriate license.
- Updating licensing records.
- Restoring contractual compliance.
- Implementing security improvements.
- Correcting administrative deficiencies.

Prompt corrective action may reduce the need for more significant contractual or legal remedies.

#### 11.4 Cooperation During Investigation

A responsible party that cooperates fully during a compliance review or investigation may receive more favorable consideration than one who obstructs or delays the enforcement process.

Examples of cooperation include:

- Providing requested information.
- Preserving relevant evidence.
- Responding within reasonable timeframes.
- Assisting with compliance verification.
- Implementing agreed corrective measures.

Cooperation does not eliminate responsibility but may support a more proportionate enforcement outcome.

#### 11.5 Limited Harm

Where the verified violation resulted in little or no measurable harm to the publisher, legitimate license holders, or other affected parties, this circumstance may be considered when determining the appropriate remedy.

Limited harm should not excuse non-compliance but may support corrective rather than punitive responses where consistent with the objectives of the licensing framework.

#### 11.6 First-Time Violation

A verified first-time violation may warrant a more educational and corrective approach than repeated misconduct, particularly where there is no evidence of deliberate infringement or commercial exploitation.

First-time offenders who demonstrate a willingness to comply should ordinarily be encouraged to restore compliance through appropriate corrective measures whenever reasonably practicable.

#### 11.7 Institutional Compliance Efforts

Where an organization has implemented reasonable licensing controls, compliance procedures, staff training, and internal oversight but nevertheless experiences an isolated compliance failure, such efforts may be considered as mitigating circumstances.

Evidence of an effective compliance program may indicate that the violation resulted from exceptional circumstances rather than systemic disregard for licensing obligations.

#### 11.8 Financial or Operational Hardship

Where appropriate and consistent with applicable law, the publisher may consider genuine financial or operational hardship when determining the manner or timing of corrective measures or negotiated settlements.

Such hardship should not excuse deliberate infringement but may support:

- Reasonable payment arrangements.
- Extended compliance timelines.
- Phased licensing upgrades.
- Other mutually agreed solutions that restore compliance while remaining fair to all parties.

#### 11.9 Overall Assessment of Mitigating Factors

No single mitigating factor automatically determines the outcome of an enforcement decision.

The publisher shall consider:

- The seriousness of the verified violation.
- The credibility of the mitigating evidence.
- The overall compliance history.
- The presence of any aggravating factors.
- The need to protect intellectual property.
- The objectives of achieving fair, proportionate, and sustainable compliance.

Mitigating factors should be evaluated collectively rather than in isolation, ensuring that enforcement decisions remain balanced, transparent, and consistent with the guiding principles established throughout this Manual.

---

### 12. Settlement Options

The publisher recognizes that many licensing disputes can be resolved more efficiently through voluntary settlement rather than prolonged enforcement proceedings or litigation. Accordingly, where appropriate, the parties may seek to resolve verified licensing matters through negotiated settlement arrangements that restore compliance, protect intellectual property, and minimize unnecessary legal costs and disruption.

Settlement is intended to provide a practical, fair, and cooperative method of resolving disputes while preserving the publisher's legitimate rights and encouraging long-term compliance with the Engineering Handbook licensing framework.

Nothing contained within this Section obligates either party to enter into a settlement agreement, nor does it prevent the publisher from pursuing other lawful remedies where settlement is inappropriate or unsuccessful.

#### 12.1 Voluntary Nature of Settlement

Settlement discussions shall ordinarily be voluntary unless otherwise required by applicable law or contractual obligations.

Either party may:

- Propose settlement discussions.
- Accept or decline settlement negotiations.
- Request clarification of proposed terms.
- Seek independent legal or professional advice before entering into an agreement.

Participation in settlement discussions shall not, by itself, constitute an admission of liability unless expressly stated in the final agreement.

#### 12.2 Appropriate Circumstances for Settlement

Settlement may be appropriate where:

- The violation has been acknowledged.
- The parties wish to avoid unnecessary litigation.
- Compliance can be restored through negotiated measures.
- Outstanding licensing issues can be resolved cooperatively.
- The costs of formal proceedings outweigh the likely benefits.
- Continued business or educational relationships are desirable.

Settlement may be less appropriate where serious fraud, commercial piracy, organized infringement, or other deliberate misconduct requires stronger legal enforcement.

#### 12.3 Settlement Terms

A settlement agreement may include one or more of the following terms, as appropriate:

- Payment of outstanding licensing fees.
- Purchase of additional licenses.
- Removal of unauthorized copies.
- Restoration of licensing compliance.
- Compliance with specified corrective measures.
- Agreed financial compensation where appropriate.
- Future compliance commitments.
- Confidentiality provisions where permitted by law.
- Other mutually agreed contractual obligations.

Settlement terms shall remain subject to applicable law and the mutual agreement of the parties.

#### 12.4 Corrective Actions

As part of a negotiated settlement, the responsible party may agree to undertake corrective measures designed to prevent future violations.

Corrective actions may include:

- Updating licensing records.
- Improving administrative controls.
- Strengthening account security.
- Conducting internal compliance reviews.
- Implementing staff training.
- Removing unauthorized content.
- Adopting improved license management procedures.

Successful completion of agreed corrective actions may be considered when evaluating future compliance.

#### 12.5 Payment Arrangements

Where financial obligations form part of a settlement, the parties may mutually agree upon reasonable payment arrangements consistent with applicable law and the governing agreement.

Such arrangements may include:

- Lump-sum payments.
- Installment schedules.
- Payment deadlines.
- License upgrade plans.
- Other mutually acceptable financial terms.

Failure to comply with agreed payment arrangements may result in further contractual or legal action where permitted.

#### 12.6 Confidentiality of Settlement

Where permitted by applicable law, settlement agreements may contain confidentiality provisions governing the disclosure of settlement negotiations or agreed terms.

Confidentiality provisions shall not prevent disclosures required by:

- Applicable law.
- Court orders.
- Regulatory authorities.
- Enforcement of the settlement agreement.
- Other legally recognized obligations.

#### 12.7 Effect of Settlement

Unless otherwise expressly provided, a properly executed settlement agreement shall resolve only those matters specifically identified within the agreement.

Settlement of one dispute does not automatically:

- Modify unrelated contractual obligations.
- Waive future enforcement rights.
- Authorize future non-compliance.
- Affect unrelated licensing matters.

The publisher retains all rights relating to future or unrelated violations unless expressly waived in writing.

#### 12.8 Failure of Settlement

Where settlement negotiations do not result in an agreement or where an executed settlement agreement is materially breached, the publisher may pursue any lawful remedies available under:

- The applicable license agreement.
- This Manual.
- Applicable copyright law.
- Civil law.
- Other relevant legal provisions.

Participation in unsuccessful settlement discussions shall not prejudice the legal rights of either party.

#### 12.9 Good-Faith Negotiations

The publisher encourages settlement discussions to be conducted in good faith, with honesty, professionalism, and a genuine willingness to resolve verified licensing issues efficiently.

Good-faith negotiations should seek to:

- Restore compliance.
- Protect intellectual property.
- Resolve disputes fairly.
- Reduce unnecessary legal expense.
- Preserve appropriate professional relationships where possible.

The settlement framework established throughout this Section is intended to provide a flexible and efficient mechanism for resolving licensing disputes while safeguarding the publisher's intellectual property, respecting the rights of legitimate license holders, and promoting long-term compliance with the Engineering Handbook licensing framework.

---

### 13. Appeals

The Engineering Handbook licensing framework recognizes that enforcement decisions should be fair, transparent, and subject to appropriate review where circumstances warrant. Accordingly, individuals and organizations affected by certain administrative or contractual decisions may request that those decisions be reconsidered through the appeal process described in this Section.

The purpose of an appeal is to provide an opportunity to review whether an enforcement decision was made consistently with the applicable license agreement, the provisions of this Manual, and the available evidence. An appeal is not intended to delay compliance unnecessarily or to provide repeated opportunities to challenge matters that have already been fairly determined.

Unless otherwise required by applicable law or the governing agreement, the publisher retains discretion regarding the procedures applicable to individual appeals.

#### 13.1 Right to Request Review

Subject to the applicable license agreement and relevant legal requirements, an individual or organization may request review of certain administrative or contractual decisions where they reasonably believe that:

- Relevant evidence was overlooked.
- A material factual error occurred.
- The applicable licensing provisions were incorrectly applied.
- New evidence has become available.
- The selected remedy is disproportionate to the verified violation.
- Other circumstances justify reconsideration.

The submission of an appeal does not automatically suspend the effectiveness of the original decision unless the publisher expressly determines otherwise.

#### 13.2 Submission of an Appeal

An appeal should ordinarily be submitted in writing and should include sufficient information to permit meaningful review.

Where appropriate, the appeal should identify:

- The decision being challenged.
- The reasons for requesting review.
- Relevant supporting evidence.
- Any newly available information.
- The specific outcome being requested.
- Any other information reasonably necessary for reconsideration.

Incomplete appeals may require additional information before review can proceed.

#### 13.3 Review Process

Upon receiving a properly submitted appeal, the publisher may review:

- The original enforcement decision.
- The available evidence.
- Any newly submitted information.
- The applicable contractual provisions.
- The relevant provisions of this Manual.
- Any other material reasonably necessary to ensure a fair review.

The review should be conducted objectively and independently from the original decision wherever reasonably practicable.

#### 13.4 Additional Information

During the review process, the publisher may request additional documentation or clarification where necessary.

Examples include:

- Licensing records.
- Purchase documentation.
- Technical information.
- Compliance reports.
- Explanations relating to the disputed facts.
- Other relevant supporting materials.

Failure to provide reasonably requested information may limit the publisher's ability to reconsider the original decision.

#### 13.5 Possible Outcomes

Following review of the appeal, the publisher may:

- Uphold the original decision.
- Modify the selected remedy.
- Reduce or remove certain administrative measures.
- Request additional corrective action.
- Return the matter for further investigation.
- Replace the original decision with an alternative outcome consistent with this Manual.
- Take any other lawful action appropriate to the verified circumstances.

Each appeal shall be determined according to its own facts and applicable contractual obligations.

#### 13.6 Final Administrative Decision

Unless otherwise provided by applicable law or the governing agreement, the publisher's decision following completion of the internal appeal process shall ordinarily constitute the final administrative determination under this Manual.

Nothing contained within this Section limits any legal rights that either party may possess under applicable law to pursue other lawful dispute resolution procedures.

#### 13.7 Relationship with Legal Proceedings

The existence of an internal appeal process does not prevent either party from exercising legal rights available under applicable law where appropriate.

Likewise, the initiation of legal proceedings does not necessarily require the publisher to continue or suspend an internal appeal unless required by law, court order, or contractual obligation.

The relationship between administrative appeals and formal legal proceedings shall be governed by the applicable legal framework and the relevant contractual provisions.

#### 13.8 Good-Faith Participation

Both the publisher and the responsible party should participate in the appeal process honestly, professionally, and in good faith.

The appeal process should not be used to:

- Delay legitimate enforcement unnecessarily.
- Conceal relevant evidence.
- Misrepresent material facts.
- Circumvent contractual obligations.
- Harass or burden the other party.

Good-faith participation promotes fair decision-making and efficient resolution of licensing disputes.

#### 13.9 Fair and Independent Review

The appeal process established throughout this Section is intended to strengthen confidence in the Engineering Handbook licensing framework by ensuring that enforcement decisions remain transparent, evidence-based, proportionate, and consistent with the guiding principles established throughout this Manual.

Every appeal shall be assessed on its own merits, taking into account the available evidence, applicable contractual obligations, relevant legal requirements, and the overarching objective of achieving fair, lawful, and sustainable compliance.

---

### 14. Collection and Recovery

Where financial obligations arise under the Engineering Handbook licensing framework, the publisher may take reasonable and lawful steps to recover amounts properly owed under the applicable license agreement, negotiated settlement, contractual arrangement, or legally enforceable judgment. Collection and recovery activities shall be conducted fairly, proportionately, and in accordance with applicable law.

The primary objective of collection and recovery is to restore contractual compliance and recover legitimate financial obligations rather than to impose punitive consequences. All recovery efforts shall respect applicable legal protections, contractual limitations, and the rights of all parties involved.

Nothing contained within this Section authorizes collection activities that are unlawful, unreasonable, or inconsistent with the governing jurisdiction.

#### 14.1 Recovery of Outstanding Financial Obligations

The publisher may seek recovery of financial obligations arising from:

- Unpaid license fees.
- Outstanding settlement payments.
- Contractually agreed charges.
- Approved licensing upgrades.
- Other amounts lawfully payable under the applicable agreement.

Recovery efforts shall be limited to amounts properly due under the governing contractual or legal framework.

#### 14.2 Payment Requests

Before pursuing more significant recovery measures, the publisher may issue written payment requests identifying:

- The amount claimed.
- The basis of the financial obligation.
- The applicable contractual provision.
- Any relevant supporting information.
- The requested payment period.
- Available methods for resolving the outstanding obligation.

Where appropriate, payment requests should provide a reasonable opportunity for voluntary resolution.

#### 14.3 Negotiated Payment Arrangements

Where immediate payment presents practical difficulties, the publisher may, at its discretion, negotiate reasonable payment arrangements consistent with the applicable agreement and governing law.

Such arrangements may include:

- Installment payment schedules.
- Revised payment deadlines.
- License upgrade plans.
- Structured settlement payments.
- Other mutually agreed financial arrangements.

Failure to comply with an agreed payment arrangement may result in further contractual or legal action where permitted.

#### 14.4 Collection Through Contractual Remedies

Where outstanding financial obligations remain unresolved, the publisher may exercise contractual remedies available under the applicable license agreement.

Such remedies may include:

- Suspension of license privileges.
- Temporary access restrictions.
- License termination.
- Suspension of support services.
- Other contractual measures expressly authorized by the governing agreement.

Contractual remedies should be exercised proportionately and consistently with the principles established throughout this Manual.

#### 14.5 Civil Recovery Proceedings

Where voluntary payment and contractual remedies do not satisfactorily resolve outstanding obligations, the publisher may pursue recovery through appropriate civil legal proceedings where authorized by applicable law.

Civil recovery may include claims relating to:

- Outstanding contractual obligations.
- Copyright-related damages.
- Breach of contract.
- Recovery of legally recognized losses.
- Other lawful monetary remedies.

Any such proceedings shall remain subject to the jurisdiction of the competent court.

#### 14.6 Record of Recovery Actions

The publisher should maintain reasonable records relating to collection and recovery activities, including where appropriate:

- Payment requests.
- Correspondence.
- Settlement agreements.
- Payment records.
- Compliance documentation.
- Recovery proceedings.
- Other relevant administrative records.

Maintaining accurate records promotes transparency, accountability, and consistent enforcement.

#### 14.7 Good-Faith Recovery Practices

Collection and recovery activities should be conducted professionally, respectfully, and in good faith.

The publisher should seek to:

- Resolve disputes efficiently.
- Encourage voluntary payment.
- Avoid unnecessary escalation.
- Communicate clearly with the responsible party.
- Consider reasonable settlement opportunities where appropriate.

Recovery practices should remain consistent with applicable legal standards governing fair commercial conduct.

#### 14.8 Limitation of Recovery Measures

Nothing contained within this Section authorizes recovery of amounts that are not lawfully owed or otherwise recoverable under the applicable contractual or legal framework.

Recovery efforts remain subject to:

- Applicable law.
- Judicial oversight where required.
- Contractual limitations.
- Statutory limitations.
- Principles of proportionality and fairness.
- Any other applicable legal restrictions.

Where uncertainty exists regarding the amount recoverable, the matter should be resolved in accordance with the governing agreement or the applicable legal process.

#### 14.9 Purpose of Collection and Recovery

The collection and recovery framework established throughout this Section is intended to ensure that legitimate financial obligations arising under the Engineering Handbook licensing framework may be resolved fairly, transparently, and lawfully while encouraging voluntary compliance, protecting intellectual property, preserving contractual relationships where appropriate, and maintaining the long-term sustainability of the Engineering Handbook publishing ecosystem.

---

### 15. No Criminal Authority

The Engineering Handbook licensing framework is a private publishing and licensing system intended to govern the contractual use of copyrighted educational materials. Nothing contained within this Manual shall be interpreted as granting the publisher any governmental, judicial, regulatory, or law enforcement authority.

The remedies described throughout this Part are contractual, administrative, civil, or otherwise lawful measures available to the publisher under applicable agreements and relevant legal principles. They do not create criminal offences, establish criminal liability, or authorize the publisher to impose criminal penalties.

Questions concerning criminal responsibility remain exclusively within the jurisdiction of the competent governmental authorities and courts operating under applicable law.

#### 15.1 No Power to Impose Criminal Penalties

The publisher does not possess authority to:

- Impose criminal fines.
- Order imprisonment.
- Conduct criminal investigations.
- Execute search or seizure powers.
- Compel testimony under criminal law.
- Exercise police or prosecutorial functions.
- Perform any governmental enforcement activities reserved to public authorities.

Any reference within this Manual to legal enforcement shall be interpreted only within the scope of the publisher's lawful contractual and civil rights.

#### 15.2 Civil and Contractual Nature of Enforcement

Except where otherwise required by applicable law, enforcement activities conducted by the publisher are limited to lawful civil and contractual measures, including:

- Administrative compliance actions.
- Contractual remedies.
- Financial recovery.
- Civil legal proceedings.
- Settlement negotiations.
- Alternative dispute resolution.
- Other lawful mechanisms recognized by the applicable legal framework.

These measures are intended to protect intellectual property and restore licensing compliance rather than to punish criminal conduct.

#### 15.3 Referral to Competent Authorities

Where the publisher becomes aware of conduct that may constitute a criminal offence under applicable law, the publisher may, where lawful and appropriate, refer the matter to the competent governmental authorities.

Examples may include:

- Large-scale commercial piracy.
- Counterfeiting.
- Identity fraud.
- Organized intellectual property crime.
- Forgery.
- Other conduct potentially falling within the jurisdiction of law enforcement agencies.

Any decision regarding criminal investigation, prosecution, or criminal penalties shall remain exclusively within the authority of the competent public authorities.

#### 15.4 Cooperation with Lawful Investigations

Where required by applicable law or lawful legal process, the publisher may cooperate with competent governmental authorities by providing information, documentation, or other evidence lawfully available to the publisher.

Such cooperation shall be conducted in accordance with:

- Applicable privacy laws.
- Data protection requirements.
- Court orders.
- Statutory obligations.
- Other applicable legal requirements.

Nothing in this Manual authorizes disclosure of information beyond what is legally permitted or required.

#### 15.5 Preservation of Legal Rights

Nothing contained within this Part shall:

- Limit the rights of governmental authorities.
- Restrict the jurisdiction of competent courts.
- Prevent lawful criminal investigations.
- Affect statutory rights available under applicable law.
- Reduce the legal protections available to either party.
- Override mandatory legal requirements.

This Manual shall always be interpreted consistently with the applicable legal framework governing copyright, contracts, civil proceedings, privacy, and related matters.

#### 15.6 Interpretation of Enforcement Provisions

Whenever enforcement provisions contained within this Manual are interpreted, they shall be understood as referring exclusively to lawful contractual, administrative, financial, civil, or other legally recognized remedies available to the publisher.

No provision of this Manual shall be construed as creating criminal liability, expanding governmental authority, or replacing the functions of courts, regulators, or law enforcement agencies.

#### 15.7 Final Statement

This Part establishes a comprehensive framework governing the fines, penalties, remedies, settlements, appeals, and recovery procedures applicable to the Engineering Handbook licensing framework. Its purpose is to promote lawful use of copyrighted educational materials, encourage voluntary compliance, protect the publisher's intellectual property, and provide consistent guidance for fair and proportionate enforcement.

All remedies described throughout this Part shall be interpreted and applied in accordance with the governing license agreement, applicable law, and the guiding principles of fairness, proportionality, transparency, consistency, and good-faith enforcement established throughout this Manual.

---

### 16. Decision Summary

This Part establishes the official framework governing the consequences of violations within the Engineering Handbook licensing ecosystem. It defines the administrative, contractual, financial, and civil remedies that may be applied when license agreements, copyright protections, or related contractual obligations are violated. The framework emphasizes fairness, proportionality, transparency, evidence-based decision-making, and voluntary compliance while protecting the publisher's intellectual property and the rights of legitimate license holders.

The Part first explains the purpose and scope of enforcement, distinguishing between fines, penalties, and remedies, and establishes guiding principles that govern every enforcement decision. It then classifies the various forms of licensing violations—including administrative errors, license misuse, unauthorized sharing, institutional non-compliance, commercial piracy, fraud, counterfeiting, repeat violations, aggravated misconduct, and good-faith violations—to ensure that enforcement actions remain consistent and proportionate.

Subsequent sections describe the full range of administrative penalties, financial remedies, civil remedies, contractual remedies, and institutional enforcement measures available to the publisher. The Part further establishes principles governing repeat violations, aggravating and mitigating circumstances, graduated penalty tiers, negotiated settlements, internal appeals, lawful recovery of financial obligations, and the limitations of the publisher's enforcement authority.

Finally, this Part clarifies that the Engineering Handbook licensing framework operates solely as a private contractual and civil enforcement system. It does not create criminal offences, confer governmental authority, or replace the jurisdiction of courts or law enforcement agencies. Instead, it provides a comprehensive, legally compliant framework that promotes responsible licensing, encourages voluntary compliance, safeguards copyrighted educational materials, and ensures the long-term sustainability and integrity of the Engineering Handbook publishing ecosystem.

---

## PART VIII - Institutional and Organizational Licensing

---

### 1. Purpose and Scope

Institutional and organizational licensing enables educational institutions, commercial organizations, governmental bodies, libraries, research institutions, and other eligible entities to lawfully access and use the Engineering Handbook Series under structured multi-user licensing arrangements.

Unlike individual licenses, which are granted to a single licensed customer, institutional licenses are designed to support multiple authorized users operating within a common administrative, educational, professional, or organizational environment while ensuring compliance with the publisher's intellectual property rights and licensing framework.

This Part establishes the policies governing the acquisition, administration, management, expansion, renewal, suspension, and termination of institutional licenses. It also defines the responsibilities of organizations, designated license administrators, authorized users, and the publisher throughout the lifecycle of an institutional licensing relationship.

Nothing contained within this Part transfers ownership of the Engineering Handbook Series or any associated intellectual property to an institution or organization. Institutional licenses grant only the limited rights expressly provided by the applicable license agreement.

This Part should be interpreted together with all other Parts of the Publishing, Copyright & Licensing Manual, including those governing copyright ownership, licensing models, digital rights management, compliance procedures, enforcement, and remedies.

---

#### 1.1 Purpose

The primary objectives of institutional licensing are to:

- provide lawful multi-user access to the Engineering Handbook Series;
- support educational, research, governmental, and professional activities;
- simplify license administration for organizations;
- establish consistent organizational licensing standards;
- protect the publisher's intellectual property rights;
- encourage responsible use of licensed publications;
- facilitate scalable licensing as organizations grow; and
- maintain fairness between institutional and individual license holders.

Institutional licensing seeks to balance accessibility with responsible intellectual property management by providing organizations with licensing solutions that reflect their operational requirements while preserving the integrity of the Engineering Handbook publishing ecosystem.

---

#### 1.2 Scope

Unless otherwise specified in the applicable license agreement, this Part applies to every institutional or organizational license issued by the publisher, including licenses granted to:

- universities and colleges;
- schools and educational academies;
- libraries;
- research institutions;
- government departments and agencies;
- commercial organizations;
- engineering firms;
- consulting organizations;
- professional associations;
- non-profit organizations;
- training providers; and
- any other eligible legal entity approved by the publisher.

This Part governs institutional licensing regardless of whether the licensed materials are accessed through printed publications, digital publications, online platforms, enterprise portals, or other authorized distribution methods.

---

#### 1.3 Relationship with Individual Licenses

Institutional licenses are separate from individual licenses and shall not be interpreted as replacing or extending individual licensing rights unless expressly stated in the applicable agreement.

An individual license:

- is granted to a single licensed customer;
- is generally non-transferable;
- may not be converted into an institutional license without the publisher's approval; and
- does not authorize organizational or enterprise-wide use.

An institutional license:

- is granted to an eligible legal entity;
- authorizes use by multiple authorized users within the licensed scope;
- is administered by the organization or its designated representatives; and
- remains subject to all applicable organizational licensing obligations.

The existence of an institutional license does not automatically authorize every employee, student, contractor, affiliate, or visitor of the organization to access the Engineering Handbook Series. Access remains limited to authorized users acting within the scope of the applicable license agreement.

---

#### 1.4 Governing Principles

Institutional licensing under the Engineering Handbook Series shall be administered in accordance with the following principles:

#### Lawful Licensing

Every organization shall obtain an appropriate license before accessing or distributing the Engineering Handbook Series beyond the permissions granted under applicable law.

#### Responsible Administration

Organizations should maintain appropriate internal procedures for managing licensed resources, authorized users, access controls, and compliance obligations.

#### Fair Access

Institutional licensing should provide organizations with practical and scalable access to educational resources while ensuring that licensing terms remain fair to both the publisher and legitimate license holders.

#### Protection of Intellectual Property

All institutional licensing activities shall respect the publisher's copyrights, trademarks, database rights, digital rights management systems, and other intellectual property rights.

#### Proportional Licensing

Organizations should obtain licensing arrangements that reasonably reflect their actual operational requirements, anticipated usage, and authorized user population.

#### Accountability

Organizations remain responsible for administering institutional licenses in accordance with the applicable agreement and for taking reasonable steps to prevent unauthorized use within their controlled environments.

#### Good-Faith Cooperation

The publisher and institutional license holders should cooperate in good faith when addressing licensing questions, administrative matters, compliance issues, license renewals, and organizational changes.

#### Scalability

Institutional licensing should support organizational growth by allowing licensing arrangements to expand, upgrade, or otherwise evolve as operational requirements change over time.

#### Compliance

Organizations shall comply with all applicable license agreements, publisher policies, contractual obligations, and relevant legal requirements governing the use of the Engineering Handbook Series.

Collectively, these principles establish the foundation for institutional and organizational licensing throughout the Engineering Handbook publishing ecosystem. The remaining provisions of this Part explain how these principles apply to organizational eligibility, license administration, authorized users, access management, compliance obligations, renewals, and other operational aspects of institutional licensing.

### 2. Eligible Organizations

Institutional licenses are intended for legally recognized organizations that require authorized access to the Engineering Handbook Series for educational, research, governmental, professional, or commercial purposes. Eligibility to obtain an institutional license is determined by the publisher in accordance with this Manual, the applicable licensing policies, and any additional eligibility requirements established for specific licensing programs.

Approval of an institutional license is not automatic. The publisher may request reasonable information necessary to verify the legal identity, operational status, intended use, and licensing requirements of an applicant before granting, renewing, modifying, or expanding an institutional license.

Organizations shall provide accurate and complete information during the licensing process. The publisher may decline, suspend, or terminate an application or license where material information is false, misleading, incomplete, or otherwise inconsistent with the applicable licensing requirements.

The following categories identify the principal organizations that may be eligible for institutional licensing.

#### 2.1 Educational Institutions

Educational institutions may obtain institutional licenses for teaching, learning, academic research, curriculum development, laboratory instruction, faculty development, and other legitimate educational activities.

Eligible educational institutions may include:

- universities;
- colleges;
- schools;
- technical institutes;
- polytechnic institutions;
- vocational training centers;
- accredited online education providers; and
- other recognized educational organizations approved by the publisher.

Institutional licenses granted to educational institutions shall be used solely within the scope of the applicable agreement and shall not authorize commercial redistribution of the Engineering Handbook Series.

#### 2.2 Universities and Colleges

Universities and colleges may obtain institutional licenses covering one or more faculties, departments, schools, research centers, laboratories, libraries, or administrative units, depending upon the applicable licensing model.

The scope of access, number of authorized users, campus coverage, and administrative responsibilities shall be defined by the applicable license agreement.

#### 2.3 Schools

Primary schools, secondary schools, higher secondary schools, academies, and equivalent educational institutions may obtain institutional licenses where the Engineering Handbook Series is appropriate for their educational programs.

School licenses should be administered by designated staff members responsible for ensuring compliance with the applicable licensing terms.

#### 2.4 Libraries

Public, academic, governmental, institutional, and specialized libraries may obtain licenses that permit authorized patrons to access the Engineering Handbook Series in accordance with the applicable library licensing agreement.

Library licenses shall not authorize unrestricted copying, downloading, redistribution, or reproduction beyond the permissions expressly granted by the applicable license.

#### 2.5 Government Organizations

Government ministries, departments, agencies, public authorities, regulatory bodies, public sector undertakings, defense organizations, and other governmental entities may obtain institutional licenses for official governmental purposes.

Government licensing shall remain subject to the same intellectual property protections applicable to other institutional license holders unless otherwise required by applicable law.

#### 2.6 Commercial Organizations

Engineering companies, consulting firms, software companies, manufacturing organizations, construction companies, technology businesses, and other commercial enterprises may obtain institutional licenses to support legitimate business activities.

Commercial licensing does not authorize resale, republication, redistribution, or incorporation of substantial portions of the Engineering Handbook Series into commercial products unless expressly permitted by the applicable agreement.

#### 2.7 Research Institutions

Independent research organizations, innovation centers, laboratories, scientific institutes, and similar research entities may obtain institutional licenses for research, experimentation, technical analysis, engineering development, and scholarly activities.

Research licenses shall remain subject to all applicable copyright and licensing restrictions established throughout this Manual.

#### 2.8 Professional Associations

Professional engineering societies, technical associations, accreditation bodies, certification organizations, standards organizations, and similar professional institutions may obtain institutional licenses for the benefit of their authorized personnel or members where permitted under the applicable agreement.

Membership in a licensed organization does not automatically create individual licensing rights beyond those expressly granted under the institutional license.

#### 2.9 Non-Profit Organizations

Charitable organizations, educational foundations, non-governmental organizations, community organizations, and other non-profit entities may be eligible for institutional licensing where their activities align with the educational or professional objectives of the Engineering Handbook Series.

Eligibility for any special licensing terms or discounted pricing shall be determined solely by the publisher and shall not be presumed by virtue of an organization's non-profit status.

#### 2.10 Other Eligible Organizations

The publisher may approve institutional licenses for other legally recognized organizations whose intended use is consistent with the objectives of the Engineering Handbook Series and the publisher's licensing policies.

Approval of organizations not expressly listed in this Section shall not constitute a precedent requiring approval of future applications.

Organizations shall satisfy any reasonable eligibility requirements established by the publisher before an institutional license is granted, renewed, expanded, or transferred.

The publisher reserves the right to request supporting documentation, conduct reasonable verification, or decline applications that do not satisfy the eligibility requirements established under this Manual or the applicable licensing agreement.

### 3. Types of Institutional Licenses

The publisher may offer different categories of institutional licenses to accommodate the varying operational requirements of educational institutions, commercial organizations, government entities, research organizations, libraries, and other eligible institutions. Each license type grants only those rights expressly described in the applicable license agreement and shall be interpreted in accordance with this Manual.

The selection of an appropriate institutional license shall depend upon factors including the nature of the organization, the number of authorized users, the intended use of the Engineering Handbook Series, the method of access, organizational structure, and any other licensing considerations determined by the publisher.

Unless expressly provided otherwise, institutional license types shall not be interpreted as interchangeable. Organizations shall obtain the license that accurately reflects their intended use and operational requirements.

#### 3.1 Departmental License

A Departmental License authorizes use of the Engineering Handbook Series by a specific department, division, laboratory, faculty, office, or other defined organizational unit.

Access under a Departmental License shall ordinarily be limited to authorized users assigned to the licensed department and shall not automatically extend to other departments or organizational units.

The applicable license agreement shall specify the scope of access, user limits, administrative responsibilities, and any departmental restrictions.

#### 3.2 Multi-Department License

A Multi-Department License authorizes multiple designated departments or organizational units within the same institution to access the licensed publications.

The applicable agreement shall identify the departments covered by the license and any limitations regarding user allocation, administrative control, or permitted organizational expansion.

Addition of new departments beyond those identified in the agreement may require modification of the license or acquisition of additional licensing rights.

#### 3.3 Campus License

A Campus License authorizes access across one or more campuses operated by the same educational institution, subject to the scope defined in the applicable agreement.

Campus Licenses may specify:

- covered campuses;
- eligible students;
- faculty members;
- researchers;
- administrative staff;
- library access;
- remote access permissions; and
- any other operational limitations.

Satellite campuses, affiliated colleges, or independently administered institutions shall not automatically be included unless expressly identified within the license agreement.

#### 3.4 Enterprise License

An Enterprise License is intended for large organizations requiring institution-wide access across multiple business units, offices, subsidiaries, divisions, or operational locations.

Enterprise Licenses may include centralized administration, consolidated user management, organizational reporting, and other enterprise-level licensing features where provided by the applicable agreement.

Affiliated companies, parent organizations, subsidiaries, joint ventures, contractors, or business partners shall not be covered unless expressly included within the Enterprise License.

#### 3.5 Government License

Government Licenses are intended for ministries, departments, agencies, regulatory authorities, public sector organizations, and other governmental entities requiring authorized access for official governmental purposes.

Government Licenses remain subject to the same intellectual property protections, licensing restrictions, and compliance obligations applicable to other institutional licenses unless otherwise required by applicable law or expressly agreed in writing.

#### 3.6 Library License

A Library License authorizes eligible libraries to provide controlled access to the Engineering Handbook Series for authorized patrons in accordance with the applicable agreement.

Library Licenses may include provisions relating to:

- on-site access;
- authenticated remote access;
- digital lending where permitted;
- access management;
- patron authentication; and
- usage reporting where applicable.

Library Licenses shall not authorize unrestricted copying, downloading, redistribution, or republication of the Engineering Handbook Series beyond the permissions expressly granted.

#### 3.7 Research License

A Research License is intended for research institutions, laboratories, innovation centers, and similar organizations engaged in engineering research, scientific investigation, technical development, or scholarly activities.

Research Licenses authorize access solely for legitimate research purposes and do not automatically permit commercial publication, redistribution, product integration, or derivative commercial use of the Engineering Handbook Series.

#### 3.8 Consortium License

Where approved by the publisher, multiple legally independent organizations may obtain a Consortium License under a single licensing arrangement.

The applicable agreement shall identify:

- participating organizations;
- administrative responsibilities;
- authorized user populations;
- access limitations;
- financial responsibilities; and
- governance arrangements.

Participation in a consortium shall not authorize organizations outside the approved consortium to access the licensed publications.

#### 3.9 Custom Institutional License

The publisher may negotiate custom institutional licensing arrangements where an organization's operational requirements cannot reasonably be accommodated under the standard licensing models.

Custom licenses may address matters including:

- specialized deployment environments;
- unique organizational structures;
- international operations;
- large-scale user populations;
- integrated enterprise systems;
- bespoke administrative requirements; or
- other operational considerations.

Unless expressly modified in writing, all provisions of this Manual shall continue to apply to custom institutional licenses.

#### 3.10 Selection and Modification of License Types

Organizations are responsible for selecting the institutional license that most accurately reflects their intended use and operational requirements.

Where organizational requirements change due to growth, restructuring, mergers, acquisitions, expansion, or other operational developments, the publisher may require the organization to modify, upgrade, or replace its existing institutional license to ensure continued compliance with the applicable licensing framework.

The availability, scope, pricing, and eligibility requirements of each institutional license type shall be determined by the publisher and may be revised from time to time in accordance with the publisher's licensing policies and applicable agreements.

### 4. Authorized Users

Institutional licenses authorize access to the Engineering Handbook Series only by individuals who qualify as authorized users under the applicable license agreement. Authorization is determined by the organization, subject to the limitations established by the publisher and the governing institutional license.

Institutional licenses do not create unrestricted organizational access. Only individuals who satisfy the applicable eligibility requirements and who access the Engineering Handbook Series for legitimate organizational purposes may be designated as authorized users.

Organizations are responsible for ensuring that authorized user designations remain accurate, current, and consistent with the applicable license agreement.

#### 4.1 Definition of an Authorized User

An authorized user is an individual who has been granted permission by both the institutional license holder and the applicable institutional license to access and use the Engineering Handbook Series within the scope of the rights granted under the governing agreement.

Authorized user status exists only for the duration and extent permitted by the applicable institutional license and may be modified, suspended, or revoked in accordance with the terms of the license agreement.

#### 4.2 Eligible Authorized Users

Subject to the applicable institutional license, authorized users may include:

- employees;
- faculty members;
- researchers;
- instructors;
- administrative personnel;
- enrolled students;
- librarians;
- designated contractors;
- approved consultants; and
- other individuals expressly authorized under the applicable agreement.

The publisher may establish additional eligibility requirements for particular institutional licensing programs.

#### 4.3 User Authentication

Organizations shall implement reasonable procedures to ensure that access to the Engineering Handbook Series is limited to authorized users.

Authentication mechanisms may include:

- institutional accounts;
- authenticated single sign-on systems;
- organizational identity providers;
- directory services;
- secure credentials;
- access tokens; or
- other reasonable authentication methods.

Organizations remain responsible for maintaining appropriate authentication procedures throughout the duration of the institutional license.

#### 4.4 Responsibilities of Authorized Users

Authorized users shall:

- comply with the applicable institutional license agreement;
- use the Engineering Handbook Series only for authorized purposes;
- protect their authentication credentials;
- avoid unauthorized sharing of licensed materials;
- respect applicable copyright and intellectual property rights;
- comply with organizational policies governing licensed resources; and
- promptly report suspected unauthorized access or misuse where reasonably practicable.

Individual authorized users remain responsible for their own conduct notwithstanding the existence of an institutional license.

#### 4.5 Organizational Responsibilities

The institutional license holder shall take reasonable measures to:

- maintain accurate user records;
- grant access only to eligible users;
- remove access for individuals who are no longer authorized;
- prevent unauthorized account sharing;
- monitor compliance with organizational licensing policies where appropriate; and
- cooperate with the publisher regarding licensing administration and compliance matters.

Organizations are expected to administer authorized user access in a manner consistent with the applicable license agreement and accepted information security practices.

#### 4.6 Temporary Users

The applicable institutional license may permit temporary access for visiting faculty, guest researchers, temporary employees, interns, exchange students, or other temporary participants where expressly authorized.

Temporary users shall remain subject to the same licensing restrictions and compliance obligations applicable to permanent authorized users unless otherwise provided by the applicable agreement.

Organizations shall remove temporary access when the individual's authorized relationship with the organization ends or when continued access is no longer permitted under the institutional license.

#### 4.7 Former Authorized Users

Individuals who cease to qualify as authorized users shall no longer be entitled to access the Engineering Handbook Series under the institutional license unless another valid license independently authorizes such access.

Organizations should remove or disable access within a reasonable period after the individual's authorization ends.

The termination of authorized user status does not affect any continuing obligations relating to confidentiality, intellectual property, or previous unauthorized use.

#### 4.8 Shared Accounts

Unless expressly authorized by the applicable institutional license, shared accounts, generic login credentials, anonymous organizational accounts, or other mechanisms that prevent reasonable identification of authorized users shall not be used to access the Engineering Handbook Series.

Organizations should assign access through individually identifiable accounts wherever reasonably practicable.

#### 4.9 Authorized User Limits

Institutional licenses may specify limitations relating to:

- maximum authorized users;
- concurrent users;
- departmental allocations;
- campus allocations;
- enterprise user limits;
- geographical restrictions; or
- other operational limitations.

Organizations shall administer user access within the applicable limits established by the institutional license agreement.

#### 4.10 Changes to Authorized Users

Organizations may add, remove, replace, or reassign authorized users throughout the duration of the institutional license, provided that such changes remain consistent with the applicable agreement.

The publisher may require organizations to maintain reasonably accurate records of authorized users where necessary for license administration, compliance verification, or institutional support.

Nothing in this Section shall be interpreted as granting permanent licensing rights to individual authorized users independent of the institutional license. Authorized access exists solely by virtue of the applicable institutional license agreement and remains subject to its terms, limitations, suspension, expiration, or termination.

### 5. License Administration

Effective license administration is essential to ensuring that institutional licenses are managed accurately, responsibly, and consistently throughout their duration. Institutional license holders shall establish appropriate administrative procedures to oversee access to the Engineering Handbook Series, maintain compliance with the applicable license agreement, and ensure that licensed resources are used only by authorized users.

Each institution remains responsible for the administration of its own institutional license unless the applicable agreement expressly provides otherwise.

#### 5.1 Designated License Administrator

Each institutional license holder shall designate one or more individuals to serve as the primary license administrator.

The license administrator shall act as the principal point of contact between the organization and the publisher regarding licensing matters.

Responsibilities of the license administrator may include:

- managing institutional licensing records;
- administering authorized user access;
- coordinating license renewals;
- communicating with the publisher;
- responding to licensing inquiries;
- overseeing organizational compliance; and
- performing other reasonable administrative duties relating to the institutional license.

Organizations may change their designated license administrator at any time by notifying the publisher in accordance with the applicable administrative procedures.

#### 5.2 Administrative Records

Organizations shall maintain reasonably accurate records relating to the administration of their institutional license.

Such records may include:

- license agreements;
- renewal records;
- authorized user information;
- user allocation records;
- organizational contact information;
- licensing correspondence;
- compliance documentation;
- payment records; and
- other administrative information reasonably necessary for license management.

Records should be retained for the period required by the applicable agreement, organizational policy, or governing law.

#### 5.3 Organizational Contact Information

Institutional license holders shall maintain current administrative contact information throughout the duration of the license.

Organizations should promptly notify the publisher of material changes affecting:

- legal name;
- organizational address;
- billing information;
- designated administrators;
- official email addresses;
- organizational ownership where relevant;
- mergers or restructurings affecting the license; or
- other information reasonably necessary for license administration.

Failure to maintain accurate administrative information may delay licensing services, renewals, compliance communications, or other administrative processes.

#### 5.4 Internal Administration

Organizations should establish appropriate internal procedures for managing institutional access to the Engineering Handbook Series.

Such procedures may include:

- user onboarding;
- user removal procedures;
- access approval workflows;
- periodic access reviews;
- credential management;
- internal compliance monitoring;
- security controls; and
- documentation of licensing responsibilities.

The specific administrative procedures adopted by an organization remain its responsibility provided they are consistent with the applicable institutional license.

#### 5.5 Organizational Changes

Where an organization undergoes significant operational changes that may affect the institutional license, the organization should notify the publisher within a reasonable period.

Examples include:

- mergers;
- acquisitions;
- corporate restructuring;
- division of organizational units;
- changes in legal ownership;
- institutional renaming;
- establishment of additional campuses;
- closure of organizational units; or
- other material organizational changes.

The publisher may review whether the existing institutional license continues to accurately reflect the organization's operational requirements.

#### 5.6 Delegation of Administrative Responsibilities

A designated license administrator may delegate administrative responsibilities to other authorized personnel where appropriate.

Delegation of administrative duties does not transfer legal responsibility for compliance with the institutional license.

The institutional license holder remains responsible for ensuring that delegated administrators perform their duties in accordance with the applicable agreement and this Manual.

#### 5.7 Administrative Communications

Official communications relating to institutional licensing may be delivered using the contact information designated by the institutional license holder.

Administrative communications may include:

- renewal notices;
- compliance notifications;
- licensing updates;
- invoices;
- policy changes;
- maintenance announcements;
- security notifications;
- support communications; and
- other matters relating to the administration of the institutional license.

Organizations are responsible for ensuring that designated administrative contacts remain capable of receiving such communications.

#### 5.8 Administrative Reviews

The publisher may periodically review institutional licensing information to ensure that administrative records remain accurate and current.

Administrative reviews are intended to support effective license management and should not be interpreted as compliance investigations unless expressly stated otherwise.

Organizations should cooperate reasonably with requests for administrative verification that are directly related to license administration.

#### 5.9 Administrative Responsibilities of the Publisher

The publisher shall administer institutional licenses in a fair, consistent, and commercially reasonable manner.

The publisher may:

- maintain licensing records;
- process license applications;
- administer renewals;
- update licensing information;
- provide administrative support;
- issue licensing documentation;
- manage institutional accounts; and
- perform other administrative functions reasonably necessary for operating the institutional licensing program.

Nothing in this Section obligates the publisher to provide administrative services beyond those expressly included within the applicable institutional license agreement.

#### 5.10 Administrative Integrity

Both the publisher and institutional license holders should administer institutional licenses in good faith and maintain accurate administrative records throughout the licensing relationship.

Proper license administration promotes compliance, reduces administrative disputes, supports effective access management, and contributes to the long-term integrity and sustainability of the Engineering Handbook institutional licensing framework.

### 6. Seat Allocation and User Limits

Institutional licenses may establish limitations on the number of authorized users, concurrent users, departments, campuses, or other organizational units permitted to access the Engineering Handbook Series. These limitations are intended to ensure that licensed usage remains consistent with the scope of the applicable institutional license and the licensing model selected by the organization.

Unless expressly provided otherwise, organizations shall administer user access within the limits specified in the applicable license agreement.

#### 6.1 Licensed Seats

A licensed seat represents the right for one authorized user to access the Engineering Handbook Series in accordance with the applicable institutional license.

Unless otherwise specified in the applicable agreement, a licensed seat does not constitute ownership of the licensed publications and may only be used within the scope of the institutional license.

The number of licensed seats available to an organization shall be determined by the applicable agreement.

#### 6.2 Allocation of Seats

Organizations are responsible for allocating licensed seats among authorized users in a fair, accurate, and administratively controlled manner.

Seat allocation may be organized according to:

- departments;
- faculties;
- campuses;
- business units;
- project teams;
- research groups;
- organizational divisions; or
- other administrative structures approved by the organization.

Organizations should maintain reasonably accurate records of seat allocations where appropriate.

#### 6.3 Reassignment of Seats

Subject to the applicable institutional license, organizations may reassign licensed seats when an authorized user:

- leaves the organization;
- changes departments;
- no longer requires access;
- changes responsibilities; or
- otherwise ceases to qualify as an authorized user.

Seat reassignment should be completed within a reasonable period and in accordance with the organization's internal administrative procedures.

#### 6.4 Concurrent User Limits

Certain institutional licenses may specify limits on the number of users permitted to access the Engineering Handbook Series simultaneously.

Where concurrent user limitations apply, organizations shall implement reasonable administrative or technical measures to ensure that concurrent usage remains within the limits established by the applicable agreement.

Temporary excess usage resulting from isolated technical events should be addressed promptly upon discovery.

#### 6.5 Exceeding Licensed Capacity

Organizations shall not knowingly exceed the licensed number of authorized users, licensed seats, or other applicable usage limitations.

Where organizational growth or operational requirements cause actual usage to exceed the licensed capacity, the organization should promptly obtain an appropriate license upgrade, additional seats, or another licensing arrangement approved by the publisher.

Unintentional or temporary excess usage should be corrected as soon as reasonably practicable after it is identified.

#### 6.6 Shared Seat Restrictions

Unless expressly authorized by the applicable institutional license, licensed seats shall not be shared simultaneously among multiple individuals in a manner that circumvents the authorized user limitations established by the agreement.

Organizations should ensure that seat allocation practices accurately reflect actual authorized usage.

#### 6.7 Reserved and Inactive Seats

Organizations may maintain unassigned or reserved licensed seats for future authorized users where permitted by the applicable agreement.

Inactive seats remain part of the licensed allocation but do not increase the total number of seats authorized under the institutional license.

The publisher may establish reasonable administrative policies relating to prolonged inactive allocations where necessary for effective license management.

#### 6.8 Monitoring Seat Utilization

Organizations are encouraged to periodically review seat utilization to ensure that licensed resources continue to reflect operational requirements.

Periodic reviews may assist organizations in:

- identifying unused allocations;
- reallocating licensed seats;
- planning future license expansions;
- improving administrative efficiency;
- reducing unnecessary licensing costs; and
- supporting ongoing compliance.

Nothing in this Section requires organizations to conduct continuous monitoring unless expressly required by the applicable agreement.

#### 6.9 Expansion of Licensed Capacity

Where an organization's operational requirements increase, additional licensed seats or expanded user capacity may be obtained in accordance with the publisher's applicable licensing policies.

Expansion of licensed capacity may include:

- additional user seats;
- departmental expansions;
- campus expansions;
- enterprise upgrades;
- organizational restructuring; or
- other approved licensing modifications.

Expanded capacity becomes effective only after approval by the publisher and completion of the applicable licensing process.

#### 6.10 Compliance with User Limits

Organizations remain responsible for ensuring that the number of authorized users, licensed seats, concurrent users, and other applicable usage limitations remain consistent with the institutional license agreement.

Compliance with user limits promotes fair licensing, protects the publisher's intellectual property rights, supports accurate license administration, and ensures that institutional licensing remains sustainable for all legitimate license holders.

### 7. Access Management

Institutional license holders are responsible for administering access to the Engineering Handbook Series in a secure, controlled, and organized manner. Appropriate access management helps ensure that licensed publications remain available to authorized users while reducing the risk of unauthorized use, accidental disclosure, or misuse of licensed resources.

Access to the Engineering Handbook Series shall be limited to authorized users acting within the scope of the applicable institutional license agreement.

#### 7.1 Access Authorization

Organizations shall establish reasonable procedures for granting access to authorized users.

Access should be granted only after verifying that the individual:

- qualifies as an authorized user;
- requires access for legitimate organizational purposes;
- has been assigned the necessary permissions; and
- is subject to the applicable institutional licensing policies.

Organizations should avoid granting broader access than is reasonably necessary for the user's intended responsibilities.

#### 7.2 Authentication and Identity Verification

Access to licensed resources should be protected through appropriate authentication mechanisms.

Authentication methods may include:

- institutional user accounts;
- single sign-on systems;
- directory services;
- identity providers;
- multi-factor authentication where appropriate;
- secure credentials; or
- other reasonable authentication mechanisms.

Organizations remain responsible for protecting authentication systems used to administer institutional access.

#### 7.3 Access Permissions

Organizations should assign access permissions according to operational requirements and organizational responsibilities.

Access permissions may be differentiated based upon:

- departments;
- faculties;
- campuses;
- organizational roles;
- research groups;
- administrative responsibilities;
- licensing categories; or
- other reasonable organizational structures.

Permissions should be reviewed periodically to ensure continued accuracy.

#### 7.4 Credential Security

Authorized users shall take reasonable measures to protect authentication credentials associated with institutional access.

Organizations should encourage users to:

- maintain confidential credentials;
- use strong authentication practices;
- avoid credential sharing;
- promptly report suspected credential compromise;
- update credentials where appropriate; and
- comply with applicable organizational security policies.

Credential compromise should be addressed promptly to minimize unauthorized access.

#### 7.5 Access Reviews

Organizations are encouraged to conduct periodic reviews of user access to ensure that institutional access remains consistent with operational requirements and the applicable license agreement.

Access reviews may include:

- verification of authorized users;
- removal of inactive accounts;
- review of access permissions;
- confirmation of departmental assignments;
- identification of unnecessary privileges; and
- correction of outdated user information.

Periodic reviews support effective license administration and organizational security.

#### 7.6 Suspension of Access

Organizations may temporarily suspend access for an authorized user where reasonably necessary to:

- investigate suspected misuse;
- protect organizational systems;
- address security incidents;
- enforce internal organizational policies;
- comply with legal obligations; or
- administer the institutional license.

Temporary suspension of organizational access does not, by itself, terminate the institutional license unless otherwise provided by the applicable agreement.

#### 7.7 Revocation of Access

Organizations shall remove or revoke access where an individual:

- ceases to qualify as an authorized user;
- leaves the organization;
- no longer requires access;
- materially violates applicable organizational policies; or
- otherwise becomes ineligible under the institutional license.

Revocation of organizational access shall not affect any continuing legal or contractual obligations that survive termination of access.

#### 7.8 Remote Access

Where permitted by the applicable institutional license, organizations may provide secure remote access to authorized users.

Remote access should be administered using reasonable security measures designed to ensure that only authorized users obtain access to licensed resources.

Organizations remain responsible for administering remote access in accordance with the applicable institutional license agreement.

#### 7.9 Technical Access Controls

Organizations are encouraged to implement reasonable technical controls to support secure administration of institutional licensing.

Such controls may include:

- authentication systems;
- authorization controls;
- access logging;
- session management;
- device management;
- network security measures;
- account lifecycle management; and
- other reasonable administrative or technical safeguards.

The specific technical measures adopted remain the responsibility of the organization unless otherwise required by the applicable agreement.

#### 7.10 Access Management Responsibilities

Effective access management is a shared responsibility between the publisher, the institutional license holder, administrators, and authorized users.

Organizations remain responsible for administering user access in accordance with the applicable institutional license, while authorized users remain responsible for using licensed resources only within the permissions granted to them.

Proper access management supports organizational security, protects the publisher's intellectual property, promotes responsible use of the Engineering Handbook Series, and contributes to the long-term integrity of the institutional licensing framework.

### 8. Permitted Institutional Use

Institutional licenses authorize organizations and their authorized users to use the Engineering Handbook Series only for the purposes expressly permitted under the applicable license agreement. All rights not expressly granted remain reserved by the publisher.

Permitted use shall be interpreted narrowly and shall not be construed as granting any implied rights, ownership interests, intellectual property rights, or unrestricted usage beyond the scope of the applicable institutional license.

#### 8.1 General Permitted Use

Authorized users may access and use the Engineering Handbook Series solely for legitimate organizational purposes consistent with the applicable institutional license.

Permitted activities may include:

- education;
- teaching;
- learning;
- research;
- professional reference;
- engineering practice;
- internal training;
- academic study; and
- other purposes expressly authorized by the applicable agreement.

Use of the Engineering Handbook Series shall remain subject to all applicable copyright, licensing, and intellectual property provisions contained in this Manual.

#### 8.2 Educational Use

Educational institutions may permit authorized students, instructors, faculty members, and academic staff to access the Engineering Handbook Series for legitimate educational activities.

Educational use may include:

- classroom instruction;
- curriculum support;
- coursework;
- laboratory activities;
- academic preparation;
- independent study;
- faculty development; and
- other educational activities consistent with the institutional license.

Educational use does not authorize reproduction or redistribution beyond the permissions expressly granted.

#### 8.3 Research Use

Authorized users may use the Engineering Handbook Series for lawful research, engineering analysis, scientific investigation, technical reference, literature review, and related scholarly activities.

Research use does not authorize:

- republication of substantial portions of the Engineering Handbook Series;
- creation of competing publications;
- commercial redistribution;
- unauthorized derivative publications; or
- any other activity that exceeds the scope of the applicable institutional license.

#### 8.4 Professional and Internal Organizational Use

Commercial organizations, government entities, research institutions, and other eligible organizations may use the Engineering Handbook Series as an internal professional reference where permitted by the applicable license.

Internal professional use may include:

- technical consultation;
- engineering reference;
- employee training;
- professional development;
- standards review;
- project planning;
- internal knowledge development; and
- other legitimate internal organizational activities.

Internal use shall not be interpreted as authorizing external commercial exploitation of the Engineering Handbook Series.

#### 8.5 Internal Sharing

Authorized users may share limited references to the Engineering Handbook Series with other authorized users within the same licensed organization where reasonably necessary for legitimate organizational activities.

Internal sharing shall remain subject to the applicable institutional license and shall not involve unauthorized duplication, redistribution, republication, or dissemination beyond the authorized user community.

#### 8.6 Printing and Downloading

Where permitted by the applicable institutional license, authorized users may print or download limited portions of the Engineering Handbook Series for their own lawful organizational use.

Printed or downloaded copies:

- remain subject to copyright protection;
- shall not become the property of the user;
- shall not remove or alter copyright notices;
- shall not be redistributed outside the permitted scope; and
- remain governed by the applicable license agreement.

The publisher may establish reasonable limits regarding printing or downloading under particular licensing programs.

#### 8.7 Citation and Academic Referencing

Authorized users may cite the Engineering Handbook Series in accordance with accepted academic, scholarly, or professional citation standards.

Proper citation does not authorize reproduction of copyrighted material beyond the permissions otherwise granted by applicable copyright law or the institutional license.

#### 8.8 Incidental Organizational Copies

Where reasonably necessary for technical operation, security, indexing, caching, accessibility, backup, or other incidental organizational purposes, temporary or incidental copies may be created by organizational systems.

Such copies:

- shall exist only to support authorized access;
- shall remain subject to copyright protection;
- shall not constitute separate licensed copies; and
- shall not be used for independent redistribution or publication.

#### 8.9 No Implied Rights

Nothing contained in this Section shall be interpreted as granting permission to:

- reproduce substantial portions of the Engineering Handbook Series;
- publish or republish the publications;
- create competing works;
- remove copyright notices;
- sublicense licensed materials;
- transfer institutional licensing rights;
- distribute copies outside the licensed organization; or
- exercise any right not expressly granted by the applicable license agreement.

All rights not expressly granted remain reserved by the publisher.

#### 8.10 Interpretation of Permitted Use

Permitted institutional use shall always be interpreted consistently with:

- the applicable institutional license agreement;
- this Manual;
- applicable copyright law;
- applicable intellectual property law; and
- other governing legal obligations.

Where uncertainty exists regarding whether a particular activity is permitted, the activity shall be considered unauthorized unless the publisher expressly approves it in writing.

### 9. Prohibited Institutional Use

Institutional licenses grant only the limited rights expressly described in the applicable license agreement. Any activity that exceeds those expressly granted rights constitutes prohibited use unless otherwise authorized in writing by the publisher or required by applicable law.

The examples contained in this Section are illustrative and shall not be interpreted as an exhaustive list of prohibited activities.

#### 9.1 Unauthorized Redistribution

Organizations and authorized users shall not redistribute the Engineering Handbook Series, in whole or in part, beyond the scope of the applicable institutional license.

Prohibited redistribution includes:

- public distribution;
- external organizational sharing;
- internet publication;
- uploading to publicly accessible platforms;
- unauthorized file sharing;
- unauthorized email distribution; or
