- any other form of distribution not expressly authorized by the publisher.

#### 9.2 Unauthorized Reproduction

Except as expressly permitted by the applicable institutional license or applicable law, organizations and authorized users shall not reproduce substantial portions of the Engineering Handbook Series.

Prohibited reproduction includes:

- mass copying;
- systematic duplication;
- commercial reproduction;
- creation of duplicate publications;
- reproduction for resale; or
- any other unauthorized copying beyond the rights granted under the institutional license.

#### 9.3 Unauthorized Commercial Exploitation

Institutional licenses shall not be used to support unauthorized commercial exploitation of the Engineering Handbook Series.

Without the publisher's prior written authorization, organizations and authorized users shall not:

- sell copies of the publications;
- license the publications to third parties;
- include substantial content within commercial products;
- create competing commercial publications;
- monetize licensed content independently; or
- otherwise commercially exploit the Engineering Handbook Series beyond the scope of the applicable institutional license.

#### 9.4 Unauthorized Public Availability

Organizations and authorized users shall not make the Engineering Handbook Series publicly available through:

- public websites;
- publicly accessible repositories;
- file-sharing services;
- public cloud storage;
- open educational repositories;
- public databases; or
- other publicly accessible systems,

unless expressly authorized by the publisher.

#### 9.5 Circumvention of License Restrictions

Organizations and authorized users shall not intentionally circumvent technical, contractual, administrative, or licensing measures designed to enforce the institutional license.

Prohibited conduct includes attempts to bypass:

- user limits;
- authentication controls;
- access restrictions;
- technical protection measures;
- licensing controls;
- organizational access policies; or
- other lawful security mechanisms.

#### 9.6 Unauthorized Sharing of Credentials

Authorized users shall not share authentication credentials with individuals who are not authorized users under the applicable institutional license.

Organizations shall take reasonable measures to discourage and prevent unauthorized credential sharing where practicable.

#### 9.7 Removal of Intellectual Property Notices

Organizations and authorized users shall not remove, obscure, modify, or falsify:

- copyright notices;
- publisher identification;
- license information;
- ownership notices;
- digital watermarks;
- attribution statements; or
- other proprietary notices associated with the Engineering Handbook Series.

#### 9.8 Automated Collection and Data Extraction

Unless expressly authorized by the publisher, organizations and authorized users shall not use automated methods to systematically collect, copy, extract, index, scrape, harvest, or reproduce substantial portions of the Engineering Handbook Series.

This restriction includes automated technologies such as:

- web crawlers;
- scraping tools;
- automated download systems;
- bots;
- bulk extraction software;
- automated replication systems; or
- other similar technologies.

Reasonable indexing or technical processing necessary for authorized organizational access shall not be prohibited where consistent with the applicable institutional license.

#### 9.9 Misrepresentation of Licensing Rights

Organizations and authorized users shall not falsely represent that they possess rights beyond those granted under the applicable institutional license.

Prohibited misrepresentations include:

- claiming ownership of the Engineering Handbook Series;
- representing the organization as the publisher;
- claiming authority to sublicense the publications;
- asserting unrestricted distribution rights; or
- making other false representations concerning licensing or ownership.

#### 9.10 General Prohibition

Any use of the Engineering Handbook Series that exceeds the rights expressly granted under the applicable institutional license, violates this Manual, infringes applicable intellectual property rights, or contravenes applicable law shall constitute prohibited institutional use.

The publisher reserves all rights not expressly granted and may take appropriate administrative, contractual, or legal action in response to prohibited use in accordance with this Manual and applicable law.

### 10. Remote Access and Off-Campus Access

Institutional licenses may permit authorized users to access the Engineering Handbook Series from locations outside the physical premises of the licensed organization, subject to the applicable institutional license agreement and the organization's access management procedures.

Remote access privileges exist solely to support legitimate institutional activities and shall not be interpreted as granting unrestricted personal access independent of the institutional license.

#### 10.1 Eligibility for Remote Access

Only authorized users who qualify under the applicable institutional license may access the Engineering Handbook Series remotely.

Remote access shall remain subject to:

- the applicable institutional license agreement;
- organizational access policies;
- user authentication requirements;
- applicable security procedures; and
- other conditions established by the publisher or the organization.

#### 10.2 Authorized Remote Access Methods

Organizations may provide remote access using reasonable technical methods appropriate for secure institutional administration.

Such methods may include:

- institutional single sign-on systems;
- virtual private networks (VPNs);
- federated identity services;
- authenticated web portals;
- secure proxy services;
- managed authentication platforms; or
- other secure access technologies.

The specific technical implementation remains the responsibility of the organization unless otherwise provided by the applicable agreement.

#### 10.3 Security Requirements

Organizations should implement reasonable safeguards to protect remote access from unauthorized use.

Reasonable safeguards may include:

- secure authentication;
- encrypted communications;
- session management;
- device security requirements;
- account monitoring;
- access logging where appropriate; and
- other reasonable security measures.

Organizations remain responsible for administering remote access in a manner consistent with accepted information security practices.

#### 10.4 Responsibilities of Authorized Users

Authorized users accessing the Engineering Handbook Series remotely shall:

- protect their authentication credentials;
- use secure devices where reasonably practicable;
- avoid unauthorized sharing of access;
- comply with organizational security policies;
- report suspected unauthorized access where appropriate; and
- use the licensed publications only for authorized institutional purposes.

Remote access shall not exempt authorized users from any licensing obligations applicable to on-site access.

#### 10.5 Personal Devices

Where permitted by organizational policy, authorized users may access the Engineering Handbook Series using personally owned devices.

Organizations may establish reasonable requirements relating to:

- device security;
- authentication;
- software configuration;
- access controls;
- organizational policies; and
- protection of licensed materials.

The publisher assumes no responsibility for the security or management of personally owned devices.

#### 10.6 Geographic Access

Unless otherwise restricted by the applicable institutional license or applicable law, authorized users may access the Engineering Handbook Series from locations outside the organization's physical premises while acting within the scope of their authorized institutional activities.

The publisher may impose reasonable geographic restrictions where required by:

- licensing arrangements;
- applicable law;
- export controls;
- sanctions;
- governmental requirements; or
- other legal obligations.

#### 10.7 Temporary Loss of Remote Access

Remote access may be temporarily unavailable due to:

- system maintenance;
- security incidents;
- technical failures;
- authentication issues;
- organizational administrative actions;
- network disruptions; or
- other operational circumstances.

Temporary interruption of remote access shall not, by itself, constitute a breach of the institutional license or create an obligation for uninterrupted availability unless expressly provided by the applicable agreement.

#### 10.8 Unauthorized Remote Access

Organizations shall take reasonable steps to prevent unauthorized individuals from obtaining remote access to the Engineering Handbook Series.

Where unauthorized remote access is discovered, the organization should take appropriate corrective measures, which may include:

- disabling compromised accounts;
- resetting authentication credentials;
- investigating the incident;
- updating security controls; and
- notifying the publisher where appropriate under the applicable agreement.

#### 10.9 Remote Access Records

Organizations may maintain reasonable administrative records relating to remote access where necessary for:

- security administration;
- license management;
- compliance verification;
- troubleshooting;
- auditing;
- operational support; or
- other legitimate administrative purposes.

Any collection or processing of user information shall remain subject to applicable privacy laws and organizational privacy policies.

#### 10.10 Scope of Remote Access Rights

Remote access is an administrative method of accessing the Engineering Handbook Series and does not expand the rights granted under the institutional license.

All remote use remains subject to:

- the applicable institutional license agreement;
- this Manual;
- applicable copyright law;
- applicable intellectual property law; and
- all other governing legal and contractual obligations.

Any activity that would be prohibited when performed on the organization's premises remains equally prohibited when performed through remote or off-campus access.

### 11. Institutional Networks and Technical Deployment

Institutional licenses may permit deployment of the Engineering Handbook Series within approved organizational networks and technical environments, subject to the applicable institutional license agreement. Technical deployment shall support authorized institutional access while preserving the publisher's intellectual property rights and maintaining the security and integrity of licensed resources.

Nothing in this Section shall be interpreted as granting organizations ownership of the Engineering Handbook Series or authority to deploy the publications beyond the scope expressly authorized by the applicable institutional license.

#### 11.1 Approved Deployment Environments

Organizations may deploy the Engineering Handbook Series within approved institutional environments where permitted by the applicable license.

Approved deployment environments may include:

- institutional networks;
- campus networks;
- corporate intranets;
- authenticated internal portals;
- digital library systems;
- learning management systems;
- research platforms; and
- other organizational systems authorized by the applicable agreement.

Deployment outside approved environments requires the publisher's prior written authorization.

#### 11.2 Internal Network Access

Organizations may provide access through their internal networks to authorized users in accordance with the applicable institutional license.

Internal network deployment shall remain subject to:

- authorized user limitations;
- authentication requirements;
- organizational security controls;
- applicable user limits; and
- other licensing restrictions established by the publisher.

#### 11.3 Learning Management Systems

Educational institutions may integrate the Engineering Handbook Series with institutional learning management systems where expressly permitted by the applicable license.

Such integration shall be limited to authorized users and shall not permit unrestricted downloading, redistribution, republication, or public availability of the licensed publications.

The organization remains responsible for ensuring that learning management systems operate consistently with the applicable institutional license.

#### 11.4 Digital Library Integration

Libraries and eligible organizations may integrate licensed publications into authenticated digital library environments where authorized by the applicable agreement.

Digital library integration shall:

- restrict access to authorized users;
- preserve copyright and ownership notices;
- maintain applicable authentication controls;
- comply with user limitations; and
- operate within the scope of the institutional license.

#### 11.5 Cloud-Based Services

Organizations may utilize cloud-based infrastructure to administer authorized institutional access where consistent with the applicable institutional license and organizational security requirements.

Cloud deployment shall not:

- create publicly accessible copies;
- permit unauthorized third-party access;
- remove applicable licensing restrictions; or
- expand the rights granted under the institutional license.

Organizations remain responsible for selecting and administering secure cloud environments.

#### 11.6 Technical Protection Measures

Organizations shall not intentionally disable, interfere with, remove, or circumvent technical measures implemented to protect the Engineering Handbook Series.

Technical protection measures may include:

- authentication systems;
- authorization controls;
- access restrictions;
- digital watermarking;
- license verification mechanisms;
- encryption;
- usage controls; or
- other reasonable technical safeguards.

#### 11.7 System Maintenance

Organizations may perform reasonable technical maintenance necessary to administer institutional access.

Maintenance activities may include:

- authentication updates;
- network configuration;
- system migration;
- infrastructure upgrades;
- security improvements;
- backup administration; and
- other routine operational activities,

provided that such activities remain consistent with the applicable institutional license.

#### 11.8 Third-Party Service Providers

Organizations may engage third-party technology service providers to support the administration of institutional access where reasonably necessary.

Organizations remain responsible for ensuring that such providers:

- act solely on behalf of the organization;
- access licensed materials only as reasonably necessary to provide contracted services;
- maintain appropriate confidentiality and security protections; and
- do not obtain independent licensing rights under the institutional license.

Use of third-party service providers shall not transfer any rights granted under the institutional license.

#### 11.9 Technical Changes

The publisher may make reasonable technical changes to the delivery, authentication, security, administration, or deployment of the Engineering Handbook Series where necessary to:

- improve security;
- enhance performance;
- support new technologies;
- maintain compatibility;
- comply with legal requirements; or
- improve the institutional licensing program.

Reasonable technical changes shall not materially reduce the rights expressly granted under an active institutional license unless required by applicable law or the applicable agreement.

#### 11.10 Scope of Technical Deployment Rights

Technical deployment rights exist solely to facilitate authorized institutional access under the applicable institutional license.

Nothing in this Section authorizes organizations to:

- reproduce additional copies beyond those reasonably necessary for authorized deployment;
- distribute licensed publications outside the licensed organization;
- create derivative publishing systems;
- sublicense technical deployments;
- transfer deployment rights to third parties; or
- exercise any right not expressly granted under the applicable institutional license.

All technical deployment shall remain subject to this Manual, the applicable institutional license agreement, and all applicable copyright and intellectual property laws.

### 12. License Fees, Billing and Payment

Institutional licenses may be subject to license fees determined by the publisher in accordance with the applicable institutional licensing program. License fees compensate the publisher for the limited licensing rights granted under the applicable agreement and do not constitute the purchase or transfer of ownership of the Engineering Handbook Series.

Unless otherwise expressly agreed in writing, all institutional licensing fees are payable in accordance with the applicable license agreement and the publisher's then-current licensing policies.

#### 12.1 License Fees

Institutional license fees may vary depending upon factors including:

- license type;
- number of authorized users;
- licensed seats;
- departments covered;
- campuses covered;
- enterprise scope;
- duration of the license;
- organizational category; and
- other reasonable licensing factors determined by the publisher.

The publisher may revise institutional pricing for future licensing periods. Pricing revisions shall not affect active licenses unless expressly provided by the applicable agreement.

#### 12.2 Billing Arrangements

Institutional licenses may be billed using billing arrangements determined by the publisher and agreed upon by the institutional license holder.

Billing arrangements may include:

- one-time license fees;
- annual billing;
- multi-year billing;
- recurring subscription billing;
- installment arrangements where approved; or
- other billing models offered by the publisher.

The applicable license agreement shall govern the organization's billing obligations.

#### 12.3 Payment Terms

Institutional license holders shall pay all applicable licensing fees within the payment period specified in the applicable invoice or license agreement.

Unless otherwise agreed in writing:

- payment shall be made in the approved payment method;
- payments shall be made in the designated currency;
- organizations remain responsible for ensuring timely payment; and
- payment obligations survive administrative changes within the organization.

#### 12.4 Taxes and Government Charges

Unless expressly stated otherwise, license fees do not include applicable:

- taxes;
- duties;
- levies;
- governmental charges;
- withholding obligations; or
- similar statutory assessments.

Institutional license holders remain responsible for paying all applicable governmental charges associated with the institutional license except where the publisher is legally required to collect or remit such amounts.

#### 12.5 Purchase Orders

Where an organization requires the use of purchase orders or similar procurement documentation, such documentation shall be provided in accordance with the organization's procurement procedures.

Issuance of a purchase order shall not modify the publisher's licensing terms unless the publisher expressly agrees in writing.

Any conflicting terms contained within purchase orders or procurement documents shall not supersede this Manual or the applicable institutional license agreement unless expressly accepted by the publisher.

#### 12.6 Late Payments

Where payment is not received by the applicable due date, the publisher may take reasonable administrative measures, including:

- issuing payment reminders;
- temporarily withholding license activation;
- delaying license renewal;
- suspending administrative services;
- suspending access where permitted by the applicable agreement; or
- pursuing other remedies available under this Manual or applicable law.

The publisher may also recover reasonable collection costs where permitted by applicable law or the applicable agreement.

#### 12.7 Refunds

License fees are generally non-refundable unless:

- the applicable license agreement expressly provides otherwise;
- the publisher approves a refund in writing;
- applicable consumer protection law requires a refund; or
- applicable law otherwise mandates reimbursement.

Any approved refund shall be processed in accordance with the publisher's applicable refund procedures.

#### 12.8 Renewal Billing

Where institutional licenses are renewable, renewal invoices or billing notices may be issued prior to the expiration of the current licensing period.

Organizations remain responsible for reviewing renewal documentation and communicating any required licensing changes before renewal where reasonably practicable.

Failure to renew an institutional license may result in expiration of the licensed access rights.

#### 12.9 Billing Disputes

Organizations should notify the publisher within a reasonable period after discovering any billing error or invoice discrepancy.

Both parties should cooperate in good faith to investigate and resolve legitimate billing disputes as promptly as reasonably practicable.

Undisputed portions of an invoice shall remain payable in accordance with the applicable payment terms unless otherwise agreed in writing.

#### 12.10 Financial Responsibilities

Institutional license holders remain responsible for fulfilling all financial obligations arising under the applicable institutional license agreement.

Payment of license fees grants only the limited licensing rights expressly provided under the applicable agreement and shall not be interpreted as transferring ownership, copyright, publishing rights, or any intellectual property rights in the Engineering Handbook Series.

All ownership rights remain exclusively vested in the publisher unless expressly assigned by a separate written agreement.

### 13. License Term, Renewal and Expiration

Institutional licenses remain effective only for the period specified in the applicable institutional license agreement. Upon expiration of the license term, all licensing rights granted under the agreement shall cease unless the license is renewed or otherwise extended by the publisher.

The duration of an institutional license does not affect the publisher's ownership of the Engineering Handbook Series or any intellectual property rights associated with the publications.

#### 13.1 License Term

Each institutional license shall specify its effective commencement date and, where applicable, its expiration date.

Institutional licenses may be offered for:

- fixed terms;
- annual periods;
- multi-year periods;
- subscription-based durations; or
- other licensing periods established by the publisher.

The applicable institutional license agreement shall govern the duration of the license.

#### 13.2 Commencement of the License

Unless otherwise specified in the applicable agreement, an institutional license becomes effective upon the latest of:

- execution of the applicable license agreement;
- receipt of the applicable license fee;
- activation of licensed access by the publisher; or
- another effective date expressly stated in the agreement.

Access prior to the effective date is not authorized unless expressly approved by the publisher.

#### 13.3 Renewal

Institutional licenses may be renewed in accordance with the applicable license agreement and the publisher's licensing policies.

Renewal may require:

- submission of a renewal request;
- payment of applicable renewal fees;
- verification of organizational information;
- confirmation of licensing requirements; or
- completion of other reasonable renewal procedures established by the publisher.

Renewal creates a new licensing period and does not constitute a transfer of ownership or perpetual licensing rights.

#### 13.4 Renewal Modifications

At the time of renewal, the organization and the publisher may agree to modify the institutional license.

Modifications may include changes to:

- license type;
- authorized user limits;
- licensed seats;
- organizational scope;
- departments covered;
- campuses covered;
- pricing;
- administrative contacts; or
- other licensing terms.

Unless expressly agreed otherwise, all other provisions of the institutional license shall continue to apply during the renewed licensing period.

#### 13.5 Expiration of the License

Upon expiration of an institutional license, the organization's rights to access and use the Engineering Handbook Series shall terminate unless renewed or otherwise extended by the publisher.

Following expiration, organizations shall cease any further use of the licensed publications except where continued use is expressly authorized by:

- a renewed institutional license;
- another valid license;
- applicable law; or
- the publisher's written authorization.

Expiration does not affect obligations that expressly survive the end of the institutional license.

#### 13.6 Grace Periods

The publisher may, at its sole discretion, provide a temporary administrative grace period following license expiration.

A grace period:

- is not guaranteed;
- may be withdrawn at any time;
- does not constitute renewal;
- does not waive payment obligations; and
- shall not create any expectation of continued access for future licensing periods.

Any access provided during a grace period remains subject to this Manual and the applicable institutional license agreement.

#### 13.7 Failure to Renew

Where an institutional license is not renewed before its expiration, the publisher may:

- deactivate organizational access;
- disable authentication services;
- suspend administrative support associated with the expired license;
- archive licensing records; and
- take other reasonable administrative actions consistent with the expiration of the institutional license.

Failure to renew does not relieve the organization of any outstanding financial or legal obligations arising before expiration.

#### 13.8 Early Renewal

Organizations may request renewal before the expiration of the current institutional license where permitted by the publisher.

Early renewal shall not automatically extend the current license term unless expressly agreed in writing.

The publisher may determine the effective date of any early renewal in accordance with its licensing policies.

#### 13.9 Survival of Certain Provisions

Expiration or non-renewal of an institutional license shall not affect provisions of this Manual or the applicable agreement that are intended to survive expiration.

Such provisions may include those relating to:

- copyright ownership;
- intellectual property rights;
- confidentiality;
- payment obligations;
- limitation of liability;
- dispute resolution;
- governing law;
- record retention; and
- other provisions that by their nature survive expiration.

#### 13.10 Effect of Renewal and Expiration

Renewal restores licensing rights only for the renewed licensing period and only to the extent provided by the renewed institutional license.

Expiration or non-renewal terminates the organization's licensed access but does not transfer ownership of the Engineering Handbook Series, extinguish the publisher's intellectual property rights, or authorize continued use beyond the scope expressly permitted by applicable law or a renewed license.

All rights not expressly granted remain reserved by the publisher.

### 14. Suspension and Termination of Institutional Licenses

The publisher may suspend or terminate an institutional license in accordance with the applicable license agreement, this Manual, or applicable law. Suspension and termination are administrative and contractual remedies intended to protect the publisher's intellectual property rights, maintain the integrity of the institutional licensing program, and ensure compliance with licensing obligations.

Unless otherwise required by applicable law or expressly provided in the applicable agreement, the publisher retains discretion regarding the appropriate administrative response to non-compliance.

#### 14.1 Grounds for Suspension

The publisher may suspend an institutional license where there are reasonable grounds to believe that the organization has:

- materially violated the institutional license agreement;
- exceeded authorized licensing rights;
- failed to satisfy applicable payment obligations;
- permitted significant unauthorized access;
- engaged in prohibited use;
- provided materially inaccurate licensing information; or
- otherwise materially failed to comply with this Manual.

Suspension may be temporary while the relevant matter is investigated or resolved.

#### 14.2 Grounds for Termination

The publisher may terminate an institutional license where:

- material breaches remain unremedied after a reasonable opportunity to cure, where appropriate;
- repeated violations demonstrate persistent non-compliance;
- fraudulent conduct materially affects the licensing relationship;
- the organization intentionally infringes the publisher's intellectual property rights;
- continued licensing is prohibited by applicable law; or
- termination is otherwise authorized under the applicable institutional license agreement.

Termination shall not be exercised arbitrarily and shall be based upon legitimate contractual, legal, or administrative grounds.

#### 14.3 Temporary Suspension

During a period of suspension, the publisher may:

- disable organizational access;
- suspend remote access;
- deactivate authentication services;
- restrict administrative functions;
- temporarily withhold support services; or
- implement other reasonable measures necessary to administer the suspension.

Suspension does not automatically terminate the institutional license unless termination subsequently occurs.

#### 14.4 Notice of Suspension or Termination

Where reasonably practicable, the publisher should provide notice of suspension or termination identifying:

- the general basis for the action;
- the effective date;
- any corrective measures, where applicable;
- available administrative procedures; and
- other information reasonably necessary for the organization to understand the action.

Nothing in this Section prevents immediate suspension where necessary to protect the publisher's rights, security, or legal interests.

#### 14.5 Opportunity to Remedy

Where appropriate and consistent with the nature of the non-compliance, the publisher may provide the organization with a reasonable opportunity to remedy the issue before terminating the institutional license.

The availability of an opportunity to remedy shall depend upon factors including:

- the seriousness of the breach;
- prior compliance history;
- the likelihood of successful remediation;
- protection of intellectual property rights; and
- other relevant circumstances.

The publisher is not obligated to provide an opportunity to remedy where immediate action is reasonably necessary.

#### 14.6 Effect of Termination

Upon termination of an institutional license:

- all licensed access rights shall cease;
- authorized user access may be disabled;
- remote access rights shall terminate;
- institutional authentication may be deactivated;
- administrative support associated with the license may cease; and
- any continued use of the Engineering Handbook Series shall require a separate valid license or other lawful authorization.

Termination does not affect obligations intended to survive termination.

#### 14.7 Organizational Responsibilities Following Termination

Following termination, the organization shall:

- discontinue use of the Engineering Handbook Series;
- remove access for authorized users;
- cease any unauthorized distribution;
- comply with any applicable post-termination obligations contained in the license agreement; and
- cooperate with reasonable administrative measures relating to the terminated license.

Nothing in this Section requires destruction of records where retention is required by applicable law or other surviving legal obligations.

#### 14.8 Voluntary Termination

An institutional license holder may request termination of its institutional license in accordance with the applicable agreement.

Voluntary termination:

- does not automatically entitle the organization to a refund;
- does not relieve accrued payment obligations;
- remains subject to applicable contractual provisions; and
- becomes effective in accordance with the applicable agreement or the publisher's written confirmation.

#### 14.9 Survival of Rights and Obligations

Termination of an institutional license shall not affect:

- the publisher's ownership of the Engineering Handbook Series;
- accrued payment obligations;
- intellectual property rights;
- confidentiality obligations;
- dispute resolution provisions;
- limitation of liability provisions;
- record retention obligations where applicable; or
- any other provisions intended to survive termination.

Such provisions shall continue to operate in accordance with this Manual and the applicable institutional license agreement.

#### 14.10 No Waiver of Other Remedies

Suspension or termination of an institutional license does not limit any other contractual, administrative, equitable, or legal remedies available to the publisher under this Manual, the applicable institutional license agreement, or applicable law.

The exercise of one remedy shall not prevent the publisher from exercising any other rights or remedies available in relation to the same or related matters.

### 15. Compliance, Monitoring and License Verification

Institutional license holders are responsible for ensuring that their use of the Engineering Handbook Series remains consistent with the applicable institutional license agreement, this Manual, and applicable law. Reasonable compliance measures help maintain the integrity of the institutional licensing program while protecting the rights of both the publisher and licensed organizations.

Compliance activities shall be conducted in a fair, reasonable, and proportionate manner consistent with applicable legal and contractual obligations.

#### 15.1 Organizational Compliance

Institutional license holders shall take reasonable steps to ensure that:

- access is limited to authorized users;
- user limits are observed;
- licensed materials are used only for permitted purposes;
- prohibited activities are prevented where reasonably practicable;
- administrative records remain reasonably accurate; and
- organizational licensing policies remain consistent with the applicable institutional license.

Organizations remain responsible for compliance throughout the duration of the institutional license.

#### 15.2 Internal Monitoring

Organizations may conduct reasonable internal monitoring to assist with the administration of their institutional licenses.

Internal monitoring may include:

- user account reviews;
- access verification;
- seat utilization reviews;
- authentication reviews;
- security monitoring;
- administrative record verification; and
- other reasonable internal compliance activities.

Internal monitoring should be conducted in accordance with applicable privacy laws and organizational policies.

#### 15.3 Publisher Verification

The publisher may request reasonable information necessary to verify that an institutional license is being administered in accordance with the applicable agreement.

Verification requests may relate to:

- organizational eligibility;
- license type;
- authorized user limits;
- institutional contact information;
- organizational structure;
- licensing scope;
- payment status; or
- other information reasonably necessary for license administration.

Verification requests shall be limited to information reasonably relevant to the administration of the institutional license.

#### 15.4 Compliance Reviews

Where reasonably necessary, the publisher may conduct administrative compliance reviews to verify continued compliance with institutional licensing requirements.

Compliance reviews may include examination of:

- licensing records;
- organizational information;
- user allocations;
- license administration procedures;
- access management practices; and
- other information directly relevant to the institutional license.

Compliance reviews shall be conducted in a commercially reasonable manner and with reasonable regard for the organization's normal operations.

#### 15.5 Cooperation

Institutional license holders should cooperate in good faith with reasonable compliance or verification requests made by the publisher.

Reasonable cooperation may include:

- providing requested documentation;
- confirming licensing information;
- correcting administrative inaccuracies;
- designating appropriate organizational representatives; and
- responding within a reasonable period.

Nothing in this Section requires disclosure of information protected by applicable law, legal privilege, or contractual confidentiality obligations owed to third parties.

#### 15.6 Correction of Non-Compliance

Where non-compliance is identified, organizations should take reasonable corrective action as promptly as reasonably practicable.

Corrective actions may include:

- updating user records;
- removing unauthorized access;
- correcting administrative errors;
- upgrading the institutional license where appropriate;
- strengthening internal controls; or
- implementing other reasonable remedial measures.

Prompt corrective action may be considered by the publisher when determining the appropriate administrative response.

#### 15.7 Record Retention

Organizations should retain licensing records for a reasonable period consistent with:

- the applicable institutional license agreement;
- applicable law;
- organizational record retention policies; and
- legitimate administrative requirements.

The publisher may also retain licensing records for administrative, legal, financial, and operational purposes in accordance with applicable law and its record retention policies.

#### 15.8 Confidentiality of Compliance Information

Information obtained during compliance reviews or license verification shall be handled in accordance with:

- applicable privacy laws;
- confidentiality obligations;
- applicable contractual provisions; and
- the publisher's legitimate business requirements.

The publisher shall use compliance information only for legitimate licensing, administrative, legal, operational, or enforcement purposes unless otherwise required by applicable law.

#### 15.9 Good Faith Administration

Both the publisher and institutional license holders should administer compliance activities in good faith.

Compliance measures should promote:

- accurate license administration;
- protection of intellectual property;
- fair treatment of licensed organizations;
- responsible use of licensed publications; and
- long-term sustainability of the institutional licensing program.

Compliance activities are intended to support lawful licensing rather than unnecessarily interfere with the legitimate operations of institutional license holders.

#### 15.10 Effect of Non-Compliance

Failure to comply with the applicable institutional license agreement or this Manual may result in appropriate administrative, contractual, or legal action, including:

- requests for corrective action;
- suspension of licensed access;
- termination of the institutional license;
- recovery of applicable fees or damages where permitted by law; or
- other remedies available under this Manual, the applicable institutional license agreement, or applicable law.

Nothing in this Section limits any rights or remedies otherwise available to the publisher.

### 16. Privacy, Confidentiality and Data Protection

The administration of institutional licenses may require the collection, processing, storage, and use of certain organizational and user information. Both the publisher and institutional license holders shall handle such information in accordance with applicable privacy laws, contractual obligations, and recognized principles of responsible information management.

Nothing in this Section authorizes either party to collect or process personal information beyond what is reasonably necessary for the administration of the institutional license.

#### 16.1 Privacy Principles

The publisher and institutional license holders should process personal and organizational information in a manner that is:

- lawful;
- fair;
- transparent where appropriate;
- limited to legitimate purposes;
- proportionate to operational requirements;
- reasonably accurate;
- appropriately secured; and
- retained only for as long as reasonably necessary or required by applicable law.

#### 16.2 Information Collected

Information processed for institutional license administration may include:

- organizational identification information;
- administrative contact information;
- authorized user information;
- licensing records;
- authentication information;
- billing information;
- payment records;
- technical access information; and
- other information reasonably necessary for administering the institutional license.

The specific categories of information processed shall depend upon the applicable licensing arrangement.

#### 16.3 Purpose of Processing

Information collected under an institutional license may be processed for legitimate purposes including:

- license administration;
- authentication;
- access management;
- billing and payment administration;
- customer support;
- compliance verification;
- security administration;
- legal compliance;
- operational improvement; and
- other purposes reasonably related to the administration of the institutional license.

Information shall not be processed for purposes materially inconsistent with the applicable license agreement unless otherwise permitted by applicable law.

#### 16.4 Confidential Information

Each party shall treat confidential information received from the other party with reasonable care.

Confidential information may include:

- licensing agreements;
- pricing information;
- technical deployment details;
- authentication systems;
- organizational records;
- business information;
- security procedures; and
- other information identified as confidential or reasonably understood to be confidential.

Confidential information shall not be disclosed except:

- with the consent of the disclosing party;
- where reasonably necessary for administration of the institutional license;
- where disclosure is required by applicable law; or
- as otherwise permitted by the applicable agreement.

#### 16.5 Information Security

Both the publisher and institutional license holders should implement reasonable administrative, technical, and organizational measures designed to protect information against:

- unauthorized access;
- unauthorized disclosure;
- accidental loss;
- destruction;
- alteration;
- misuse; or
- other reasonably foreseeable security risks.

The specific security measures adopted shall depend upon the nature of the information being processed and the operational requirements of each party.

#### 16.6 Third-Party Service Providers

Either party may engage third-party service providers to support legitimate operational activities relating to the institutional license.

Where third-party providers process information on behalf of a party, that party remains responsible for ensuring that such providers:

- process information only for authorized purposes;
- implement appropriate security measures;
- maintain confidentiality;
- comply with applicable legal obligations; and
- act consistently with the applicable contractual arrangements.

Engagement of third-party providers does not transfer ownership of the information processed.

#### 16.7 Legal Disclosure

Nothing in this Manual prevents either party from disclosing information where disclosure is required by:

- applicable law;
- a valid court order;
- lawful governmental authority;
- regulatory requirements; or
- another legally binding obligation.

Where legally permissible, the receiving party should provide reasonable notice to the other party before making such disclosure.

#### 16.8 Data Retention and Disposal

Information collected for institutional license administration should be retained only for:

- the duration reasonably necessary to administer the institutional license;
- compliance with legal obligations;
- resolution of disputes;
- enforcement of contractual rights;
- financial recordkeeping; or
- other legitimate operational purposes.

When information is no longer required, it should be securely deleted, anonymized, archived, or otherwise disposed of in accordance with applicable law and established retention policies.

#### 16.9 Cross-Border Processing

Where institutional licensing activities involve multiple jurisdictions, the processing of information shall remain subject to applicable data protection laws governing the relevant jurisdictions.

The publisher and institutional license holders shall take reasonable steps to ensure that international transfers of information, where applicable, comply with relevant legal requirements.

#### 16.10 Privacy and Confidentiality Obligations

Privacy, confidentiality, and data protection obligations continue throughout the duration of the institutional license and, where applicable, after its expiration or termination to the extent required by:

- applicable law;
- contractual obligations;
- confidentiality commitments;
- surviving provisions of the institutional license; or
- this Manual.

Nothing in this Section transfers ownership of organizational information, personal information, or intellectual property unless expressly provided by a separate written agreement.

### 17. Institutional License Transfer, Assignment and Organizational Changes

Institutional licenses are granted to the specific organization identified in the applicable institutional license agreement. Unless expressly authorized by the publisher in writing, institutional licenses are personal to the licensed organization and may not be transferred, assigned, sublicensed, or otherwise conveyed to another legal entity.

Nothing in this Section shall be interpreted as transferring ownership of the Engineering Handbook Series or any associated intellectual property rights.

#### 17.1 General Restriction on Transfer

Institutional licenses shall not be:

- assigned;
- transferred;
- sold;
- sublicensed;
- pledged;
- leased;
- licensed onward; or
- otherwise conveyed,

without the publisher's prior written approval.

Any purported transfer made without such approval shall be void to the extent permitted by applicable law.

#### 17.2 Assignment Requests

An institutional license holder may request the publisher's approval for the assignment or transfer of an institutional license.

The publisher may consider factors including:

- the identity of the proposed assignee;
- organizational continuity;
- licensing eligibility;
- compliance history;
- payment status;
- operational requirements; and
- any other circumstances reasonably relevant to the licensing relationship.

The publisher may approve, refuse, or approve subject to reasonable conditions.

#### 17.3 Mergers and Acquisitions

Where an institutional license holder is involved in a merger, acquisition, consolidation, or similar corporate transaction, the organization shall notify the publisher within a reasonable period where the transaction may materially affect the institutional license.

The publisher may determine whether:

- the existing license may continue;
- the license requires modification;
- a new institutional license is required; or
- additional licensing conditions should apply.

Continuation of an institutional license following a merger or acquisition shall not be automatic unless expressly confirmed by the publisher.

#### 17.4 Organizational Restructuring

Where an organization undergoes internal restructuring, including:

- departmental reorganization;
- institutional renaming;
- division of organizational units;
- creation of additional campuses;
- consolidation of departments; or
- similar operational changes,

the organization should notify the publisher where such changes materially affect the scope of the institutional license.

The publisher may require reasonable modifications to ensure that the institutional license accurately reflects the organization's revised structure.

#### 17.5 Change of Legal Identity

Where the legal identity of the institutional license holder changes due to incorporation, conversion, legal reorganization, or similar legal events, the organization shall notify the publisher.

The publisher may require updated:

- legal documentation;
- licensing information;
- billing information;
- administrative records; or
- execution of a replacement institutional license.

A change of legal identity does not automatically transfer licensing rights to the successor entity.

#### 17.6 Internal Administrative Changes

Routine internal administrative changes that do not alter the legal identity of the institutional license holder may generally be implemented without requiring a new institutional license.

Examples include:

- appointment of new license administrators;
- changes to departmental contacts;
- organizational email updates;
- internal reporting changes;
- administrative restructuring; or
- other operational adjustments.

Organizations should maintain reasonably current licensing information following such changes.

#### 17.7 Successor Organizations

Where the publisher approves continuation of an institutional license following an approved organizational transition, the successor organization shall assume the applicable rights and obligations specified by the publisher or contained within the revised institutional license agreement.

The scope of any approved continuation shall be determined solely by the publisher's written authorization.

#### 17.8 Effect of Unauthorized Transfer

An unauthorized transfer, assignment, sublicense, or attempted conveyance of an institutional license may constitute a material breach of the applicable institutional license agreement.

The publisher may respond by taking appropriate administrative, contractual, or legal action, including:

- refusing recognition of the purported transfer;
- suspending licensed access;
- terminating the institutional license;
- requiring execution of a new license; or
- exercising any other available rights or remedies.

#### 17.9 Publisher Reorganization

A reorganization, merger, acquisition, assignment, or transfer affecting the publisher shall not invalidate existing institutional licenses unless continuation becomes legally or operationally impossible.

Any successor to the publisher's publishing business may administer institutional licenses in accordance with applicable law and the existing licensing framework.

#### 17.10 Continuity of Licensing Rights

Institutional licensing rights continue only for the licensed organization identified in the applicable agreement and only for the duration and scope expressly authorized by the publisher.

No organizational change, corporate transaction, internal restructuring, or legal event shall expand, transfer, or create additional licensing rights except to the extent expressly approved by the publisher in writing or otherwise required by applicable law.

### 18. Institutional Support and Customer Services

The publisher may provide administrative, technical, and customer support services to institutional license holders in accordance with the applicable institutional license agreement, the publisher's support policies, and available operational resources.

Support services are intended to facilitate the effective administration and use of the Engineering Handbook Series and shall not be interpreted as creating obligations beyond those expressly assumed by the publisher.

#### 18.1 Scope of Support

Subject to the applicable institutional license, the publisher may provide support relating to:

- license administration;
- account management;
- authentication assistance;
- access issues;
- billing inquiries;
- renewal assistance;
- technical guidance;
- licensing clarification; and
- other reasonable support relating to the institutional licensing program.

The availability and scope of support may vary according to the applicable institutional license.

#### 18.2 Designated Organizational Contacts

Support requests should ordinarily be submitted by the designated license administrator or another authorized organizational representative.

The publisher may require reasonable verification of the requester's authority before discussing institutional licensing matters or making administrative changes.

#### 18.3 Technical Assistance

Where appropriate, the publisher may provide reasonable technical assistance concerning:

- account activation;
- authentication issues;
- access configuration;
- institutional deployment;
- compatibility questions;
- license activation;
- remote access administration; and
- other technical matters directly related to the Engineering Handbook Series.

Technical assistance does not include administration of the organization's internal information technology infrastructure unless expressly agreed in writing.

#### 18.4 Response Times

The publisher shall make commercially reasonable efforts to respond to support requests within a reasonable period.

Response times may vary depending upon:

- the nature of the request;
- operational workload;
- business hours;
- system availability;
- request complexity; and
- other operational considerations.

Nothing in this Section guarantees any specific response or resolution time unless expressly agreed in writing.

#### 18.5 Organizational Responsibilities

Institutional license holders remain responsible for:

- administering their internal systems;
- managing authorized users;
- maintaining organizational authentication systems;
- providing accurate licensing information;
- performing internal troubleshooting where appropriate; and
- cooperating with the publisher during support activities.

The publisher is not responsible for issues arising solely from the organization's internal systems or third-party infrastructure.

#### 18.6 Maintenance Communications

The publisher may issue support notices regarding:

- scheduled maintenance;
- software updates;
- security advisories;
- service interruptions;
- licensing changes;
- authentication updates;
- policy revisions; or
- other operational matters.

Organizations should ensure that designated administrative contacts remain able to receive such communications.

#### 18.7 Support Limitations

Unless expressly included within the applicable institutional license, the publisher is not obligated to provide:

- on-site technical services;
- custom software development;
- internal network administration;
- institutional IT consulting;
- user training beyond standard documentation;
- integration with third-party systems; or
- other professional services.

Such services may be provided only under a separate written agreement.

#### 18.8 Third-Party Technologies

Where institutional access utilizes third-party technologies or services, the publisher may provide reasonable assistance relating to integration with the Engineering Handbook Series.

However, the publisher does not assume responsibility for:

- third-party software;
- third-party infrastructure;
- internet connectivity;
- cloud service availability;
- organizational IT systems; or
- products or services supplied by independent third parties.

#### 18.9 Support Records

The publisher may maintain records relating to support requests for purposes including:

- service improvement;
- quality assurance;
- license administration;
- technical troubleshooting;
- compliance;
- dispute resolution; and
- operational management.

Support records shall be handled in accordance with applicable privacy and confidentiality obligations.

#### 18.10 Support Services

Support services are provided solely to facilitate the administration and lawful use of institutional licenses.

The provision of support shall not modify the applicable institutional license, expand the rights granted under the license, create additional warranties, or transfer any ownership or intellectual property rights relating to the Engineering Handbook Series.

### 19. Accessibility and Inclusive Access

The publisher is committed to making the Engineering Handbook Series reasonably accessible to a broad range of readers and institutional users. Institutional licensing shall, where reasonably practicable, support accessibility, inclusive learning, and equitable access while respecting applicable copyright laws and the publisher's intellectual property rights.

Nothing in this Section requires the publisher to provide accessibility features beyond those required by applicable law or expressly included within the applicable institutional license.

#### 19.1 Accessibility Principles

The publisher shall make commercially reasonable efforts to support accessibility through appropriate publishing practices, technological improvements, and ongoing evaluation of accessibility requirements.

Accessibility initiatives should seek to:

- improve usability;
- support inclusive education;
- reduce unnecessary barriers to access;
- facilitate lawful access for eligible users; and
- promote equitable availability of educational resources.

#### 19.2 Accessibility Features

Where reasonably practicable, the Engineering Handbook Series may incorporate accessibility features such as:

- searchable digital text;
- selectable text;
- structured headings;
- navigational bookmarks;
- alternative text for illustrations where appropriate;
- accessible document structure;
- compatibility with assistive technologies; and
- other reasonable accessibility enhancements.

The availability of particular accessibility features may vary depending upon the publication format, edition, or technical platform.

#### 19.3 Compatibility with Assistive Technologies

Where reasonably practicable, digital editions of the Engineering Handbook Series should be designed to support compatibility with commonly used assistive technologies.

Such technologies may include:

- screen readers;
- screen magnification software;
- text-to-speech systems;
- keyboard navigation tools;
- alternative input devices; and
- other accessibility technologies.

The publisher does not guarantee compatibility with every device, platform, operating system, or assistive technology.

#### 19.4 Institutional Accessibility Responsibilities

Institutional license holders remain responsible for providing accessible access within their own technological environments.

Organizations should:

- implement appropriate accessibility policies;
- configure institutional systems to support accessibility where reasonably practicable;
- assist authorized users in accessing available accessibility features; and
- comply with applicable accessibility laws governing their operations.

#### 19.5 Accessible Formats

Where reasonably practicable and consistent with applicable law, the publisher may provide or authorize accessible versions of the Engineering Handbook Series for eligible users.

The availability of accessible formats shall depend upon:

- technical feasibility;
- legal requirements;
- publishing resources;
- applicable licensing arrangements; and
- operational considerations.

Provision of accessible formats shall not authorize unauthorized reproduction or redistribution of the Engineering Handbook Series.

#### 19.6 Reasonable Accommodation Requests

Institutional license holders may submit reasonable requests relating to accessibility where necessary to support eligible authorized users.

The publisher shall consider such requests in good faith while taking into account:

- technical feasibility;
- legal obligations;
- intellectual property protection;
- operational capabilities; and
- the availability of reasonable alternative solutions.

Approval of any accommodation remains at the publisher's discretion unless otherwise required by applicable law.

#### 19.7 Preservation of Intellectual Property

Accessibility measures shall not be interpreted as authorizing:

- unrestricted copying;
- removal of copyright notices;
- unauthorized redistribution;
- public dissemination;
- creation of competing publications; or
- any activity exceeding the applicable institutional license.

All accessible versions of the Engineering Handbook Series remain protected by copyright and all other applicable intellectual property rights.

#### 19.8 Continuous Improvement

The publisher may periodically review accessibility practices to improve the usability and inclusiveness of future editions of the Engineering Handbook Series.

Such improvements may include:

- enhanced document structure;
- improved navigation;
- expanded compatibility;
- updated accessibility technologies;
- revised publishing workflows; and
- other reasonable accessibility enhancements.

Nothing in this Section obligates the publisher to retrofit previously published editions unless otherwise required by applicable law.

#### 19.9 Applicable Laws

Accessibility obligations shall be interpreted consistently with:

- applicable disability laws;
- accessibility regulations;
- educational accessibility requirements;
- applicable copyright law;
- intellectual property law; and
- other applicable legal requirements.

Where applicable law imposes greater accessibility obligations than those described in this Manual, the applicable law shall prevail to the extent of the inconsistency.

#### 19.10 Inclusive Access

The publisher and institutional license holders share a common objective of promoting lawful, inclusive, and equitable access to the Engineering Handbook Series.

Accessibility initiatives shall be implemented in a manner that balances the legitimate needs of users requiring accessible access with the publisher's responsibility to protect its intellectual property rights, maintain the integrity of the publications, and administer institutional licenses fairly and consistently.

### 20. Service Availability, Maintenance and Technical Interruptions

The publisher shall make commercially reasonable efforts to provide reliable access to the Engineering Handbook Series throughout the duration of an active institutional license. However, uninterrupted availability cannot be guaranteed, and temporary interruptions may occur due to maintenance, technical issues, security requirements, or circumstances beyond the publisher's reasonable control.

Nothing in this Section creates a guarantee of continuous, uninterrupted, or error-free access unless expressly provided by a separate written agreement.

#### 20.1 Service Availability

The publisher shall make commercially reasonable efforts to maintain the availability of licensed services consistent with the nature of the institutional licensing program.

Service availability may be affected by:

- scheduled maintenance;
- software updates;
- infrastructure upgrades;
- security measures;
- technical failures;
- third-party service interruptions; or
- circumstances beyond the publisher's reasonable control.

#### 20.2 Scheduled Maintenance

The publisher may periodically perform scheduled maintenance to:

- improve system performance;
- enhance security;
- deploy updates;
- correct technical issues;
- upgrade infrastructure;
- improve compatibility; or
- maintain operational reliability.

Where reasonably practicable, advance notice of significant scheduled maintenance may be provided to institutional license holders.

#### 20.3 Emergency Maintenance

The publisher may perform emergency maintenance without prior notice where reasonably necessary to:

- address security vulnerabilities;
- respond to cyber incidents;
- prevent data loss;
- restore operational stability;
- protect intellectual property;
- comply with legal obligations; or
- address other urgent technical circumstances.

Emergency maintenance shall be limited to the extent reasonably necessary to resolve the relevant issue.

#### 20.4 Technical Interruptions

Temporary interruptions may result from:

- hardware failures;
- software defects;
- telecommunications failures;
- internet disruptions;
- cloud infrastructure issues;
- authentication failures;
- power outages; or
- other operational events.

The publisher shall make commercially reasonable efforts to restore services within a reasonable period following discovery of the interruption.

#### 20.5 Third-Party Dependencies

Certain aspects of institutional access may depend upon services provided by independent third parties.

Such dependencies may include:

- internet service providers;
- cloud infrastructure providers;
- authentication providers;
- domain name services;
- content delivery networks;
- payment processors; or
- other external technology providers.

The publisher shall not be responsible for interruptions arising solely from failures of independent third-party services beyond the publisher's reasonable control.

#### 20.6 Organizational Responsibilities

Institutional license holders remain responsible for maintaining their own:

- network infrastructure;
- internet connectivity;
- authentication systems;
- organizational devices;
- internal security;
- software compatibility; and
- local technical environments.

Technical issues originating within the organization's own systems do not constitute failures of the publisher's services.

#### 20.7 Software Updates

The publisher may periodically update software, security mechanisms, authentication procedures, or technical platforms supporting the Engineering Handbook Series.

Organizations should cooperate with reasonable technical changes necessary to maintain secure and effective institutional access.

Software updates shall not materially reduce the licensing rights expressly granted under an active institutional license unless required by applicable law or the applicable agreement.

#### 20.8 Temporary Suspension of Services

The publisher may temporarily suspend all or part of the institutional service where reasonably necessary for:

- maintenance;
- security;
- operational stability;
- legal compliance;
- infrastructure migration;
- disaster recovery; or
- protection of the publisher's systems or intellectual property.

Temporary service suspension under this Section shall not, by itself, constitute termination of the institutional license.

#### 20.9 No Guaranteed Uptime

Unless expressly agreed in writing, the publisher does not guarantee:

- uninterrupted availability;
- continuous operation;
- specific uptime percentages;
- immediate restoration following interruptions;
- compatibility with every technological environment; or
- uninterrupted access during maintenance periods.

The publisher's obligations are limited to making commercially reasonable efforts to provide reliable institutional access.

#### 20.10 Effect of Service Interruptions

Temporary interruptions in service shall not:

- transfer ownership of the Engineering Handbook Series;
- expand institutional licensing rights;
- waive applicable licensing restrictions;
- create additional intellectual property rights;
- excuse compliance with this Manual; or
- modify the applicable institutional license agreement.

Both the publisher and institutional license holders shall cooperate in good faith to minimize the impact of significant technical interruptions and to restore authorized access as reasonably practicable.

### 21. Intellectual Property within Institutional Environments

The grant of an institutional license does not transfer ownership of the Engineering Handbook Series or any associated intellectual property rights. All copyrights, trademarks, database rights, design rights, trade secrets, and other intellectual property rights remain exclusively owned by the publisher or the applicable rights holders unless expressly assigned by a separate written agreement.

Institutional license holders and authorized users receive only the limited licensing rights expressly granted under the applicable institutional license agreement.

#### 21.1 Ownership of Intellectual Property

The publisher retains exclusive ownership of all intellectual property rights relating to the Engineering Handbook Series, including:

- copyright;
- publishing rights;
- trademarks;
- service marks;
- trade dress;
- database rights;
- design rights;
- compilation rights;
- editorial content; and
- all other proprietary rights.

Nothing contained in an institutional license shall be interpreted as assigning or transferring ownership of any intellectual property to the institutional license holder or any authorized user.

#### 21.2 Institutional License Does Not Create Ownership

Payment of institutional license fees or lawful access to the Engineering Handbook Series does not create:

- ownership rights;
- co-ownership rights;
- publishing rights;
- editorial rights;
- copyright interests;
- trademark rights;
- database ownership; or
- any other proprietary interest.

Institutional licenses grant only limited rights of access and use in accordance with the applicable agreement.

#### 21.3 Preservation of Copyright Notices

Organizations and authorized users shall preserve all:

- copyright notices;
- ownership notices;
- publisher identifications;
- attribution statements;
- licensing notices;
- digital watermarks; and
- other proprietary markings,

appearing in the Engineering Handbook Series.

Such notices shall not be removed, obscured, altered, or replaced except where expressly authorized by the publisher or required by applicable law.

#### 21.4 Institutional Materials

Nothing in this Manual grants the publisher ownership of materials independently created by the institutional license holder.

Organizations retain ownership of:

- internal teaching materials;
- institutional policies;
- independently created research;
- organizational documentation;
- internal presentations;
- administrative records; and
- other materials created independently of the Engineering Handbook Series.

Ownership of institutional materials does not authorize incorporation of copyrighted content from the Engineering Handbook Series beyond the rights expressly granted under the applicable institutional license.

#### 21.5 User-Created Notes and Annotations

Authorized users may create personal notes, highlights, bookmarks, annotations, and similar study materials for their own lawful institutional use where permitted by the applicable license.

Such notes remain the property of their creators.

However, user-created notes shall not be used as a means of reproducing or redistributing substantial portions of the Engineering Handbook Series in a manner inconsistent with this Manual or the applicable institutional license.

#### 21.6 Feedback and Suggestions

Organizations and authorized users may voluntarily provide suggestions, recommendations, comments, or other feedback regarding the Engineering Handbook Series.

Unless otherwise agreed in writing, the publisher may use such feedback for purposes including:

- improving future editions;
- correcting errors;
- enhancing accessibility;
- improving technical systems;
- refining licensing programs; or
- developing related publications.

Providing feedback does not entitle the contributor to ownership, compensation, editorial control, or authorship unless expressly agreed by the publisher in writing.

#### 21.7 Institutional Branding

Nothing in the institutional license authorizes organizations to:

- represent themselves as the publisher;
- use the publisher's trademarks beyond lawful nominative reference;
- imply publisher endorsement;
- create misleading branding;
- alter publisher logos; or
- otherwise misrepresent the relationship between the organization and the publisher.

Any authorized use of the publisher's branding shall comply with the publisher's applicable branding policies.

#### 21.8 Derivative Intellectual Property

Organizations and authorized users shall not create or distribute derivative publications that substantially reproduce or adapt the Engineering Handbook Series except where expressly authorized by the publisher or permitted by applicable law.

Independent works that merely reference or properly cite the Engineering Handbook Series shall not be considered prohibited derivative publications solely for that reason.

#### 21.9 Protection of Intellectual Property

Institutional license holders should take reasonable measures to respect and protect the publisher's intellectual property rights by:

- limiting access to authorized users;
- preventing unauthorized copying;
- discouraging unlawful redistribution;
- maintaining copyright notices;
- reporting significant infringements where appropriate; and
- cooperating with reasonable intellectual property protection measures.

These responsibilities support the continued availability and sustainability of the Engineering Handbook Series.

#### 21.10 Reservation of Rights

Except for the limited licensing rights expressly granted under the applicable institutional license agreement, all rights relating to the Engineering Handbook Series remain exclusively reserved by the publisher.

No implied license, waiver, assignment, transfer, estoppel, or other legal doctrine shall be interpreted as granting additional intellectual property rights unless expressly stated in a written agreement signed by the publisher.

### 22. Security Incidents, Breach Reporting and Incident Response

Institutional license holders and the publisher share a common interest in maintaining the security, integrity, and lawful administration of the Engineering Handbook Series. Where security incidents affect institutional licensing, both parties should act promptly, reasonably, and in good faith to mitigate risks, restore authorized access where appropriate, and protect intellectual property rights.

Nothing in this Section creates obligations beyond those imposed by the applicable institutional license agreement or applicable law.

#### 22.1 Security Incidents

A security incident includes any event that may reasonably compromise:

- authorized access;
- authentication credentials;
- institutional accounts;
- licensing information;
- technical protection measures;
- confidential licensing information; or
- the secure administration of the Engineering Handbook Series.

A security incident does not necessarily constitute a legal breach or data breach under applicable law.

#### 22.2 Organizational Responsibilities

Institutional license holders should establish reasonable procedures for responding to security incidents affecting institutional access.

Reasonable procedures may include:

- identifying affected systems;
- limiting unauthorized access;
- protecting authentication credentials;
- preserving relevant records;
- restoring secure operations; and
- implementing reasonable corrective measures.

Organizations remain responsible for incidents arising within their own information technology environments.

#### 22.3 Publisher Responsibilities

Where security incidents affect systems operated by the publisher, the publisher shall make commercially reasonable efforts to:

- investigate the incident;
- contain the impact;
- restore services where reasonably practicable;
- protect intellectual property;
- implement appropriate corrective measures; and
- comply with applicable legal obligations.

The publisher may determine the appropriate technical and administrative response based upon the nature of the incident.

#### 22.4 Reporting Security Incidents

Where an organization becomes aware of a security incident that may materially affect the institutional license or the Engineering Handbook Series, the organization should notify the publisher within a reasonable period.

Reports should include, where reasonably available:

- a general description of the incident;
- the approximate date of discovery;
- the systems or services affected;
- actions already taken; and
- an appropriate organizational contact.

The publisher may request additional information reasonably necessary to understand the incident.

#### 22.5 Incident Investigation

Each party may conduct reasonable investigations relating to security incidents affecting its own systems or responsibilities.

Where appropriate, the parties should cooperate in good faith to:

- determine the nature of the incident;
- identify affected licensing services;
- restore secure operations;
- prevent recurrence; and
- protect the publisher's intellectual property rights.

Nothing in this Section requires disclosure of legally privileged information or confidential information protected by applicable law.

#### 22.6 Mitigation Measures

Following identification of a security incident, reasonable mitigation measures may include:

- resetting authentication credentials;
- disabling compromised accounts;
- strengthening authentication procedures;
- implementing additional security controls;
- correcting technical vulnerabilities;
- restoring authorized access; and
- other reasonable remedial actions.

The specific mitigation measures adopted shall depend upon the nature and severity of the incident.

#### 22.7 Preservation of Evidence

Where reasonably practicable, organizations and the publisher should preserve records relating to significant security incidents that may be relevant for:

- technical investigation;
- compliance review;
- contractual administration;
- legal proceedings;
- insurance matters; or
- regulatory requirements.

Evidence preservation shall be conducted in accordance with applicable law and legitimate operational requirements.

#### 22.8 Communication During Incidents

The publisher may communicate with institutional license holders regarding significant incidents affecting institutional licensing.

Such communications may include:

- security advisories;
- temporary operational instructions;
- authentication updates;
- restoration notices;
- recommended corrective measures; or
- other information reasonably necessary to support secure administration.

Organizations should ensure that designated administrative contacts remain capable of receiving such communications.

#### 22.9 Compliance with Applicable Law

Nothing in this Section limits any obligations imposed by applicable law relating to:

- cybersecurity;
- data protection;
- breach notification;
- regulatory reporting;
- governmental investigations; or
- lawful disclosure requirements.

Where applicable law imposes additional obligations, those obligations shall prevail to the extent of any inconsistency.

#### 22.10 Incident Response Framework

Effective incident response supports the continued security, reliability, and integrity of the institutional licensing program.

Both the publisher and institutional license holders should administer security incidents in a timely, proportionate, and commercially reasonable manner while protecting authorized users, preserving intellectual property rights, maintaining operational continuity where reasonably practicable, and complying with applicable legal and contractual obligations.

### 23. Relationship with Other License Types

Institutional licenses form one component of the publisher's overall licensing framework. Different categories of licenses are designed to address different user groups, operational requirements, and methods of access. Unless expressly stated otherwise, each license category operates independently and grants only the rights specifically provided under its applicable license agreement.
