Nothing in this Section shall be interpreted as expanding, replacing, or modifying the rights granted under any other license type unless expressly agreed by the publisher in writing.

#### 23.1 Independent License Categories

The publisher may offer multiple categories of licenses, including:

- individual licenses;
- student licenses;
- educational licenses;
- institutional licenses;
- enterprise licenses;
- government licenses;
- library licenses;
- research licenses; and
- other specialized licensing programs established by the publisher.

Each license category is governed by its own applicable terms and conditions.

#### 23.2 No Automatic Conversion

Obtaining one category of license does not automatically create eligibility for, convert into, or replace another category of license.

For example:

- an individual license does not become an institutional license;
- an institutional license does not create individual ownership rights;
- an enterprise license does not automatically include unrelated organizations; and
- a library license does not authorize unrestricted institutional deployment.

Separate licensing arrangements may be required where multiple license categories are needed.

#### 23.3 Individual Licenses

Where an individual also accesses the Engineering Handbook Series through an institutional license, any independently acquired individual license shall remain separate unless expressly consolidated by the publisher.

The rights granted under an individual license remain governed by the applicable individual licensing agreement.

#### 23.4 Multiple Concurrent Licenses

An organization or individual may hold more than one valid license simultaneously where permitted by the publisher.

Each license shall be administered independently unless the publisher expressly provides otherwise.

Compliance with one license shall not excuse non-compliance with another separate licensing agreement.

#### 23.5 Conflicting License Provisions

Where multiple licenses apply to the same organization or individual, each license governs only the rights granted under that particular agreement.

If an apparent conflict arises between separate licensing agreements, the publisher may determine the appropriate interpretation consistent with:

- the applicable agreements;
- this Manual;
- the intended scope of each license; and
- applicable law.

#### 23.6 Organizational and Individual Rights

Institutional licensing rights belong to the institutional license holder and exist solely for the benefit of authorized users acting within the scope of the institutional license.

Authorized users do not acquire permanent personal licensing rights merely because they accessed the Engineering Handbook Series through an institutional license.

Independent licensing rights arise only through a separate valid license granted directly by the publisher.

#### 23.7 Transition Between License Types

Where an organization or individual requires a different licensing arrangement due to changing operational requirements, the publisher may approve:

- license upgrades;
- license conversions;
- replacement licenses;
- additional licenses; or
- other licensing arrangements,

subject to the publisher's applicable licensing policies.

Any transition becomes effective only upon the publisher's approval and completion of the applicable licensing process.

#### 23.8 Specialized Licensing Programs

The publisher may establish specialized licensing programs for particular sectors, industries, educational initiatives, governmental projects, or other operational purposes.

Specialized licensing programs shall supplement, rather than replace, this Manual unless the publisher expressly provides otherwise.

#### 23.9 Interpretation of Multiple Licenses

Where an organization or individual benefits from more than one applicable license, each license shall be interpreted independently according to its own terms.

No broader licensing rights shall be implied merely because multiple licenses exist simultaneously.

All rights remain limited to those expressly granted under the applicable licensing agreements.

#### 23.10 Reservation of Licensing Authority

The publisher retains exclusive authority to determine:

- available license categories;
- eligibility requirements;
- licensing criteria;
- transitions between license types;
- licensing policies;
- administrative procedures; and
- other matters relating to the publisher's licensing framework.

Except as expressly provided by the applicable license agreement, no person or organization acquires rights under any license category beyond those specifically granted by the publisher.

### 24. General Institutional Licensing Provisions

This Section establishes the general legal and administrative provisions governing institutional licenses. These provisions apply to all institutional license holders unless expressly modified by the applicable institutional license agreement or required otherwise by applicable law.

These provisions are intended to promote consistent interpretation, administration, and enforcement of institutional licenses throughout the Engineering Handbook licensing framework.

#### 24.1 Entire Institutional License

The applicable institutional license agreement, together with this Manual and any documents expressly incorporated by reference, constitutes the entire agreement governing the institutional license.

Any prior discussions, negotiations, representations, proposals, or understandings relating to the institutional license are superseded by the executed licensing agreement unless expressly preserved in writing.

#### 24.2 Order of Precedence

Unless expressly provided otherwise, the following order of precedence shall apply where inconsistencies arise:

1. the executed institutional license agreement;
2. written amendments signed by the publisher;
3. this Manual;
4. publisher policies expressly incorporated by reference; and
5. other supporting administrative documentation.

Nothing in this Section shall limit the application of mandatory provisions of applicable law.

#### 24.3 Amendments

The publisher may amend this Manual from time to time.

Unless otherwise required by applicable law or the applicable institutional license agreement:

- amendments shall generally apply prospectively;
- amendments shall not retroactively alter vested contractual rights;
- active institutional licenses shall continue under their applicable contractual terms unless the agreement provides otherwise; and
- renewed or newly issued institutional licenses may become subject to updated provisions.

#### 24.4 Waiver

Failure by the publisher to enforce any provision of an institutional license on one occasion shall not constitute:

- a waiver of that provision;
- a waiver of any future breach;
- a permanent modification of the licensing agreement; or
- a relinquishment of any legal or contractual rights.

Any waiver shall be effective only if made expressly in writing by the publisher.

#### 24.5 Severability

If any provision of this Manual or the applicable institutional license agreement is determined to be invalid, unlawful, or unenforceable by a court or other competent authority, the remaining provisions shall continue in full force and effect to the maximum extent permitted by applicable law.

The invalid provision shall, where reasonably possible, be interpreted or modified to achieve its original purpose while remaining legally enforceable.

#### 24.6 Force Majeure

Neither the publisher nor the institutional license holder shall be responsible for delays or failures in performance resulting from events beyond their reasonable control, including:

- natural disasters;
- acts of government;
- armed conflict;
- terrorism;
- labor disputes;
- widespread telecommunications failures;
- major cyber incidents;
- pandemics;
- utility failures; or
- other comparable events.

The affected party shall make commercially reasonable efforts to minimize the impact of such events where practicable.

#### 24.7 No Partnership or Agency

Nothing contained in an institutional license shall be interpreted as creating:

- a partnership;
- a joint venture;
- an agency relationship;
- a franchise;
- an employment relationship; or
- any fiduciary relationship

between the publisher and the institutional license holder.

Each party remains an independent legal entity.

#### 24.8 Assignment by the Publisher

The publisher may assign, transfer, delegate, or otherwise administer its rights and obligations relating to institutional licenses in connection with:

- business restructuring;
- corporate reorganization;
- merger;
- acquisition;
- sale of publishing assets; or
- other legitimate business transactions,

provided that such assignment does not materially diminish the institutional license holder's contractual rights.

#### 24.9 Interpretation

Headings, titles, and numbering contained in this Manual are provided solely for convenience and shall not affect the interpretation of any provision.

Unless the context clearly requires otherwise:

- the singular includes the plural;
- the plural includes the singular;
- references to one gender include all genders;
- references to persons include natural persons and legal entities; and
- the words "including," "includes," and "include" mean "including without limitation."

#### 24.10 Final Institutional Provisions

This Section concludes the institutional licensing framework governing the Engineering Handbook Series.

Institutional licenses shall be administered in accordance with:

- the applicable institutional license agreement;
- this Manual;
- applicable copyright law;
- applicable intellectual property law; and
- other applicable legal requirements.

All rights not expressly granted under an institutional license remain exclusively reserved by the publisher.

### 25. Final Institutional Licensing Provisions

This Part establishes the complete institutional licensing framework governing the Engineering Handbook Series. Institutional licenses are intended to provide organizations with clearly defined, limited rights of access and use while preserving the publisher's exclusive ownership of the publications and all associated intellectual property rights.

This Part shall be interpreted consistently with the remainder of this Manual, the applicable institutional license agreement, and applicable law.

#### 25.1 Comprehensive Interpretation

The provisions contained within this Part shall be interpreted as a unified institutional licensing framework.

Individual Sections shall not be interpreted in isolation where doing so would produce results inconsistent with:

- the applicable institutional license agreement;
- this Manual;
- applicable copyright law;
- applicable intellectual property law; or
- the publisher's legitimate licensing objectives.

#### 25.2 Good Faith Administration

The publisher and institutional license holders should administer institutional licenses honestly, fairly, and in good faith.

Good faith administration includes:

- maintaining accurate licensing information;
- cooperating on administrative matters;
- respecting contractual obligations;
- protecting intellectual property rights;
- resolving reasonable administrative issues constructively; and
- supporting lawful use of the Engineering Handbook Series.

#### 25.3 Continued Protection of Intellectual Property

Nothing contained within this Part shall:

- assign copyright;
- transfer ownership;
- create co-ownership;
- grant publishing rights;
- authorize unrestricted reproduction;
- authorize unrestricted redistribution; or
- diminish the publisher's intellectual property rights.

All intellectual property rights remain exclusively vested in the publisher unless expressly assigned by a separate written agreement.

#### 25.4 Relationship with the Entire Manual

This Part forms an integral component of the Publishing, Copyright & Licensing Manual.

Institutional licensing provisions shall be interpreted together with all other applicable Parts of this Manual, including those governing:

- copyright ownership;
- licensing principles;
- digital rights management;
- enforcement;
- remedies;
- dispute resolution;
- liability; and
- other applicable legal and administrative provisions.

#### 25.5 Compliance with Applicable Law

Nothing contained in this Part authorizes any person or organization to engage in conduct prohibited by applicable law.

Where mandatory provisions of applicable law conflict with this Part, those mandatory legal requirements shall prevail only to the extent of the inconsistency.

All remaining provisions shall continue in full force and effect.

#### 25.6 Future Institutional Licensing Programs

The publisher may establish additional institutional licensing programs, specialized organizational licenses, or administrative procedures to address future operational, educational, technological, or commercial requirements.

Unless expressly stated otherwise, future institutional licensing programs shall supplement, rather than replace, the framework established in this Part.

#### 25.7 No Implied Rights

No provision contained in this Part shall be interpreted as granting any right, license, authorization, immunity, or permission except those expressly granted by:

- the applicable institutional license agreement;
- this Manual; or
- applicable law.

All rights not expressly granted remain reserved by the publisher.

#### 25.8 Continuing Obligations

Where applicable, obligations relating to:

- copyright protection;
- intellectual property;
- confidentiality;
- payment obligations;
- dispute resolution;
- limitation of liability;
- record retention; and
- other provisions intended by their nature to survive,

shall continue after the expiration or termination of the institutional license.

#### 25.9 Official Institutional Licensing Framework

This Part constitutes the publisher's official institutional licensing framework for the Engineering Handbook Series.

It establishes standardized principles governing:

- institutional eligibility;
- organizational licensing;
- authorized access;
- institutional administration;
- compliance;
- operational management;
- protection of intellectual property; and
- the rights and responsibilities of institutional license holders.

#### 25.10 Conclusion of Part VI

This concludes **Part VI — Institutional and Organizational Licensing** of the Publishing, Copyright & Licensing Manual.

Together with the preceding Parts of this Manual, these provisions establish a comprehensive institutional licensing framework intended to support lawful educational, research, governmental, commercial, and organizational use of the Engineering Handbook Series while preserving the publisher's exclusive ownership, copyright, publishing rights, and all other intellectual property rights.

Except for the limited rights expressly granted under the applicable institutional license agreement, all rights remain exclusively reserved by the publisher.

### 26. Summary of Part VIII — Institutional & Organizational Licensing

Part VIII establishes the complete legal framework for licensing organizations instead of individual customers. It explains **who may obtain an institutional license, how organizations administer licensed access, what users are permitted to do, and how organizational licensing is managed throughout its lifecycle.**

Unlike individual licensing, institutional licensing grants **limited organizational usage rights**, never ownership of the Engineering Handbook Series. The Part repeatedly reinforces that organizations receive only the rights expressly granted under the applicable license agreement.

#### Major Topics Covered

### 1. Foundation of Institutional Licensing

Defines:

- purpose
- scope
- relationship with individual licenses
- governing principles

and establishes that institutional licensing exists to provide lawful multi-user access while protecting publisher rights.

---

Defines who may obtain institutional licenses, including:

- universities
- schools
- libraries
- government agencies
- commercial organizations
- research institutions
- professional associations
- non-profits

while allowing publisher approval for other eligible entities.

Introduces scalable licensing models such as:

- Departmental
- Multi-Department
- Campus
- Enterprise
- Government
- Library
- Research
- Consortium
- Custom Institutional

together with rules for selecting and modifying license types.

---

### 4. Authorized Users

Defines:

- who qualifies as an authorized user,
- authentication,
- responsibilities,
- shared-account restrictions,
- user limits,
- adding and removing users.

The chapter clearly separates **institutional membership** from **licensing rights**.

---

### 5. Institutional Administration

Explains how organizations manage licenses through:

- license administrators,
- administrative records,
- organizational changes,
- communications,
- periodic reviews.

This creates the administrative layer necessary for enterprise licensing.

---

### 6. Seat Allocation

Introduces:

- licensed seats,
- allocation,
- reassignment,
- concurrent users,
- capacity upgrades,
- compliance with seat limits.

This defines how multi-user licensing is controlled.

---

Establishes secure access through:

- authorization,
- authentication,
- permissions,
- credential security,
- access reviews,
- suspension,
- revocation,
- remote access controls.

Separates lawful organizational use from prohibited activities.

Permitted use includes:

- education
- research
- internal professional reference

while prohibiting:

- redistribution
- commercial exploitation
- scraping
- credential sharing
- removal of copyright notices
- public distribution
- license circumvention

Covers:

- remote access
- institutional networks

- library systems

- technical safeguards

showing how digital delivery fits within licensing restrictions.

Defines:

- fees
- billing
- payments
- renewals
- expiration
- suspension
- termination

ensuring institutional licenses operate under a complete contractual lifecycle.

## PART IX — License Administration, Compliance & Operational Records

---

### 1. Purpose and Scope

Effective license administration is essential to ensuring that every license issued by the publisher remains accurate, verifiable, enforceable, and consistent throughout its lifecycle. While previous Parts establish the legal framework governing copyright ownership, licensing rights, institutional licensing, and permitted use, this Part establishes the administrative framework through which those rights are implemented, managed, and maintained.

The purpose of this Part is to define the operational policies governing the creation, administration, modification, renewal, suspension, expiration, and retirement of licenses issued for the Engineering Handbook Series. It also establishes the records, administrative procedures, compliance mechanisms, and governance principles necessary to support consistent license management across all licensing programs.

This Part applies to all licenses issued by the publisher unless a particular licensing program expressly provides otherwise. It governs the administration of individual licenses, institutional licenses, organizational licenses, enterprise licenses, educational licenses, promotional licenses, and any other licensing arrangements authorized by the publisher.

Nothing contained in this Part creates additional licensing rights beyond those expressly granted under the applicable license agreement. Administrative actions exist solely to implement, document, and enforce the rights established elsewhere in this Manual.

The objectives of this Part include:

- establishing authoritative licensing records;
- ensuring consistent administration throughout the license lifecycle;
- maintaining accurate customer and organizational information;
- supporting fair and transparent licensing operations;
- facilitating renewals, upgrades, and other administrative changes;
- preserving reliable audit trails for licensing decisions;
- promoting compliance with applicable license agreements; and
- supporting secure, scalable, and efficient license administration.

License administration shall be conducted according to the following principles:

- **Accuracy** — licensing records shall accurately reflect the legal and administrative status of each license.
- **Consistency** — comparable administrative situations shall be handled using consistent procedures.
- **Accountability** — significant administrative actions should be capable of independent verification through appropriate records.
- **Integrity** — licensing records shall be protected against unauthorized alteration or destruction.
- **Least Privilege** — administrative authority shall be limited to personnel whose responsibilities require such access.
- **Transparency** — administrative decisions should be supported by documented records where appropriate.
- **Scalability** — administrative procedures should support future growth without requiring fundamental restructuring of the licensing framework.

This Part should be interpreted together with all preceding Parts of this Manual, particularly those governing copyright ownership, licensing models, institutional licensing, compliance, enforcement, remedies, and publisher rights. Where a conflict exists between an administrative procedure and the applicable license agreement, the license agreement shall prevail to the extent of the inconsistency unless prohibited by applicable law.

The provisions contained in this Part establish the operational foundation upon which the publisher administers licensing activities throughout the Engineering Handbook publishing ecosystem.

---

---
### 2. Core Licensing Records

Effective license administration requires the maintenance of accurate, consistent, and authoritative records. Licensing records form the official administrative foundation for managing licenses throughout their lifecycle and provide the basis for operational decisions, compliance activities, customer support, and enforcement.

Licensing records document and administer licensing relationships but do not themselves create, transfer, modify, or terminate licensing rights. All licensing rights arise solely from the applicable license agreement and the provisions of this Manual.

The publisher shall maintain such records as are reasonably necessary to administer licenses throughout their lifecycle. Each record shall possess a unique identifier, remain internally consistent, and accurately reflect its current administrative status.

Where appropriate, individual records may reference one another to support efficient license administration while preserving their independent purpose and integrity.

#### 2.1 Customer Records

A Customer Record identifies the individual or legal entity that has entered into a licensing relationship with the publisher.

Customer Records should contain the information reasonably necessary to administer customer accounts, communicate regarding licensing matters, and associate customers with their respective licenses.

#### 2.2 Organization Records

An Organization Record identifies an institutional or organizational license holder.

Organization Records should maintain information necessary for administering institutional licensing, including organizational identity, designated administrators, billing information, and associated institutional licenses.

#### 2.3 License Records

A License Record is the authoritative administrative record for an individual license issued by the publisher.

Each License Record should identify the applicable license, license holder, licensing model, effective status, duration, and associated entitlements.

Administrative changes affecting a license shall be reflected through updates to the corresponding License Record while preserving an appropriate administrative history.

#### 2.4 Entitlement Records

An Entitlement Record identifies the specific publications, products, services, editions, or access rights granted under a particular license.

Entitlement Records establish the relationship between a License Record and the resources that the license holder is authorized to access or use.

#### 2.5 Administrative Action Records

Administrative Action Records document significant licensing operations, including license issuance, renewal, modification, suspension, revocation, expiration, and other approved administrative actions.

These records support accountability, operational traceability, and historical reference.

#### 2.6 Compliance Records

Compliance Records document licensing reviews, investigations, audit activities, policy exceptions, enforcement actions, and other matters relating to licensing compliance.

Such records support consistent administration, internal governance, and compliance verification throughout the licensing lifecycle.

--- 

---
### 3. License Lifecycle

Every license issued by the publisher shall be administered through a defined lifecycle that records its status from issuance until its expiration, revocation, or retirement. Lifecycle management promotes consistent administration, accurate recordkeeping, and reliable enforcement of licensing rights.

Administrative lifecycle events shall be reflected within the corresponding License Record and, where applicable, associated Entitlement Records. Significant lifecycle changes should preserve an appropriate administrative history.

#### 3.1 License Issuance

A license shall become effective only after completion of the applicable licensing requirements established by the publisher, including acceptance of the applicable license agreement and satisfaction of any required administrative or financial obligations.

Upon issuance, the publisher shall create the corresponding administrative records necessary to identify the license, license holder, and granted entitlements.

#### 3.2 License Activation

Where activation is required, licensed rights shall become exercisable only after the license has been activated in accordance with the applicable licensing procedures.

Activation shall not expand the rights granted under the applicable license agreement.

#### 3.3 License Renewal

Renewable licenses may be renewed before or upon expiration in accordance with the applicable license agreement and the publisher's renewal policies.

Renewal may include updates to licensing terms, duration, pricing, entitlements, or administrative information where applicable.

#### 3.4 License Modification

A license may be modified where approved by the publisher to reflect administrative changes, including updates to customer information, organizational information, licensing scope, or other approved amendments.

Unless expressly stated otherwise, modifications shall not create a new license and shall not affect rights unrelated to the approved change.

#### 3.5 License Upgrade

A license may be upgraded to provide additional rights, products, users, or capabilities where permitted by the publisher.

An upgrade supplements the existing licensing relationship and shall take effect only after completion of the applicable administrative procedures.

#### 3.6 License Conversion

Where permitted by the publisher, one licensing model may be converted into another through an approved administrative process.

A conversion shall not occur automatically and shall remain subject to the applicable eligibility requirements and licensing policies.

#### 3.7 License Suspension

The publisher may suspend a license in accordance with the applicable license agreement, this Manual, or applicable law.

During suspension, some or all licensed rights may be temporarily unavailable until the circumstances giving rise to the suspension have been resolved.

#### 3.8 License Expiration

A license shall expire upon completion of its applicable licensing term unless renewed or otherwise extended by the publisher.

Upon expiration, all licensed rights terminate except those that expressly survive under the applicable agreement or governing law.

#### 3.9 License Revocation

The publisher may revoke a license where revocation is authorized under the applicable license agreement, this Manual, or applicable law.

Revocation permanently terminates the affected license unless the publisher expressly issues a replacement or new license.

#### 3.10 License Retirement

A retired license represents a historical administrative record that is no longer active but is retained for recordkeeping, auditing, legal compliance, or operational purposes.

Retirement of a license record shall not affect any obligations that survive the termination of the licensing relationship.

---

---
### 4. Entitlement Management

Entitlement management governs the administrative allocation of licensed publications, services, and access rights to license holders. Entitlements define what a license authorizes rather than the license itself and shall always remain subject to the applicable license agreement.

Administrative changes affecting entitlements shall be accurately reflected in the corresponding License Record and Entitlement Records to ensure consistent license administration.

#### 4.1 Product Entitlements

Each license shall identify the publications, editions, services, or digital resources to which the license holder is entitled.

No entitlement shall be presumed unless expressly granted under the applicable license.

#### 4.2 Access Entitlements

Access entitlements determine the level of access granted to a license holder, including digital access, downloadable resources, updates, or other licensed services.

Access shall remain limited to the scope defined by the applicable license.

#### 4.3 User Entitlements

Where a license permits multiple authorized users, the publisher or institutional administrator shall allocate entitlements in accordance with the applicable licensing model and user limits.

User entitlements shall not exceed the capacity authorized by the license.

#### 4.4 Institutional Allocations

Institutional licenses may allocate entitlements across departments, campuses, business units, research groups, or other approved organizational structures.

Such allocations shall remain within the scope of the institutional license and shall not create additional licensing rights.

#### 4.5 Entitlement Changes

Entitlements may be added, removed, upgraded, or modified only through approved administrative procedures.

Any change shall become effective only after the corresponding licensing records have been updated.

#### 4.6 Verification of Entitlements

The publisher may verify entitlement records to ensure that licensed access accurately reflects the applicable license agreement.

Discrepancies identified during verification may be corrected through appropriate administrative action.

#### 4.7 Termination of Entitlements

Upon suspension, expiration, revocation, or termination of a license, all associated entitlements shall terminate unless otherwise provided by the applicable license agreement or governing law.

Historical entitlement records may be retained for administrative, legal, or auditing purposes.

---

---
### 5. Administrative Operations

Administrative operations govern routine changes to licensing information while preserving the continuity and integrity of the licensing relationship. Approved administrative actions shall be accurately reflected in the corresponding licensing records and shall not modify licensing rights unless expressly authorized by the applicable license agreement.

#### 5.1 Customer Information Updates

License holders shall maintain accurate and current contact information. The publisher may update customer records following verification of the requested changes.

#### 5.2 Organization Information Updates

Institutional license holders shall promptly notify the publisher of material changes affecting organizational identity, designated administrators, billing information, or other administrative details necessary for license administration.

#### 5.3 Account Merging

Where multiple customer accounts belonging to the same individual or organization are identified, the publisher may consolidate such accounts following appropriate verification.

Account consolidation shall preserve valid licensing records and historical administrative information.

#### 5.4 Administrative Corrections

The publisher may correct clerical, typographical, formatting, or administrative errors that do not alter the legal rights or obligations established under the applicable license agreement.

Material corrections affecting licensing rights shall require appropriate administrative approval.

#### 5.5 License Reassignment

Where permitted under the applicable licensing model, licenses or administrative ownership may be reassigned through an approved administrative process.

Unless expressly authorized, licenses remain non-transferable.

#### 5.6 Administrative Communications

Official licensing communications may include notices relating to renewals, compliance matters, billing, policy updates, security notifications, and other administrative matters.

License holders remain responsible for maintaining valid contact information capable of receiving such communications.

#### 5.7 Record Integrity

All approved administrative actions shall be recorded in a manner that preserves historical accuracy, accountability, and traceability throughout the licensing lifecycle.

Administrative records shall not be altered in a manner that obscures previously recorded licensing actions without maintaining an appropriate audit history.

---

---
### 6. Financial Administration

Financial administration governs the licensing activities associated with payments, invoices, refunds, credits, and other financial transactions. Financial records support license administration but do not themselves establish licensing rights except as provided by the applicable license agreement.

#### 6.1 Billing Records

The publisher may maintain billing records relating to license purchases, renewals, upgrades, subscriptions, and other financial transactions associated with licensed products or services.

#### 6.2 Payment Processing

Licensing fees shall be processed using payment methods approved by the publisher.

A license shall become effective only after the applicable payment requirements have been satisfied unless otherwise authorized by the publisher.

#### 6.3 Invoices and Receipts

The publisher may issue invoices, receipts, payment confirmations, and other financial documents necessary to administer licensing transactions.

Such documents shall serve as evidence of financial transactions and shall not independently establish licensing rights.

#### 6.4 Refund Administration

Refund requests shall be administered in accordance with the applicable refund policy, license agreement, and governing law.

Approval of a refund may result in modification, suspension, or termination of the associated license where applicable.

#### 6.5 Credits and Adjustments

The publisher may issue account credits, billing adjustments, promotional credits, or pricing corrections where appropriate.

Credits shall be administered in accordance with applicable financial policies and may be subject to expiration or usage limitations.

#### 6.6 Taxes and Regulatory Charges

Applicable taxes, duties, withholding obligations, or other regulatory charges shall be administered in accordance with applicable law.

License holders remain responsible for any obligations assigned to them under the applicable agreement or governing law.

#### 6.7 Financial Records

Financial records shall be retained for accounting, auditing, legal compliance, operational administration, and dispute resolution in accordance with applicable record retention requirements.

---

---
### 7. Compliance Operations

Compliance operations support the consistent administration of licensing obligations and help ensure that licensed rights are exercised in accordance with the applicable license agreement, this Manual, and governing law.

Compliance activities shall be conducted in a fair, reasonable, and proportionate manner while respecting applicable legal and contractual requirements.

#### 7.1 Compliance Monitoring

The publisher may monitor licensing activities to verify compliance with applicable licensing terms, usage limitations, and administrative requirements.

Monitoring activities shall be limited to legitimate licensing, operational, security, and compliance purposes.

#### 7.2 Compliance Reviews

The publisher may conduct administrative reviews where circumstances reasonably indicate potential non-compliance or where verification is required for license administration.

License holders may be requested to provide reasonable information necessary to complete such reviews.

#### 7.3 Audit Activities

Where authorized by the applicable license agreement, the publisher may conduct licensing audits to verify compliance with applicable licensing obligations.

Audits shall be performed in a manner reasonably designed to minimize unnecessary disruption to legitimate business operations.

#### 7.4 Non-Compliance

Where non-compliance is identified, the publisher may take appropriate administrative action consistent with the applicable license agreement, this Manual, and governing law.

Administrative measures may include corrective actions, suspension, revocation, or other remedies available under the applicable agreement.

#### 7.5 Corrective Actions

The publisher may permit reasonable opportunities to correct identified compliance deficiencies before applying more restrictive administrative measures where appropriate.

Corrective actions shall not limit the publisher's ability to exercise any contractual or legal rights where immediate action is justified.

#### 7.6 Compliance Documentation

Records relating to compliance reviews, audits, investigations, corrective actions, and enforcement measures shall be maintained as part of the publisher's licensing administration records.

Such records support accountability, historical reference, and future administrative decision-making.

---

---
### 8. Administrative Security

Administrative security protects licensing records, customer information, and licensing operations against unauthorized access, alteration, disclosure, or destruction. Appropriate administrative, technical, and organizational safeguards shall be implemented to preserve the confidentiality, integrity, and availability of licensing systems.

#### 8.1 Access Control

Access to licensing systems and administrative records shall be restricted to authorized personnel and approved users based upon their assigned responsibilities.

Access privileges shall be reviewed periodically and modified or revoked when no longer required.

#### 8.2 Authentication

The publisher may require appropriate authentication mechanisms to verify the identity of users accessing licensing services or performing administrative operations.

Additional verification measures may be required for sensitive administrative actions.

#### 8.3 Administrative Authorization

Administrative actions affecting licenses, customer records, entitlements, financial records, or compliance records shall be performed only by individuals possessing appropriate authority.

Administrative permissions shall be granted according to the principle of least privilege.

#### 8.4 Audit Logging

The publisher may maintain audit logs recording significant administrative activities affecting licensing records or systems.

Audit logs shall support operational accountability, security investigations, compliance verification, and system integrity.

#### 8.5 Incident Management

The publisher may investigate actual or suspected security incidents affecting licensing systems or administrative records.

Where appropriate, reasonable measures may be implemented to contain, mitigate, recover from, and document such incidents.

#### 8.6 Business Continuity

The publisher may maintain backup, recovery, and continuity procedures designed to preserve licensing operations and administrative records in the event of system failures, security incidents, or other operational disruptions.

#### 8.7 Security Improvements

The publisher may periodically update administrative security measures to address evolving operational requirements, technological developments, regulatory obligations, and emerging security risks.

---

---
### 9. Data Governance

Data governance establishes the principles for managing licensing information throughout its lifecycle. The publisher shall administer licensing data in a manner that promotes accuracy, consistency, integrity, accountability, and lawful processing.

#### 9.1 Data Accuracy

Licensing records shall be maintained with reasonable accuracy and updated whenever approved administrative changes occur.

License holders are responsible for providing accurate information necessary for license administration.

#### 9.2 Data Classification

Licensing information may be classified according to its operational sensitivity, confidentiality, regulatory requirements, and business importance.

Administrative controls may vary according to the applicable data classification.

#### 9.3 Data Retention

Licensing records shall be retained for periods necessary to support license administration, legal compliance, financial reporting, dispute resolution, auditing, and legitimate business operations.

Retention periods may vary according to the type of record and applicable legal requirements.

#### 9.4 Data Archiving

Inactive licensing records may be archived for historical reference, regulatory compliance, operational continuity, or legal purposes.

Archived records shall remain protected by appropriate administrative and security controls.

#### 9.5 Data Disposal

Where licensing records are no longer required, they may be securely deleted, destroyed, anonymized, or otherwise disposed of in accordance with applicable retention policies and legal obligations.

Disposal procedures shall seek to prevent unauthorized recovery or disclosure of protected information.

#### 9.6 Data Quality

The publisher may periodically review licensing records to identify incomplete, duplicate, inconsistent, or outdated information.

Reasonable corrective measures may be implemented to maintain the overall quality and reliability of licensing data.

#### 9.7 Governance Reviews

The publisher may periodically review data governance practices to improve operational efficiency, regulatory compliance, security, and the overall administration of licensing information.

---

---
### 10. Platform Architecture

The publisher may implement one or more software platforms to support licensing administration, entitlement management, customer services, financial operations, compliance activities, and related administrative functions.

The internal architecture of such platforms may evolve over time without affecting the legal rights established under the applicable license agreement.

#### 10.1 Administrative Systems

Licensing operations may be supported by integrated administrative systems responsible for customer management, license administration, entitlement management, financial processing, compliance, and reporting.

Individual systems may operate independently or as components of a unified licensing platform.

#### 10.2 System Integration

The publisher may integrate licensing platforms with payment providers, authentication services, communication systems, accounting platforms, customer support systems, or other authorized third-party services where necessary for efficient license administration.

#### 10.3 Automation

Routine licensing operations may be performed through automated processes where appropriate.

Automated administrative processes shall remain subject to applicable licensing policies and administrative oversight.

#### 10.4 Availability

The publisher shall make reasonable efforts to maintain the availability and reliability of licensing services.

Temporary interruptions may occur due to maintenance, upgrades, security measures, operational requirements, or circumstances beyond the publisher's reasonable control.

#### 10.5 System Maintenance

The publisher may perform scheduled or emergency maintenance to improve security, stability, functionality, or performance.

Maintenance activities may temporarily affect the availability of licensing services.

#### 10.6 Platform Evolution

The publisher reserves the right to modify, replace, modernize, or restructure licensing platforms and supporting technologies as operational requirements evolve.

Such changes shall not reduce licensing rights granted under an applicable license agreement unless otherwise expressly provided.

#### 10.7 Technical Documentation

The publisher may maintain technical documentation describing licensing systems, administrative procedures, integration interfaces, operational workflows, and implementation standards for internal or authorized use.

---
### 11. Operational Scenarios

The following operational scenarios illustrate the application of the administrative principles established in this Part. These scenarios are provided solely to demonstrate common licensing operations and do not modify the rights or obligations established under any applicable license agreement.

#### 11.1 New License Issuance

A prospective customer completes the applicable licensing process, accepts the relevant license agreement, satisfies the required financial obligations, and receives the corresponding License Record and associated Entitlement Records.

#### 11.2 License Renewal

Before expiration, the license holder renews an eligible license. The publisher updates the License Record, extends the applicable licensing period, and preserves the existing administrative history.

#### 11.3 Institutional Expansion

An institutional license holder acquires additional authorized users or licensed resources. The publisher updates the applicable Organization Record, License Record, and Entitlement Records to reflect the approved expansion.

#### 11.4 Administrative Correction

An administrative error affecting customer information or licensing records is identified. Following verification, the publisher corrects the affected records while preserving an appropriate administrative history.

#### 11.5 Compliance Review

The publisher conducts a compliance review after identifying circumstances requiring verification of licensing obligations. Where necessary, appropriate corrective measures are implemented in accordance with the applicable license agreement and this Manual.

#### 11.6 License Termination

A license expires, is revoked, or is otherwise terminated. The publisher updates the corresponding licensing records, terminates applicable entitlements, and retains historical records in accordance with applicable retention policies.

---

### Decision Summary

The publisher shall maintain structured administrative processes for managing licenses throughout their lifecycle. Licensing records, entitlement management, financial administration, compliance operations, security measures, data governance, and supporting platform infrastructure collectively ensure the consistent, secure, and accountable administration of all licensing activities.

Nothing in this Part creates, modifies, or transfers licensing rights independently of the applicable license agreement. All licensing decisions shall remain subject to this Manual, the governing license agreement, and applicable law.

--- 

## PART X — LEGAL TERMS, DISPUTES, LIABILITY & INTERNATIONAL CONSIDERATIONS

This Part establishes the legal and contractual framework governing the publication, licensing, distribution, access, use, enforcement, and international operation of the Handbook Ecosystem.

---

### 1. Purpose and Scope

This Part defines the publisher's legal operating framework and provides the foundation upon which customer-facing legal documents, institutional agreements, and licensing terms may be developed.

It is intended to ensure that the publishing business operates in a legally consistent, commercially practical, and internationally scalable manner while protecting the rights and responsibilities of both the publisher and license holders.

#### 1.1 Scope

Unless expressly stated otherwise, this Part applies to:

- all handbook publications;
- editions and remastered editions;
- companion resources;
- digital platforms and services;
- licensing models;
- institutional agreements;
- commercial relationships; and
- related legal and contractual processes.

The policies contained in this Part govern the publisher's approach to:

- legal document architecture;
- contract formation;
- licensing rights and restrictions;
- ownership and intellectual property;
- institutional licensing;
- dispute resolution;
- liability management;
- technical and legal disclaimers;
- international publishing; and
- legal governance.

#### 1.2 Internal Policy and Customer Contracts

This Manual is an internal publishing and operational standard.

Customer-facing legal documents—including License Terms, Privacy Policies, Institutional Agreements, Order Forms, and other contractual documents—shall implement these policies using legally appropriate language suitable for the applicable jurisdiction.

Internal operational procedures, security controls, investigation methods, administrative workflows, and confidential publishing practices are not required to appear within public legal documents unless their disclosure is necessary.

#### 1.3 Professional Legal Review

This Manual is not a substitute for professional legal advice.

Before commercial launch, institutional licensing, international expansion, or any significant legal revision, the publisher should obtain review from qualified legal professionals to ensure compliance with applicable laws and regulatory requirements.

As laws evolve over time, legal documents should be reviewed periodically to maintain continued compliance.

#### 1.4 Guiding Principle

This Manual defines the publisher's intended operating model.

The legally enforceable rights and obligations of the publisher and license holders arise from the applicable contracts, license agreements, and governing law, rather than from this internal Manual alone.

Accordingly, all customer-facing legal documents should accurately reflect the policies established within this Manual while remaining legally valid in the jurisdictions in which they are used.

---

---
### 2. Legal Document Framework

A clear legal-document framework improves consistency, reduces ambiguity, and separates internal operational policies from customer-facing contractual obligations.

Rather than relying on a single comprehensive legal document, the publisher should maintain a structured set of documents, each serving a specific legal and operational purpose.

#### 2.1 Objectives

The legal-document framework should:

- establish legally enforceable customer rights and obligations;
- define licensing terms for different customer categories;
- separate operational policies from contractual commitments;
- reduce duplication across legal documents;
- simplify future legal updates; and
- support long-term growth of the publishing ecosystem.

#### 2.2 Core Legal Documents

The publisher may maintain documents such as:

- Master License Terms;
- Personal License Schedule;
- Institutional License Schedule;
- Commercial or Enterprise License Schedule;
- Website Terms of Use;
- Privacy Policy;
- Refund and Cancellation Policy;
- Accessibility Statement;
- Copyright and Takedown Policy;
- Contributor Agreements;
- Translator Agreements;
- Institutional Order Forms; and
- other supporting legal documents as required.

Each document should have a clearly defined purpose and should avoid unnecessarily repeating provisions contained elsewhere.

#### 2.3 Master License Terms

The Master License Terms should contain the general contractual provisions applicable across all handbook licenses, including matters such as:

- definitions;
- ownership;
- license grants;
- restrictions;
- account responsibilities;
- suspension and termination;
- liability;
- dispute resolution; and
- general contractual provisions.

License-specific rights should normally be defined within the applicable License Schedule rather than duplicating the entire agreement.

#### 2.4 License Schedules

A License Schedule supplements the Master License Terms by defining the rights and obligations applicable to a particular licensing model.

Examples include:

- Personal License Schedule;
- Institutional License Schedule;
- Commercial Training License Schedule; and
- Enterprise License Schedule.

License Schedules should remain consistent with the Master License Terms unless an authorized agreement expressly provides otherwise.

#### 2.5 Supporting Legal Documents

Certain legal matters are better addressed through independent documents rather than incorporating them into the License Terms.

Examples include:

- Privacy Policy;
- Accessibility Statement;
- Refund Policy;
- Website Terms of Use; and
- Copyright Takedown Procedures.

Maintaining separate documents improves clarity, simplifies updates, and allows each document to address its specific legal purpose.

#### 2.6 Legal Definitions

Legal documents should use consistent terminology throughout the publishing ecosystem.

Important defined terms may include:

- Handbook;
- Volume;
- Edition;
- Remastered Edition;
- License;
- License Holder;
- Authorized User;
- Institution;
- Licensed Material;
- Publication;
- Companion Resource; and
- Third-Party Material.

Definitions should be precise enough to avoid ambiguity while remaining understandable to ordinary readers.

---

---
### 3. Contract Formation

A license agreement should be formed through a clear, transparent, and legally recognizable process that allows the customer to understand and accept the applicable terms before obtaining licensed access.

The publisher should ensure that every licensing transaction creates reliable evidence demonstrating when, how, and under which terms the agreement was formed.

#### 3.1 Formation of the Agreement

A license agreement may be established through one or more legally recognized methods, including:

- online purchase with affirmative acceptance;
- electronic signature;
- signed institutional agreement;
- accepted purchase order or order form;
- authorized license grant under defined terms; or
- another legally valid contractual process.

The method of contract formation should be appropriate for the applicable license category and jurisdiction.

#### 3.2 Online Acceptance

For digital purchases, the publisher should use a clear acceptance process requiring the customer to actively agree to the applicable legal documents before completing the transaction.

The acceptance process should:

- clearly identify the applicable legal documents;
- provide reasonable access to those documents before acceptance;
- require affirmative customer action; and
- record the acceptance as part of the licensing process.

Passive or hidden acceptance mechanisms should be avoided where a more reliable method is reasonably available.

**Example**

A checkout page may require the customer to actively confirm:

> □ I have read and agree to the applicable License Terms and Privacy Policy.

The purchase should not proceed until the required confirmation has been completed.

#### 3.3 Capacity to Contract

The publisher should consider whether the person accepting the agreement has the legal capacity to enter into the contract.

This is particularly important where publications are marketed toward students or younger users.

Depending on applicable law, additional requirements may include:

- age-related eligibility rules;
- parental or guardian consent;
- institutional purchasing arrangements; or
- other legally required safeguards.

The publisher should not assume that one age requirement applies universally across all jurisdictions.

#### 3.4 Evidence of Acceptance

The licensing system should preserve appropriate evidence demonstrating the formation of each agreement.

Where practical, records may include:

- agreement version;
- acceptance timestamp;
- customer or account identifier;
- transaction reference;
- applicable license type; and
- acceptance method.

These records support licensing administration, customer support, compliance activities, and dispute resolution.

#### 3.5 Legal Review

The enforceability of electronic contracts, online acceptance mechanisms, and digital licensing processes may vary between jurisdictions.

Accordingly, the publisher should periodically review contract-formation procedures to ensure they remain consistent with applicable legal requirements and evolving commercial practices.

---

---
### 4. Ownership and License Terms

Ownership of intellectual property and the rights granted to customers are separate legal concepts.

The publisher retains ownership of the handbook and all associated intellectual property unless ownership is expressly transferred through a written agreement. Customers receive only the rights specifically granted under the applicable license.

A license grants permission to use the licensed material under defined conditions. It does not transfer copyright ownership or any intellectual property rights unless expressly stated otherwise.

#### 4.1 Ownership of Intellectual Property

Unless otherwise agreed in writing, the publisher or the applicable rights holder retains ownership of:

- handbook content;
- text and editorial material;
- illustrations and diagrams;
- layouts and publication design;
- digital assets;
- trademarks and branding;
- companion resources; and
- other protected intellectual property.

The purchase of a handbook, whether in digital or printed form, does not transfer ownership of these rights.

#### 4.2 License Grant

Each license should clearly define:

- the license holder;
- the licensed material;
- permitted purposes;
- license category;
- duration;
- transferability;
- exclusivity; and
- any applicable usage limitations.

The scope of the granted rights should be written in clear and understandable language so that customers can reasonably determine what they are permitted to do.

#### 4.3 License Restrictions

Unless expressly authorized by the applicable license or required by law, customers should not:

- redistribute licensed materials;
- resell handbook files;
- publicly upload copyrighted content;
- remove copyright or ownership notices;
- share accounts or credentials beyond the permitted scope;
- bypass technical protection measures; or
- create counterfeit or unauthorized editions.

Restrictions should be reasonable, proportionate, and consistent with applicable law.

#### 4.4 Personal, Educational, and Commercial Use

Different license categories may authorize different forms of use.

A Personal License is intended for an individual's own learning, reference, and skill development.

An Institutional License may authorize teaching, classroom use, and allocated student access within the purchased scope.

A Commercial License may authorize activities such as professional training, corporate instruction, or other commercial educational services where expressly permitted.

The applicable license should clearly identify the permitted scope of use for each category.

#### 4.5 Knowledge and Protected Material

The publisher's rights extend to the protected expression of the handbook, not to the reader's acquired knowledge or skills.

Readers remain free to:

- learn concepts;
- develop technical skills;
- apply engineering principles;
- create their own software;
- explain ideas in their own words; and
- build independent projects using their acquired knowledge.

The license protects the handbook itself and the contractual rights governing its use. It does not grant ownership over a reader's future work, professional experience, or independently created knowledge.

**Example**

A software engineer who studies database indexing from the handbook may apply those concepts while developing software for an employer without obtaining an additional license.

However, copying handbook chapters, diagrams, or substantial protected content into a paid training course or commercial publication would require appropriate authorization from the publisher.

#### 4.6 Example Code

Where the handbook contains example code, the publisher may provide separate permissions governing its use.

The rights applicable to example code should be clearly distinguished from the rights governing the handbook as a whole.

Unless expressly stated otherwise, permission to use example code does not authorize reproduction or redistribution of the accompanying handbook text, illustrations, diagrams, or other protected publication content.

---

---
### 5. Account and Platform Terms

Where the publisher distributes handbooks through an online platform, customer accounts and platform services shall be governed by clear operational rules that define the responsibilities of both the publisher and the license holder.

These policies promote secure access, reliable service, and consistent administration throughout the licensing lifecycle.

#### 5.1 Customer Accounts

Where user accounts are required, customers should:

- provide accurate registration information;
- maintain the confidentiality of account credentials;
- use only accounts that belong to them or that they are authorized to use;
- promptly update important account information when necessary; and
- notify the publisher of any known or suspected unauthorized account access.

Customers remain responsible for activities performed through their accounts unless they promptly report a known security compromise.

#### 5.2 Publisher Responsibilities

The publisher should make reasonable efforts to:

- maintain platform security;
- protect customer account information;
- safeguard licensing records;
- investigate suspected security incidents; and
- restore normal service following technical failures where reasonably practicable.

Nothing in this Manual guarantees uninterrupted availability or absolute security.

#### 5.3 Platform Availability

The publishing platform may occasionally experience:

- scheduled maintenance;
- software updates;
- infrastructure upgrades;
- security-related maintenance;
- third-party service interruptions; or
- unexpected technical failures.

The publisher should make reasonable efforts to minimize disruption while recognizing that continuous availability cannot always be guaranteed.

Where service-level commitments are offered to institutional or enterprise customers, those commitments should be defined within the applicable agreement.

#### 5.4 Publication Updates

Publications may receive updates throughout their lifecycle.

Examples include:

- editorial corrections;
- formatting improvements;
- technical clarifications;
- same-edition revisions;
- remastered editions; or
- entirely new editions.

Customer entitlement to updates shall depend upon the applicable license, purchase terms, and update policy.

The publisher should avoid promising unlimited free access to all future editions unless such a commitment forms part of the published business model.

#### 5.5 Independent Handbook Rule

Each handbook is an independent publication with its own licensing relationship unless expressly provided otherwise.

Ownership or licensing of one handbook does not automatically grant access to other handbooks within the publishing ecosystem.

Bundles, subscriptions, enterprise agreements, or promotional offers may provide broader access only where expressly stated.

#### 5.6 Sequel and Related Publications

Where the publisher designates an official sequel, companion handbook, or related publication, the relationship shall be determined solely by the publisher's publication registry.

Similarity of subject matter alone does not create a sequel relationship or extend licensing rights.

Any entitlement relating to sequels, companion publications, or bundled releases shall be governed by the applicable licensing policy rather than by assumptions based on publication titles or subject matter.

---

---
### 6. Institutional Legal Terms

Institutions often require licensing arrangements that differ from those used for individual customers. This Section establishes the legal principles governing institutional licensing while allowing agreements to be adapted for different organizational requirements.

Institutional agreements should clearly define the rights, responsibilities, and administrative obligations of both the publisher and the licensed institution.

#### 6.1 Eligible Institutions

Institutional licensing may be offered to organizations such as:

- universities;
- colleges;
- schools;
- training centers;
- libraries;
- government organizations;
- research institutions;
- nonprofit organizations; and
- commercial enterprises.

Eligibility requirements may vary depending on the applicable licensing program.

#### 6.2 Authorized Users

Institutional licenses should clearly identify who may access the licensed materials.

Authorized Users may include:

- enrolled students;
- faculty members;
- instructors;
- researchers;
- librarians;
- employees; or
- other persons expressly approved under the applicable agreement.

The institution should take reasonable steps to prevent unauthorized access by individuals who are not covered by the license.

#### 6.3 License Scope

An institutional agreement should clearly define matters including:

- licensed publications;
- number of authorized users;
- permitted methods of access;
- duration of the license;
- geographic scope, where applicable;
- renewal terms; and
- any usage limitations.

The scope of an institutional license should be sufficiently clear to allow both parties to determine the rights granted without unnecessary interpretation.

#### 6.4 Institutional Responsibilities

Institutions should make reasonable efforts to:

- administer licensed access responsibly;
- prevent unauthorized distribution;
- protect institutional credentials;
- comply with applicable license restrictions;
- cooperate with reasonable compliance inquiries; and
- notify the publisher of significant licensing issues affecting authorized access.

Institutions are not expected to guarantee that misuse can never occur, but they should respond appropriately when misuse becomes known.

#### 6.5 Publisher Responsibilities

The publisher should make reasonable efforts to:

- provide the licensed materials described in the agreement;
- maintain accurate licensing records;
- communicate significant policy changes affecting institutional customers;
- provide reasonable administrative support; and
- process renewals, amendments, or authorized modifications where applicable.

Additional obligations, such as service-level commitments or dedicated support, should be expressly defined within the applicable agreement.

#### 6.6 Institutional Customization

Institutional customers may require customized commercial terms.

Examples include:

- campus-wide licensing;
- departmental licensing;
- consortium agreements;
- volume purchasing;
- multi-year agreements;
- enterprise authentication methods; and
- customized invoicing arrangements.

Such customizations should be documented through written agreements without modifying the publisher's core intellectual property rights unless expressly authorized.

#### 6.7 Order of Legal Documents

Where multiple legal documents apply to an institutional relationship, their order of precedence should be clearly defined.

Unless otherwise agreed, the following order may apply:

1. Signed Institutional Agreement;
2. Institution-specific Order Form or Amendment;
3. Applicable License Schedule;
4. Master License Terms; and
5. Other supporting legal documents.

Clearly defining document precedence helps avoid conflicts when different documents address the same subject.

---

---
### 7. Suspension and Termination

The publisher may suspend or terminate licenses, accounts, or platform access when necessary to protect intellectual property, maintain platform integrity, enforce licensing terms, or comply with applicable legal obligations.

Such actions should be reasonable, proportionate, and consistent with the applicable agreement and governing law.

#### 7.1 Grounds for Suspension

Temporary suspension may occur where reasonably necessary, including situations involving:

- suspected unauthorized account access;
- suspected license abuse;
- excessive or abnormal system activity;
- suspected security incidents;
- investigation of potential policy violations;
- failure to comply with applicable license terms; or
- legal or regulatory requirements.

Suspension should normally be limited to the scope and duration reasonably necessary to address the underlying issue.

#### 7.2 Grounds for Termination

A license or account may be terminated where appropriate, including circumstances such as:

- material breach of the license agreement;
- repeated or intentional copyright infringement;
- fraudulent activity;
- unauthorized commercial distribution;
- deliberate circumvention of technical protection measures;
- violation of applicable laws affecting the license; or
- other significant contractual breaches.

Termination should generally be reserved for serious or persistent violations rather than minor administrative errors.

#### 7.3 Investigation Process

Before taking enforcement action, the publisher should, where reasonably practicable:

- review the available evidence;
- evaluate the seriousness of the suspected violation;
- determine whether corrective action is possible;
- document significant findings; and
- apply enforcement measures proportionate to the circumstances.

Immediate action may be appropriate where delay would present a substantial legal, financial, or security risk.

#### 7.4 Notice of Enforcement

Where appropriate, the publisher should provide reasonable notice regarding suspension or termination.

The notice may include:

- the nature of the action;
- the general reason for the decision;
- any available corrective measures;
- appeal procedures, where applicable; and
- the effective date of the action.

The publisher may withhold specific investigative details where disclosure could compromise security, legal obligations, or ongoing investigations.

#### 7.5 Effect of Termination

Unless otherwise provided by the applicable agreement or required by law, termination generally results in:

- expiration of the granted license;
- termination of future access to licensed digital materials;
- cessation of permissions granted under the license;
- continued protection of the publisher's intellectual property rights; and
- survival of contractual provisions intended to remain effective after termination.

Termination does not automatically extinguish obligations that, by their nature, are intended to continue beyond the end of the agreement.

#### 7.6 Reinstatement

Where appropriate, the publisher may consider reinstating a suspended account or license after reviewing the circumstances.

Factors that may be considered include:

- correction of the underlying issue;
- evidence of good-faith cooperation;
- absence of ongoing security concerns;
- compliance with applicable licensing requirements; and
- any other relevant circumstances.

Reinstatement is discretionary unless otherwise required by law or expressly provided in the applicable agreement.

---

---
### 8. Dispute Resolution

Disputes may occasionally arise between the publisher and license holders regarding licensing, payments, access, intellectual property, or contractual obligations. A structured dispute-resolution process promotes fairness, reduces unnecessary litigation, and encourages timely resolution.

The publisher should seek to resolve disputes professionally, efficiently, and in good faith before pursuing formal legal remedies whenever reasonably practicable.

#### 8.1 Good-Faith Resolution

Before initiating formal legal proceedings, the parties should make reasonable efforts to resolve disputes through direct communication.

This may include:

- identifying the disputed issue;
- exchanging relevant information;
- clarifying misunderstandings;
- discussing possible solutions; and
- documenting any agreed resolution.

Good-faith discussions often resolve administrative or contractual issues without requiring external proceedings.

#### 8.2 Internal Review

Where appropriate, disputes should first undergo an internal review process.

The review may consider:

- applicable license terms;
- transaction records;
- licensing history;
- customer communications;
- technical evidence; and
- other relevant documentation.

Internal review should be impartial and based upon the available evidence rather than assumptions.

#### 8.3 Alternative Dispute Resolution

Where permitted by applicable law and agreed by the parties, disputes may be resolved through alternative dispute resolution mechanisms, including:

- negotiation;
- mediation;
- arbitration; or
- other mutually agreed procedures.

Alternative dispute resolution may reduce costs, preserve business relationships, and provide a more efficient resolution than litigation.

Participation in such procedures should comply with applicable law and any contractual requirements.

#### 8.4 Court Proceedings

If a dispute cannot be resolved through reasonable efforts, either party may pursue available legal remedies before a court or other competent authority as permitted by the applicable agreement and governing law.

Nothing in this Manual limits any non-waivable legal rights or remedies provided under applicable law.

#### 8.5 Evidence and Records

In the event of a dispute, relevant records may include:

- license agreements;
- purchase records;
- invoices;
- payment confirmations;
- acceptance records;
- account activity;
- communications between the parties; and
- other relevant documentation.

Maintaining accurate records assists in establishing the factual circumstances surrounding the dispute.

#### 8.6 Limitation Periods

Claims should be brought within any limitation periods established by applicable law.

Nothing in this Manual extends, shortens, or overrides statutory limitation periods unless such modification is legally permitted and expressly agreed within the applicable contract.

#### 8.7 Continuing Obligations

Unless immediate termination is required, the existence of a dispute does not automatically suspend all contractual obligations.

The parties should continue to comply with obligations that remain reasonably capable of performance while the dispute is being resolved, unless otherwise agreed or required by law.

---

---
### 9. Governing Law and Jurisdiction

Publishing activities frequently involve customers, institutions, and partners located in different jurisdictions. Accordingly, legal documents should clearly identify the governing law and the forum responsible for resolving legal disputes where such provisions are legally enforceable.

The governing law and jurisdiction clauses provide legal certainty by establishing the legal framework applicable to the contractual relationship.

#### 9.1 Governing Law

Customer-facing agreements should specify the law governing the interpretation, validity, performance, and enforcement of the agreement.

The chosen governing law should generally reflect:

- the publisher's principal place of business;
- applicable commercial considerations;
- regulatory requirements; and
- the intended scope of the publishing operations.

The governing law clause should not attempt to exclude mandatory legal protections that cannot legally be waived.

#### 9.2 Jurisdiction

Legal documents should identify the court or other competent authority responsible for resolving disputes where litigation becomes necessary.

Jurisdiction provisions may specify:

- exclusive jurisdiction;
- non-exclusive jurisdiction; or
- another legally recognized forum agreed by the parties.

The selected jurisdiction should be commercially practical and legally appropriate for the publisher's operations.

#### 9.3 International Customers

Customers located outside the publisher's home jurisdiction remain subject to the applicable license agreement.

However, certain consumer protection laws, mandatory contractual rights, tax regulations, privacy requirements, or other statutory protections may apply based on the customer's location.

Accordingly, international operations should consider applicable local legal requirements before offering products or services within a particular jurisdiction.

#### 9.4 Conflict of Laws

Where multiple jurisdictions could potentially apply, the governing law clause should clearly establish which legal system governs the agreement to the extent permitted by applicable law.

This reduces uncertainty and assists in the consistent interpretation of contractual provisions.

#### 9.5 Severability of Jurisdiction Clauses

If a governing law or jurisdiction provision is determined to be invalid or unenforceable under applicable law, the remaining provisions of the agreement should continue to operate to the fullest extent legally permissible unless the agreement cannot reasonably function without the affected provision.

#### 9.6 Legal Compliance

The publisher should conduct its publishing activities in accordance with applicable laws governing matters such as:

- contracts;
- intellectual property;
- consumer protection;
- electronic commerce;
- taxation;
- privacy and data protection;
- accessibility; and
- other applicable legal requirements.

Legal compliance is an ongoing responsibility and should be reviewed periodically as laws and regulatory requirements evolve.

---

---
### 10. Financial and Regulatory Considerations

Commercial publishing involves financial, accounting, taxation, and regulatory obligations that extend beyond the licensing relationship itself. The publisher should conduct business operations in a manner that supports legal compliance, financial transparency, and responsible commercial practices.

This Section establishes general principles rather than jurisdiction-specific legal or tax advice.

#### 10.1 Pricing

The publisher may determine pricing based on factors such as:

- publication type;
- edition;
- license category;
- regional markets;
- institutional arrangements;
- promotional campaigns; and
- commercial strategy.

Prices may change over time unless protected by an existing contractual commitment.

#### 10.2 Taxes

Customers may be responsible for applicable taxes, duties, or governmental charges associated with their purchases where required by law.

Depending on the jurisdiction, these may include:

- sales tax;
- value-added tax (VAT);
- goods and services tax (GST);
- withholding tax; or
- other legally required charges.

The publisher should comply with applicable tax laws governing its commercial operations.

#### 10.3 Invoicing and Payment Records

The publisher should maintain appropriate financial records relating to commercial transactions.

Records may include:

- invoices;
- receipts;
- payment confirmations;
- refunds;
- credit notes;
- transaction references; and
- accounting records required by applicable law.

Financial records should be retained for the period required by applicable legal and regulatory obligations.

#### 10.4 Refunds and Cancellations
